oh, but she burns

by thiswildernessismyhome

Summary

Agatha inspects Rio with predatory eyes, eyes that are shrewd, starving. She's a murderer, Rio thinks - but she doesn't fight. She stays perfectly still as Agatha leans in. Stays still as she runs her lips up the curve of Rio's neck, feather-light and agonizing.

"Don't you want me to have fun with you?" Agatha murmurs, breath warm in her ear.

FBI Agent Rio Vidal is obsessed with hunting down serial killer Agatha Harkness. Unfortunately for her, the feeling is mutual:

Agatha's a lit match, and Rio's got a whole life ready to burn.

Chapter 1

Rio gazes down at the dead body and tries to stifle a yawn.

It’s not that this case is boring, although it is: dead guy, heart attack, what the fuck is she even doing here. But it’s not only that. There’s also the fact that she’s been up since 4am, the coffee on the plane tasted like dishwater, and once she wraps things up here all she has to look forward to is a shitty hotel room and a mountain of paperwork. And the dingy little town of Westview isn’t doing much to recommend itself, either. She’s used to being treated with suspicion by local PDs – no one’s happy when the FBI shows up, it is what it is – but the level of hostility toward the Bureau tends to be inversely correlated with the size of a town’s population. And the population of this place is approximately fuck-all and counting. She drove past seven boarded-up storefronts just to get here, and the most exciting business she spotted on Main Street was a combination hair salon and taxidermy shop.

Which makes this whole thing that much weirder. 

She glances around at the gaudy home she’s standing in, a mansion so out of place in this town that it may as well have been dropped here by aliens. Marble floors, oil paintings in gilded frames, crystal chandeliers hanging like frozen fireworks. Every inch of it meticulously decorated, and plainly intended to evoke a sort of unattainable, Gilded Age wealth – Rockefellers, Carnegies, Vanderbilts. The kind of luxury that comes with Roman numerals after your name.

The dead body does put something of a damper on the whole aesthetic, though.

“Westview have a lot of millionaires?” Rio asks the beat cop who’s babysitting her. He’s clean-shaven, military haircut, and looks to be about twelve years old. Shiny buttons on his uniform, scuffed shoes on his feet, probably calls his mother twice a week. Not even close to making detective; sending him was plainly meant as an insult, but it’s one she’s decided to ignore.

“No.”

Rio waits to see if he’s got anything else to say. She’s not surprised when he doesn’t.

“No,” she agrees. “You’re too far south to be a commuter town, so you’re not getting Wall Street money. And Westview isn’t exactly Silicon Valley. So what’s Ansel Porter doing here?”

He glances over at her, then away again. “Couldn’t say, ma’am.”

Ma’am. Ouch. 

She crouches down next to the crime scene photographer and tilts her head back and forth, examining the body without touching it. Ansel Porter, sixty-three, sprawled face-first on gold-veined marble. Death is rarely dignified, but the contrast between the body and the ornate setting makes both of them seem more grotesque, somehow. Or more amusing. Rio’s not sure which.

She stands back up and fixes her gaze on the twelve-year-old officer. “The correct answer is: his wife grew up here. Her parents are getting older, she wanted to move back home, he agreed. Reluctantly, I assume. But he still has an apartment in the city where he spends most of his time. That sound about right?”

The kid’s Adam’s apple bobs up and down. “I wouldn’t know, ma’am.”

“Yeah,” she sighs. “Alright. Well, I think I got everything I need here. Tell your boss I’m planning to get a statement from the wife, and I’ll need to speak to someone from Porter’s office.” She gives him a wan smile. “Once the ME gives the all-clear, I’ll be out of your hair.” 

“Actually, ma'am, Westview PD would be happy to conduct those interviews. Save you the trouble.”

She shoots him an amused glance. “Thanks, but the FBI does its own interviews.”

“Yes, ma’am.”

She follows the kid outside and watches him drive off in his patrol car before climbing into her rental. The temperature's dropped since she arrived, and the wind carries the smell of wood smoke and something vaguely chemical – probably from whatever factory's been slowly poisoning this place for the last fifty years. As she collapses into the driver’s seat she has to fight a sudden visceral urge to lay her head on the steering wheel and nap for an hour or three. She compromises with herself by leaning her head back, closing her eyes, and taking deep breaths as she counts to ten.

One. Two. Three. F—

“Hey!” a voice yells, banging on the window, and Rio’s eyes fly open. “Everything okay in there?” 

"Jesus,” Rio snaps, rolling down the window, heart hammering. "You scared the shit out of me."

“Sorry,” the woman standing above her drawls, though her grin makes it clear she’s not actually sorry. She’s got a plain face, no makeup, unbrushed hair pulled back into a low ponytail like an afterthought. The lapels of her canvas jacket – which Rio has to believe was chosen for practicality, because it certainly wasn’t chosen for style – frame a detective’s badge hanging around her neck. “They called me out for a dead body. Didn’t want to take any chances.” She snaps her gum between her teeth and looks delighted at her own joke.

“Right. And you are?”

“Detective Agnes O’Connor, WPD. I take it you’re our friendly Fed?”

“I’m friendlier when people aren’t banging on my car windows.” This elicits another chuckle from Agnes. “You’re a little late, detective. Officer Sanders already took me through the scene.”

Agnes’ lip curls. “Ugh. Chief sent that idiot?”

“Yeah,” Rio says, and then realizes it sounds like she’s agreeing that he’s an idiot. Which he is, but still. “He was… fine.”

Agnes gives her a skeptical look. “Aren’t you diplomatic. You got a name, Agent?”

“Vidal. Rio Vidal.”

Agnes rests her forearm on the top of the car door and looks around, chewing her gum loudly. “So what’s next on the agenda, Agent Vidal? Headed to Porter’s office?”

“I thought I’d talk to the wife first, actually.” 

“Yeah, well, good luck with that. She’s refusing to speak without her lawyer present. You know how these one-percenters are, can’t wipe their asses without running it past legal first. He’ll be here tomorrow.”

Rio sighs. “Got it. Well, then, yeah. I’ll want to speak with someone from his office.”

“Great,” Agnes says, giving her a self-satisfied smile. “Your car or mine?”

 

x

 

Agnes doesn’t say much on the ride over; it’s mostly just gum chewing and some idle humming. After the third or fourth snap of a bubble popping, Rio grips the steering wheel and glances over at her.

“So what’s Ansel Porter doing in Westview, anyway?” she asks. “Doesn’t seem like you get a lot of millionaires around here.”

“What, I don’t look like old money?” Agnes chuckles as she leans back in the passenger seat, stretching like a cat. “Nah, his wife grew up around here. They built that monstrosity of a house so she could be closer to her parents. Far as I know he still spent most of his time in New York.”

“Ah.”

“Doesn’t the FBI have some kind of file on him?”

“Yeah.”

“So you just asking to see if I’d bullshit you?”

“Yeah, pretty much.”

Agnes snorts. “Nice. How’d Patrol Officer Babyface answer?”

“Couldn’t say, ma’am,” Rio says in a deep voice, and Agnes laughs. 

“Idiot.”

Porter’s local satellite office turns out to be the first floor of an old, rambling Victorian-style house. Time hasn’t been good to the place; the paint is dull and peeling, revealing weathered wood beneath. The wraparound porch creaks under Rio’s feet, vines and grasses poking through the slats. 

“This seems a little rundown for Porter’s tastes,” she says, glancing around.

“Yeah,” Agnes says, peering in the front window. “Talk was, he only opened this office for the tax break. I’m betting he never even saw the place.” She turns to look at Rio over her shoulder. “How about I take the lead on this one?”

“Be my guest.”

The office is nicer inside than out – handsome wooden desks, shiny computers – but, like the home itself, it’s not nearly as elaborate as Rio would have expected from a multi-million dollar enterprise. It’s also entirely empty other than a bored-looking blonde woman sitting at the front desk, tapping away at the keyboard in front of her.

“Morning,” she says, glancing up at them. “How can I help you?”

“This Ansel Porter’s office?” Agnes asks gruffly.

The woman’s eyes travel between the badges hanging around both women’s necks. “May I ask what this is about?”

“Yeah, you can ask,” Agnes says. “I’m Detective O’Connor, Westview Police. This is Agent Vidal with the FBI. We’ve got some questions about Ansel Porter.”

“Ah. Well, that sounds like something that should go through legal. If you’d like to leave your information, I can have them reach out to you.”

Agnes stares at her, sucking her teeth. “Uh-huh. And you are?”

“Dottie Proctor. I’m Mr. Porter’s executive assistant.”

“And when was the last time you saw Mr. Porter?”

Dottie’s brow furrows. “Yesterday. Look, he’s not here right now—“

“Yeah, it’d be pretty weird if he was, considering we just came back from examining his dead body.”

Jesus, Agnes.

“He’s… Mr. Porter’s dead?” Dottie asks, blinking. “What happened?”

“That’s what we’re trying to find out,” Agnes says, resting her hand on her holster. 

“Was he – wait, was he murdered or something?”

Agnes’s eyes narrow. “What makes you think that?”

“I don’t know. You’re here.”

“Hm,” Agnes says, plainly unconvinced. “Okay. And where were you last night between the hours of one and three AM, Dottie Proctor?”

Dottie looks alarmed, and Rio has to stop herself from rolling her eyes. “I was at home,” Dottie tells her. “In bed.”

“At home in bed. Right. And can anyone corroborate that?”

Rio takes a step forward, resting a placating hand on Agnes’s arm. “There’s no indication of foul play, Ms. Proctor. We’re just doing our due diligence.”

Dottie glances back over at Agnes like she’s not sure whether she should answer the question, but of course Agnes still has her eyebrows raised expectantly. “I was with my husband?”

“Is that a question?” Agnes asks sarcastically.

“Like I said,” Rio interjects again. She takes another step forward, positioning herself between Dottie and Agnes. “We’re just here to rule out anything suspicious. Have you noticed anything out of the ordinary over the past few days? Anything unusual?”

It takes Dottie a moment to pull her eyes away from Agnes and meet Rio’s gaze. “Uh,” she says. “Well – it’s not unusual, but there are the letters.”

“What letters?” Agnes demands.

Dottie reaches into a desk drawer and pulls out a packet of papers. “Mr. Porter gets a lot of hate mail.” She waits for Rio to pull on a pair of latex gloves, then hands over the letters. “The AI program he developed – I guess people felt like it wasn’t fair, the way it was denying their insurance claims? Some of them were pretty upset.”

“Imagine that,” Agnes mutters.

“There are a bunch of emails, too.”

“Okay,” Rio says. “We’re going to need copies of those. Is there anything else? Any other reason you can think of that someone might have wanted to harm Mr. Porter?”

The woman opens her mouth, then closes it again. She shakes her head. “No.”

“Hang on,” Agnes says, eyes narrowing. “What were you about to say just then?”

“Nothing,” Dottie says. “I wasn’t—”

“Say it,” Agnes demands.

Rio sighs internally. “No detail is too small,” she says, smiling kindly. “You never know what might be important.”

“Well…” Dottie trails off, then leans in, dropping her voice conspiratorially. “I have access to his work email, obviously, and – look, it’s not my place to judge, but if I were his wife, and I saw some of the emails he was sending to women…” Dottie grimaces.

“He was having an affair,” Rio says. 

Agnes rolls her eyes. “Of course he was. What a jagweed.”

Rio has to curl her mouth into a strange shape to keep from laughing. “Thanks, that’s very helpful, Dottie. We’ll need copies of those emails, too.”

As they walk out a half hour later, two large file folders filled with printouts in hand, Rio shoots Agnes a look. 

“You want to maybe lay off the ‘good cop, bad cop’ thing next time we’re talking to someone who isn’t even a suspect?”

“What? That was barely bad cop.”

“You freaked her out.”

“We got what we needed, didn’t we?” Rio opens her mouth to reply, but Agnes holds up her hands. “Yeah, yeah, okay. I’ll be on my best behavior next time.”

“Thank you.”

“Shame, though.” Agnes flashes her a lazy grin as they climb back into the car. “You play good to my bad so well.”

 

x

 

The restaurant is as run down as Porter’s office – cracked pleather booths, spots worn into the formica tables, the smell of old grease hanging in the air. But Agnes had insisted it was the best pizza in town, and Rio’s pleasantly surprised to find it’s actually pretty good.

“It’s cheese on bread,” Agnes says dryly when Rio tells her so. “Even Westview can handle that.”

They take over a corner booth with a large pizza and a pitcher of beer, and start reviewing the letters. They leave the ten or so that were physically mailed in an evidence bag to preserve any evidence that might be on them. But there are nearly a hundred emails – everything from disgruntled mothers signing their real names to death threats from obviously spoofed accounts. 

“Let’s start by looking for frequent fliers,” Rio suggests. “Letters from the same email address, or different addresses but similar verbiage.”

Agnes lifts an eyebrow. “Verbiage?”

“Yeah. Like the wording.”

“I know what it means. I’m just trying to decide if I need to chug my beer.” She shrugs in response to Rio’s questioning look. “I’m playing a game where every time you sound like you work for the FBI, I drink.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “I do work for the FBI.”

Agnes tilts her head back and starts gulping down her beer and Rio snorts. “Stop it.”

Agnes puts down her glass, wiping the back of her hand across her mouth. “Gotta entertain ourselves somehow.”

“What – death threats not good enough for you?”

“Doubt it,” Agnes says, grabbing a letter from the pile. “Let’s see. ‘Die capitalist scum.’” She turns the page around so Rio can see it. “That’s it. That’s all it says. I mean what is that, a form letter? Where’s the feeling? Where’s the poetry?”

“Yeah,” Rio says with an amused shrug. “People just don’t cut letters out of magazines like they used to. It’s a dying art.”

“I’m telling you, the internet ruins everything.”

Rio picks up her glass and downs half her beer in a few large gulps.

“What?” she asks, catching her breath as Agnes stares at her blankly. “Oh – did I not mention? I’m playing a game where every time you sound like a small-town crank, I drink.”

Agnes shakes her head, breaking into a slow smile. “Mm. I see what you did there,” she says, pointing at her. “You stole my joke.”

“I did.”

“‘Small-town crank?’”

Rio eyes Agnes's shirt, her sleeves rolled up to reveal the muscles of her forearms. “If the flannel fits...” 

“Excuse me, what’s wrong with my flannel?”

“Nothing,” Rio says. “It’s – no, it’s good. You pull it off.”

“You’re damn right I do,” Agnes says, picking up another letter and squinting at the text. “Alright, let’s see what else we got. Wife with cancer… claim denied… ah, okay. ‘You’re a murderer. You might as well have stabbed her in the heart. Don’t be surprised when we start fighting back.’”

“‘You sentenced my son to death,’” Rio reads from another letter, “‘and I swear to god I’m going to make sure you suffer as much as he did.’”

“Well, that’s got a little punch, at least. Oh, here we go: ‘You think that fancy algorithm can predict when and where you’ll take your last breath, bitch?’” Agnes gives a satisfied nod. “See? Now that’s how you write a death threat.”

“Very… passionate,” Rio agrees.

“Speaking of passion.” Agnes fishes out a letter from the other, smaller pile, waggling her eyebrows. “Let’s see what Mr. Tech Genius’s secret girlfriend had to say.” She clears her throat; when she speaks, it’s in a ridiculous, breathy voice. “‘I’m not getting anything done today. I can still taste you on my lips – it’s so hard to focus when my body is aching for you.’” She rolls her eyes. “Ugh.”

Rio laughs – at the voice, at Agnes’s disgusted face – and picks up another. 

“‘I keep thinking about you sitting in that big office all by yourself,’” she reads. “‘Do you ever think about how easy it would be to lock the door and—’”

She closes her mouth.

“What?” Agnes asks.

“Nope,” Rio says. “Not reading that out loud.”

Agnes laughs and snatches the letter out of her hand. “Wow,” she laughs, skimming it. “Well, you wanted verbiage.”

“Yeah, careful what you wish for,” Rio says. “Not to speak ill of the dead, but I can’t believe that guy had women writing stuff like this to him.”

Agnes’s eyes are still scanning the page in front of her. “What, you telling me you’re not drowning in erotic love letters, Agent?”

Rio snorts into her drink. “Maybe once I make my first million.” She sets her glass back down, turning it idly, and pokes her tongue into her cheek as she looks Agnes up and down. “Why, are you?”

Agnes barks a laugh. “Me? No. I’m not exactly, uh… literary.”

“Oh, so just pictures then?” Rio asks in a teasing voice. But instead of the snarky comeback Rio’s expecting, Agnes seems to flush a little, eyes snapping back to the letter in front of her.

“Oh,” Rio says, raising her eyebrows. “Detective O’Connor. Are you seeing someone?”

“No,” she says, waving a hand like the idea is absurd.

“Ah. More of a no-strings-attached situation, then?”

“It’s not – I’m – what is this, an interrogation about my love life?” 

Rio drops her mouth into a playful gasp, eyes widening. “Love?” 

“Oh, for fuck’s sake,” Agnes grumbles. After all her bravado, this awkward bashfulness is actually kind of endearing. “Look, the dating pool in a town like this is… small. And you know how the job is. So. Yeah.”

“Well, at least they leave you something to remember them by.”

Agnes snorts a little when she laughs. “Right.”

Images suddenly flicker through Rio’s mind: those piercing blue eyes, lit only by the light of a phone in the dark, staring intently at the screen as she unbuttons her jeans – shoving her hand below the rough denim, biting her lip as her fingers find herself, eyes closing, head falling back with a groan— 

Jesus. 

Fuck.

Get it together, Vidal.

Rio hopes the warmth she can feel crawling up her face isn’t an actual blush. “Well. Anyway,” she says, valiantly attempting a return to professionalism. “Dottie’s right – if Porter was having an affair, that’d give the wife motive.” 

She picks up a slice of pizza to give herself something to do with her hands. And her mouth. 

“Sure, that and the millions of dollars she’s gonna inherit. If it even turns out to be a homicide,” Agnes says. And then she gestures at Rio’s face. “You’ve got—”

“What?”

Agnes waves her closer, and Rio leans forward into Agnes’s outstretched hand. She cups Rio’s face, running a rough thumb across her lower lip.

“Sauce,” Agnes says. Her voice and mannerisms are entirely practical, in stark contrast to the sudden wild hammering of Rio’s heart.

“Oh. Thanks.”

She runs her tongue over the place Agnes’s finger had just been and takes a long breath in. 

“…no blood, no signs of a struggle, no evidence of a break in,” Agnes is saying, and Rio forces herself to pay attention. “It’s gonna be natural causes, and you’re gonna have to go back to DC with your tail between your legs.”

Rio’s not really up for talking about what may or may not be happening between her legs at the moment.

“Maybe,” she says, licking her lips again. “Still. Guy that rich dies that young? We have to look into it.”

“Oh, well, of course. We wouldn’t want any big fancy political donors to get nervous.” 

Rio gives her a look. “I couldn’t speak to that.”

“Oh, no? That classified, Agent?” Agnes asks, lifting one corner of her mouth. She makes a big show of taking a drink, ending with an ostentatious ahhhhh. Then she rolls her eyes. “Come on – quit being a fed and have an opinion. We’re off the clock.”

Rio glances at the papers scattered between them. "Are we?"

Agnes leans back, arms stretched along the booth's cracked vinyl. "So were you born with that stick up your ass or was it a graduation gift from Quantico?”

Rio shakes her head, but she can’t help smiling back at her. “Alright, fine – yes, I’m mostly here so the FBI director can reassure a bunch of politicians that we’re looking into it. Donors get freaked out when stuff like this happens.”

“‘Stuff’ like a heart attack?”

“Porter’s well-connected. This is how the world works. I’ll spend a few days looking around, the medical examiner will confirm it was nothing, and then I’ll go.”

“Mm. Well, that all sounds very by-the-book.”

“Yup.”

Agnes leans forward and picks up her drink with a wry smile. “‘Just the facts, ma’am’?”

Rio laughs and rolls her eyes. “Yeah, alright. Take your drink.”

“I’ll be lucky if I don’t die of alcohol poisoning at this rate,” Agnes says. And then she tilts her head back and she drinks again.

Rio pretends not to watch her throat as she swallows.

 

x

 

Rio’s eyes flutter open the next morning, teased awake by the daylight glittering around the edges of the room’s blackout curtains. She burrows down into the scratchy motel blanket and groans. She’s not hungover, really; she hadn’t gotten drunk drunk. Tipsy, though. Maybe more than tipsy. Enough to have to run the events of last night through her head now, to try and decide whether or not she’d embarrassed herself. 

Pizza. Another pitcher of beer. More letters – the death threats, and the other ones. Calloused fingers curled around paper. Agnes devouring her pizza, wiping her mouth, crumpling her napkins. Eyes focused on the letters, on the words. And then, with an intensity that sent a jolt through her every time, on Rio. 

“I think I’m just going to walk,” Rio had said as they emerged into the crisp night. “They won’t tow my car, right?”

“Nah.” Agnes scratched the back of her neck, then shoved her hands into her jacket pockets. “You know where you’re going? Want company?”

Rio wasn’t entirely sure what Agnes was asking, but whatever it was, she wanted to say yes. She should have said yes; she spent the entire walk back kicking herself for not saying yes. But she didn’t.

Instead, she’d returned to the motel, unlocked her door, brushed her teeth, washed her face, changed into a tank top and boxers, crawled under the blankets, turned off the lights, and tried not to think about Agnes. She’d rested her hands on her stomach and closed her eyes. She was not going to be the sort of person who went home and got off while fantasizing about her colleagues. She was a professional. She was here to do a job.

And it didn’t even make sense. Rio liked a woman in flannel as much as the next lesbian, but Agnes really wasn’t her type. She was too gruff, too rough around the edges. Rio tended to be drawn to cerebral, hyper-articulate women, women who brought her to her knees with their cleverness and ambition and brutal wit. Sharp suits and sharp tongues. Not… small-town detectives with unbrushed hair and a sarcastic streak.

But she lifted a hand, running a finger over her lower lip, thinking about the way Agnes’s thumb had felt as it brushed across it. The image flashed again in her mind: blue eyes squeezed shut, back arching.

She’d trailed her hand back down, slipping it under her waistband, lower, but she barely had to touch herself to feel how wet she was. She gritted her teeth and groaned, pulling her hand away and flipping over onto her stomach, balling her hands into fists, shoving them under her pillow. 

She imagined Agnes pinning her down and fucking her from behind.

“Stop,” she’d said to herself, out loud, into the pillowcase. “Fuck’s sake.” It had taken what felt like hours, but eventually she’d fallen asleep with her hands clutching the sheets into starbursts.

She sits up now, checking the clock by the bed. A little before eight. The mirror hanging on the wall across from the bed reflects her outline in the dim light of the room, hair a shadowy tangle framing her face. She tilts her head from side to side. Her neck is killing her.

But an hour later she’s showered, dressed, and doing her best to act like a reasonable facsimile of an FBI agent. The smell of coffee and bacon greets her as she pushes open the door of the Westview Diner.

“Sit anywhere you like, hon,” a waitress tells her, breezing by. 

She slides into a booth and pulls out her laptop. This is what FBI agents do, right? They drink coffee, they check emails, they write up reports. They don’t sit around daydreaming about hot older women. Too busy for that. Too important.

“Well, if it isn’t DC’s finest.”

You’ve gotta be fucking kidding me.

“Morning,” Rio says, pasting a smile on her face and ignoring the flutter in her stomach as she glances up to find Agnes gazing down at her.

“You look exhausted,” Agnes says, sliding into the booth. She grins. “Late night?”

“Gee, thanks,” Rio says wryly as Agnes chuckles at her own joke. “Yeah, someone kept me up past my bedtime.”

Agnes glances around the diner, nodding hello to a group of men across the room who give her disinterested nods back. “Well,” she says after a moment, “if you think a walk would perk you up, I’m about to head out on a hike.”

“A hike? It’s Wednesday.”

“My day off,” Agnes says. She’s looking over Rio’s shoulder again, waving at the waitress to bring her coffee. 

“Oh,” Rio says. “Well – if it’s your day off, you know, you don’t have to worry about the interview with the wife. I can handle it.”

“Are you kidding? This is my case,” Agnes says as the waitress comes over with a pot of coffee and two mugs. Rio raises her eyebrows. “Fine: our case. I’m not missing that interview. Anyway – you want to come along, or what?”

Rio takes a sip of her coffee, the bitter black pooling on her tongue. 

“I didn’t really pack for hiking,” she says, gesturing at her pristine white button-up. 

“I’ve got clothes you can borrow.” 

Agnes says it casually, stirring her coffee, sipping it. Casual or not, it leads Rio’s brain down a path she can’t afford to follow: the two of them, alone on a trail together for hours, panting, exertion, sweat, the fabric of Agnes’s clothes grazing against her like brush of fingertips, like the flat palm of a hand on skin—

“I’ve… got a ton of paperwork to get through,” she says, gesturing at her laptop.

“Mm.” Agnes nods, eyeing her. And then she inhales and pushes herself up. “Well, I’ll leave you to it then.”

Rio has the uncomfortable feeling she just failed a test she didn’t realize she was taking.

“Have fun,” she tells her.

Agnes downs the last of her coffee. “Sure. Enjoy your paperwork, Agent.”

Rio’s eyes trail her out the door. She wants to stand, wants to follow. Wants to pull one of Agnes’s t-shirts on and spend the day rambling through the woods with this strange, blunt, intriguingly attractive woman. She runs a hand across the top of her laptop screen, trying to remind herself of all the reasons she shouldn’t close it right now and run after her, tell her she changed her mind.

An insistent buzz vibrates her pocket.

Right.

“Hey, boss.”

“Hey, kid, how’s it going?” Lilia asks.

“Oh, you know. It’s going.”

She stares out the window at the place Agnes had just been. 

“…Okay, well, you’re gonna have to give me a little more than that,” Lilia says. Rio can hear the ironic smile in her voice, but she can also tell that she’s not happy. “Newark is still on my ass about putting an outside agent in their jurisdiction. I told the SAC that you’d be in and out, so… you gonna be in and out? What’s going on?”
