“Uh-huh.”

“What?”

Jen gives a little shrug. “You’ve got a thing for unhinged women. Everyone knows it.”

Rio feels heat crawl up her neck. “I do not.”

“Yes, you do. You get this look when they’re around. This freaky little gleam in your eye.”

Rio opens her mouth to protest, but Jen waves a hand. “Whatever, it’s fine. We all have our things. Mine is being the most attractive person in every room, yours is a weird creepy obsession with female serial killers. So are you gonna tell me about her, or what?”

Rio tilts her head. “Oh, because I’m obsessed?”

“Yeah, yeah. Spill.”

“I don’t know. She was…” Rio trails off, trying to think of a safe answer.

She hasn’t told anyone how far things went with Agnes (with Agatha, she corrects herself for the millionth time). She knows she should – it’s a relevant detail, proof of how far Agatha is willing to go to insinuate herself into an investigation – but the fact that Rio was completely taken in by the woman professionally is bad enough. Admitting to everyone that she was also stupid enough to fall for her personally is a humiliation she hasn’t been able to convince herself to face.

“She was funny, I guess,” she says finally. “In a sarcastic way.”

Jen blinks. "That's it? You spent days with this woman and all you can come up with is 'funny in a sarcastic way'? Wow, I can’t imagine how she managed to slip past your legendary people-reading skills."

“Okay. Fine.” Rio licks her lips. “She was… I don’t know. She was arrogant. She was sort of posturing, playing it larger-than-life, but it wasn’t bullshit. And she was smart. She made me laugh.”

“Agnes did, or Agatha?”

The question is pointed, barbed, but Rio answers it anyway. She’s almost grateful to talk about it; it’s the same question that’s been plaguing her for days. “I mean… you can’t really fake charisma, right? Or intelligence. That stuff had to be her – the real her. And the rest of it was just... whatever she thought would make me trust her, I guess.”

Jen makes a thoughtful noise. “Did you?”

“Did I trust her?”

“Yeah.”

Rio rolls her eyes. “We had like three conversations.”

“You’re deflecting,” Jen says. “Interesting.”

“Oh, for fuck’s – you know this is why everyone hates interview specialists, right?”

Jen smirks. “Because we’re smarter than everyone else?”

“Yeah. That’s exactly what I meant.” Rio drops her gaze, clearing her throat as she picks at the seam of her coffee cup. “So… does everyone know?”

“About your new girlfriend?” Jen asks, and Rio shoots her a look.

Jen can push anyone’s buttons, but when it comes to Rio she's got the advantage of years of history. They'd hated each other since they trained up together at Quantico, but Lilia had some kind of intuition about partnerships, some sense that they’d work well together. Whatever the reason was, she'd thrown them together on case after case until their snide hostility evolved into... whatever this is. Healthy competition. Grudging respect. Something Rio might even call friendship, on a good day.

It’s not that she wants to lie to Jen – or to Lilia and Alice, for that matter. But what’s she supposed to do? Put down her coffee cup and announce that she fucked a serial killer?

Honestly, this would all be easier if Rio could just stop thinking about it. If she could wipe it all from her mind, somehow – Agatha’s hands, her fingers, her impatient mouth. If she could manage to forget the words she’d murmured, the feel of her breath on bare skin.

“So what—” Jen begins, but she’s interrupted by knuckles rapping on Rio’s doorframe.

“Knock, knock,” Lilia says in a lilting voice. She glances down at the cups they’re both holding. “Did someone go on a coffee run?”

“It’s pity coffee,” Rio tells her. “You don’t want any.”

“Hm,” Lilia says doubtfully. “Conference room, both of you. Alice has something.”

 

 

x

 

 

A massive picture of Agatha Harkness greets Rio as she walks inside. It’s the same one Alice had emailed her before, the young woman with the universe revolving around her. Alice has displayed it on the screen that dominates one wall of the conference room, and Rio stares up at it for a moment, trying again to reconcile this woman – her tasteful dress, her sleek hair – with the person she’d spent the past few days with.

“You good?” Alice murmurs to her as the four of them sit down around the table. Shit – Rio never called her back. Between meeting with Westview’s police chief, fielding Lilia’s questions, searching the AirB&B for evidence, and the incessant thrum of Rio’s own internal panic, things had kind of gotten away from her.

“Of course she’s good,” Jen says. “Getting to hang out with a serial killer is Rio’s dream.”

“I’m good, yeah,” she says, ignoring Jen. Alice doesn’t look entirely convinced. “I will be,” she tells her. “Once we find her.”

“Speaking of,” Lilia says, nodding at Alice.

“Right.” Alice presses a button on her laptop and the picture of Agatha disappears, replaced by the photo of a nondescript office building. “Okay. This is Mercix Pharmaceuticals, headquartered in Baltimore. They’re a biotech company – standard stuff, R&D, genomic sequencing, you know the drill. And earlier this year…”

She presses another button, and a police report appears onscreen.

“An employee they’d hired three days earlier routed a shipment of pharmaceutical-grade Prussian blue to an offsite location, then disappeared. The local PD looked into it, but they didn’t turn anything up.”

Rio scans the report. Suspect: Amelia Davis (likely alias). Caucasian female, late 40s/early 50s, brown hair.

“Okay, but you said this stuff was tracked,” Rio says. “Did the FDA look into it?”

“Well, the FDA doesn’t track individual shipments – they leave that to manufacturers and distributors. It looks like they did do a follow-up audit to make sure the facility was complying with federal security regulations, and Mercix got dinged for not flagging address changes to shipments, but that’s about it. And it’s not a controlled substance, so the DEA wasn’t interested. It just kind of… slipped through the cracks.”

The image on the screen changes again, and suddenly Rio is staring into Agatha’s eyes. The picture is an ID badge the pharmaceutical company had issued to Amelia Davis. Agatha doesn’t look like Agnes in this picture, but she doesn’t look like the young woman from the party photo, either. She’s smiling tentatively here, hair pulled back into a modest bun, wearing a button-down shirt and glasses. She looks… mousy. She looks like someone you would look right past.

Rio can’t stop looking at her.

“That’s your girl, right?” Jen asks.

Rio blinks. She manages to tear her eyes away from the photo. You get this freaky little gleam in your eye.

“That’s her.”

When she glances back up the screen has changed again, to display an array of nine crime scene photos. Dates and locations beneath the pictures show they’re all from the past twenty-five years, up and down the east coast.

“These are cases I’ve identified so far that match the MO,” Alice says. “We’ve got businessmen and a few politicians, all dead from heart attacks, and all with some indication of cyanide poisoning.”

“Any of them linked to the Energetic Sovereignty movement?” Rio asks.

“I’m looking into it, but… the group was pretty secretive. People weren’t exactly shouting about their involvement from the rooftops.”

“Well,” Lilia says, “do what you can. Start preparing a dossier on the whole cult – membership, beliefs, anything you can find. And I want to see everything you’ve got on Agatha Harkness.”

“There’s not much out there on her or the cult, as far as I can tell,” Alice says. “But I’ll get you what I can.” She presses a button, and the screen changes again to display the two pictures they have of Agatha, side-by-side. Rio stares up at her.

“We should go talk to the lab in Baltimore,” Jen says. “See if there’s anything they left out of the police report.”

The others continue talking, but Rio barely hears them. She studies the photos, eyes flickering back and forth between them. It’s like looking at two different women – sisters, maybe, or cousins. She can’t figure out quite how she’s managed to transform herself so completely. Is it the hair? The glasses? Something in her posture?

“Agent Vidal,” Lilia says, and Rio jumps a little.

“Yeah – sorry. Yes?”

Lilia sighs. “Head in the game, kid. I want a task force on this woman, and I want you to head it up. Track her down, bring her in. Got it?”

A task force. Rio spares half a second to feel gratitude for the vote of confidence, and another half-second to wonder if this is just Lilia’s version of pity coffee. But the reason doesn’t really matter.

“Yeah. Absolutely,” she says. “We’ll find her.”

“Good,” Lilia says, standing up from the table. “Alright, then. I’ll leave you to it.”

Lilia gathers her things and starts to leave, but she pauses in the doorway, turning back around to look at the three of them.

“There’s no indication that she’s ever done this before. Infiltrated an investigation.” Her eyes land on Rio. “Why do you think she did it now?”

Rio’s been asking herself the same question since the moment she opened that envelope.

“Honestly? I have no idea.”

Alice shrugs. “Maybe she liked you.”

“Or maybe she wanted to murder you,” Jen says in a perky voice.

“Yeah,” Rio says dryly. “The thought had crossed my mind.”

“That is the question we need to answer,” Lilia says. “Why this, and why now. Focus on that, and it’ll lead us to her.”

 

 

x

 

 

They’ve nearly arrived at the lab when Rio announces the change of plan.

“Excuse me?” Jen demands from the passenger’s seat. “What do you mean, you’re not coming?”

“Look,” Rio says. “We’re going to have to check out both the lab and the warehouse, right? So why not divide and conquer?”

“Uh, because we made the trip specifically for this? You don’t even want to hear what they have to say?”

“I’ll hear what they have to say when you tell me what they said.” She glances over at Jen, whose eyes are narrowed suspiciously. “Hey, I’m just trying to be nice. I figured you’d rather do the interview in the nice clean lab and let me handle the dusty warehouse full of spiders, but if you want to do both, that’s fine with me.”

Jen purses her lips as she considers. “Well,” she says after a beat. “When you put it that way.”

“Mm-hm. You’re welcome.”

Rio’s not entirely sure why, but she wants to see that warehouse, and she wants to see it alone. She’s fairly certain this trip isn’t going to turn up any smoking guns – they already know Agatha stole the Prussian blue, and she’s smart enough not to leave anything really incriminating behind. But if there is anything worth finding, it’s certainly not going to be discovered in some sterile lab where Agatha pretended to be a mild-mannered scientist by day. It’s going to be in that warehouse – and Rio wants time to see it, to examine the place without Jen following her around whining about dirt and cobwebs.

But it’s more than that. For some reason she can’t quite articulate, she just… wants to be somewhere she knows Agatha has been. Not Agnes. Not Amelia Davis. Agatha. As herself.

Rio drops Jen off at Mercix – “Enjoy your spiders,” she’d said, gliding out of the car without a backward glance – and makes her way to the warehouse, weeds and gravel crunching beneath her tires as she pulls up to the building. She shuts off the engine and peers out her windshield. The day is bright, sun glittering off the jagged edges of broken windows. Graffiti competes for space with ivy on the worn brick of the exterior, though none of the paint seems fresh – apparently even taggers haven’t bothered making the trek this far outside of town recently.

The entrance to the building is a gap of darkness like a missing tooth. Rio rests her hand on her gun as she slowly walks inside. It takes her eyes a moment to adjust to the dim light.

She can tell right away that she’s not likely to find much here. The space is vast and mostly empty, littered with a few old crates and pallets. The cement floor is strewn with cardboard, shingles, random debris. Rio doesn’t know what she expected, really: that Agatha would have made this some sort of home base? A lair? She’s not a fucking supervillain.

She wanders around, gently nudging trash and small pieces of lumber out of the way with the toe of her shoe. Some of the pallets have been stacked into shapes that could maybe be tables, and she examines each of them closely, but if Agatha made cyanide poisoning here she didn’t leave anything behind. Rio makes her way over to a set of doors, one of them hanging off its hinges, leading to what must have been the main office of the factory that used to be here. She stands in the doorway, looking around. Some old shelving built into the wall; a few rickety wooden chairs missing legs or spindles.

There’s nothing. This is nothing. There’s no sign of Agatha, no clues to be had. This was a stupid waste of time. She should have done the interview with Jen.

“Hey, sweetheart.”

Rio spins around and raises her gun in one fluid movement.

Agatha Harkness stands before her, looking outrageously, unfairly beautiful. Her hair is piled on top of her head like a crown, her outfit elegant, immaculate. She’s wearing a white button-up shirt, her hands tucked in the pockets of her wide-legged pants, long coat nearly sweeping the floor like a gown. Her presence here is so entirely unexpected – and so bafflingly incongruent with the decrepit building around them – that all Rio can do for a few seconds is blink at her like an idiot.

“What are you—?” she begins, but the sound of her own voice reminds her where she is, who she is, what she’s doing here. “Agatha Harkness,” she says, the words hard, clipped. “You’re under arrest for the murder of Ansel Porter.”

Agatha looks vaguely amused. “Am I?”

“Show me your hands.”

Agatha tilts her head at Rio, giving her a knowing smile. “Mm. Well, you do like me with my hands above my head, don’t you?”

She removes her hands from her pockets and slowly lifts them, and Rio moves quickly, circling around behind her. She holsters her weapon and reaches for the handcuffs on her belt.

“Really, baby?” Agatha says. “Come on, don’t ruin handcuffs for us. We haven’t even had any fun with them yet.”

She steps back suddenly, dropping her weight to try and knock Rio off balance, but Rio’s not some baby-faced beat cop making her first arrest. She moves with Agatha, using the momentum to spin her around and slam her back into the wall. Her body presses against Agatha's, pinning her in place, and Rio can feel the warmth radiating through Agatha's shirt, smell her perfume – earthy and lush, different than what Agnes had worn – mixed with the dust and decay of the warehouse.

“Ooh, aren’t you big and strong,” Agatha says. She bites her lower lip. “We can play this game, but if you’re gonna hurt me, sweetheart, make it hurt.”

“Shut up,” Rio says. Their faces are inches apart, Agatha’s breath warm against her skin. “What are you doing here?”

“I thought you might be upset about the way we left things.”

“The way we left – you mean the murder? You mean worming your way into my investigation and nearly destroying my career? Completely humiliating me? That way we left things?”

Agatha clicks her tongue. “I knew you’d be upset.”

“Why did you kill Porter?”

“What?” Agatha asks, widening her eyes innocently. “Oh, I don’t think you’ll find evidence I had anything to do with that.”

“Why were you hanging around the case? Why pretend to be a cop?”

Agatha tilts her chin up, bringing her mouth closer to Rio's. The movement is small, subtle, but it’s the thing that almost makes Rio take a step back. Almost.

“Maybe I just saw something I liked,” Agatha murmurs. “You’ve never told a lie to get close to a pretty girl?”

“I’ve never fucking murdered anyone.”

“I’ve got to say, I was a little surprised you went for Agnes, though,” Agatha continues as though Rio hadn’t spoken. “I wasn’t sure she’d be your type.”

“She’s not,” Rio snaps.

“No?” Agatha gives her a wry smirk. “That’s not how it seemed when I was knuckle-deep inside you.”

The memory hits her with the force of a bullet, and she clenches her jaw as she fights against the tight ache building low in her belly. She should step back, call this in. She should do her fucking job.

Instead she stays pressed against Agatha, breathing.

“So are you going to be hunting me now?” Agatha asks. “Ooh – tell me there’s some sort of elite squad dedicated to my downfall.”

Her playful tone almost feels familiar. It almost feels like Agnes, except there’s an edge beneath it that wasn’t there before. Agnes had a softness to her, a quiet vulnerability, but Agatha is pure confidence all the way down.

“No one’s going to be hunting you,” Rio says, tightening her grip on Agatha’s arm, “because you’re under arrest.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “You know, this would be a lot more fun if you stopped being such a fucking FBI agent about everything.”

She moves, fast and sudden, spinning them both around and slamming Rio against the rough brick wall.

Rio’s stronger, and she has a gun; she could fight her off. But she doesn’t. Her training is screaming at her to move, to regain control, but her body betrays her. She doesn’t fight when Agatha slides a thigh between her legs, pressing up against her with deliberate pressure; she doesn’t fight when Agatha’s hand finds her throat. Memories come roaring to the surface at her touch: Agnes's rough hands, the way she'd whispered Rio's name, the desperate need that had consumed them both. The way Agnes had panted and licked her lips; the way she’d come undone, again and again, back arching and desperate.

But this isn't Agnes.

Agatha inspects Rio now with predatory eyes, eyes that are shrewd, starving. She’s a murderer, Rio thinks – but still, she doesn’t fight. She stays perfectly still as Agatha leans in. Stays still as she runs her lips up the curve of Rio’s neck, feather-light and agonizing.

“Don’t you want me to have fun with you?” she murmurs, breath hot in Rio’s ear, and groan escapes the back of Rio’s throat, small and needy.

She clamps her mouth shut, but it’s too late. Agatha lifts a knowing eyebrow.

“That’s what I thought,” she says.

Rio’s mind buzzes. She feels like a deer staring into the eyes of a wolf, hungering for the vulgar bite of its teeth.

She lifts her hand and places it over Agatha’s on her throat.

She should pull her away. She should take Agatha’s arm, twist at the wrist, slam her into the wall and handcuff her.

Instead, she tightens her grip. She presses her fingers around Agatha's hand until she can feel Agatha's nails digging into her skin, hard enough to bruise. Agatha’s eyes widen slightly, searching Rio’s face, hungry and euphoric.

Together their grip tightens, slow and deliberate. Rio’s pulse pounds in her ears as her breathing becomes shallow, restricted, and then ceases altogether.

An eternity seems to pass between them as they stare at one another. Agatha’s eyes are a deep azure, her pupils blown. The look on her face is fervent as a true believer praying to her god.

Rio drops her hand to Agatha's wrist, tugging a little, signaling for her to let go. But Agatha doesn’t let go. If anything, her grip tightens.

Fuck. Rio tries to rasp out her name – Agatha – but no sound comes out.

“Shhh, baby,” Agatha says softly.

Rio pulls on Agatha's arm, urgent now, her survival instincts belatedly kicking in. She tries to push her away, but Agatha presses against her harder, using her full body weight to pin Rio to the wall.

“Ah ah,” she tsks. “Don’t fight me.”

Don’t fight a serial killer wrapping her hands around my throat? Rio thinks, heart pounding wildly in her chest. Adrenaline floods her system as her brain shouts at her that she needs air, she needs to breathe, but somewhere beneath her panic the echo of Agnes’s voice comes back to her like a whisper:

I want you to feel this.

Words spoken like a promise, like an incantation. Like something she needed Rio to understand.

Rio's lightheaded and desperate, her vision beginning to telescope. Klaxons are ringing in her ears, but beneath that primal alarm something else is singing – a dark, hungry note that says yes. That says more.

I want you to feel this.

And she does feel it – the exquisite edge between control and chaos, between life and death, between who she's supposed to be and who she really is.

And so she does the only thing she can think of to do in the face of this woman. The only thing she wants to do, in the darkest and quietest part of herself.

She gives in.

“That’s it,” Agatha murmurs as Rio drops her hands to her sides. Her lungs burn, but she doesn't look away from Agatha's face. They stare at one another as Rio struggles to stay conscious. Agatha leans in, close, like she might kiss her, and Rio closes her eyes, ready to accept it.

And then she gasps, throwing her head back and sucking in air as Agatha finally releases her grip. Each breath in is the sweetest thing Rio has ever tasted, and she gulps it down, her vision refocusing, her dizziness coming back into balance. Agatha’s hand is still on Rio’s throat, gently stroking it with her thumb.

“Oh, we are going to have fun together,” she says in a delighted voice.

Rio grabs Agatha’s wrist, hard, and pulls it away. “You’re under arrest,” she manages to rasp.

Agatha purses her lips mischievously. “Are you sure?” she asks slowly, shifting her thigh, and Rio has to work hard to keep her eyes from fluttering closed at the jolt of pleasure between her legs.

There’s a sudden clicking sound, and the feel of cold metal biting into Rio’s wrist. She snaps her head down to find Agatha handcuffing her to a metal pipe.

“What are – are you fucking kidding me?” Rio asks hoarsely, handcuffs clanging as she tries to lunge toward Agatha, who’s backing away.

“Aww.” Agatha sticks out her lower lip in an exaggerated pout. “Sorry, sweetheart. But you look so much better in handcuffs than I do.”

Rio bares her teeth and growls, rooting around on her belt for the keys. She glances down, searching with shaking hands, desperately hoping Agatha hadn’t stolen them along with the handcuffs.

“This was great,” Agatha calls over her shoulder. “We’ll have to do it again sometime.” Rio glances back up in time to see her blow her a kiss from the doorway.

And then she’s gone.

Chapter 3

Rio stares down at the crime scene photos scattered across her desk and tries to focus. Nine victims over twenty-five years, all of them dead from what appeared to be heart attacks, all of them powerful or notable enough that the police had bothered digging into cause of death. Alice had warned her that there could be more victims – Like, tens more, she’d said, hundreds more – if it turns out Agatha’s MO goes beyond killing the rich and famous. There wouldn’t be crime scene photos if no one suspected a crime.

The scenes in the photos are bloodless, almost serene. A man sitting at a desk, head lolling back. A woman in her car, still parked in the garage, keys in the ignition. Death like a jarring period in the middle of an unfinished sentence.

How did Agatha get close to them? Rio wonders, staring down at the pictures. Did she sneak in? Did she pose as an employee? A friend? A lover?

Her stomach twists at the thought of Agatha tracing a teasing fingertip over the lower lip of the woman in the car, pressing a kiss to her delicate jawline. The woman had been on her way to work when she died. Was Agatha upstairs in her bed when it happened? Was she stretching out, naked and feline and content, luxuriating in the feeling of having killed her?

Are you really jealous of a woman she murdered?  She closes her eyes and shakes her head, trying to clear her thoughts.

But when she opens her eyes again, her gaze wanders over to the other photo on her desk: Agatha, young and haughty, staring directly into the camera like she’s daring Rio to look away. Rio leans in, studying the shape of her mouth, wincing as she tilts her head.

The bruises on her neck have faded to a pale yellow-green, hidden beneath makeup and the high collar of her shirt. And after a lot of tea with honey, her voice is finally back to normal. But she can still feel the phantom pressure of Agatha’s hand every time she moves. Can still remember the way her pulse had jumped to meet her touch like it was coming home.

By the time she’d managed to free herself from the handcuffs and run outside, Agatha was long gone. Rio had stalked around the entire property, desperately searching for something she could bring back to the team that wasn’t a bruised neck, bruised wrists, bruised ego. But there was nothing.

“Uh, did you smoke three hundred packs of cigarettes while you were gone?” Jen had asked when Rio picked her up from Mercix. “What’s wrong with your voice?”

Rio should have told her then and there. She should have owned up to the basic facts, at least, admitted that Agatha had gotten the jump on her, gotten away. Instead, in the face of yet another failure… Rio panicked.

“Allergies,” she’d rasped. “Told you it was gonna be dusty.”

Jen had given a prim sniff. “If you brought spiders into this car, I will scream.”

"Rio?"

She jerks her head up to find Alice standing in her doorway. “God – you startled me.”

“Sorry,” Alice says, stepping inside. “I said your name a few times. You okay?”

“Yeah,” Rio says, quickly shuffling the photos on her desk into a neat stack. “What’s up?”

“You told me to work on tracking down anyone who might be able to talk to us about Agatha Harkness. I think I found someone.”

Rio has to stop herself from jumping to her feet. “Have I told you lately that you're incredible?"

"And beautiful, and brilliant."

"Well, it's true. Who'd you find?”

“Her sixth-grade teacher.”

“Sixth grade?” Rio echoes. “There’s no one a little more… recent?”

Alice shrugs. “She pretty much goes off the grid once she’s eighteen. Lot of aliases, credit cards and IDs under different names… I’m still trying to piece it all together. But back then she was just Agatha, so this is what we’ve got.”

“Right. Sorry, I didn’t mean – this is great. Background will be helpful. How long until we can set something up?”

“You can go today, if you want. She’s only about an hour outside the city.”

Rio does stand now, already reaching for her suit jacket. “Amazing. Have you seen Jen?”

“She’s testifying in court today. That trafficking case.”

“Shit,” Rio says, deflating a little. “Right.”

“Do you need her?”

Rio doesn’t. Or she shouldn’t, anyway – she’s done a million interviews on her own. But she doesn’t want to be alone for this one.

The problem is, she’d misread Agnes. Badly. She had no inkling she wasn’t who she said she was. Nothing set off alarm bells, not even when they slept together. And then, after whatever the fuck happened at the warehouse…

It’s not like she expects Agatha to waltz into this teacher’s house and throw her up against a wall. She’s just not sure she could trust herself if she did.

“It’d be nice to have two sets of eyes on this one,” she says. “It’s a complex case.”

Alice gives her a knowing look. “You don’t need two sets of eyes on some little old lady, Rio. You’re letting Agatha Harkness get to you.”

“I’m not letting—”

“Yes you are. Look, I get it – it threw you off that she inserted herself into the investigation. But don’t start second-guessing yourself. You are an excellent agent, okay?”

Rio could tell her. She could explain. Alice would understand – she'd try to, at least. She’s always been the kindest of all of them, the most understanding, the most protective. She'd probably be gentle with Rio. She’d probably help her figure out what to do next.

I should have fought, Rio could say. I should have pushed Agatha away, cuffed her. I should have ripped her hand away from my throat.

But I didn’t. I stared into her eyes, and I submitted.

I gave myself to her.

I tightened my grip.

But something fierce and possessive flares in Rio's chest at the thought of putting that moment into words, making it real, and official, and part of the case file. A thing that people could put their eyes on, question and judge her over. She knows how it would look. What they’d think, what they’d say. And they’d probably be right.

Everything in her riots at the thought of letting anyone else near that moment. It’s something that belongs to her. To her, and to Agatha. No one else.

“How about you come with me?” she asks Alice, a question guaranteed to change the subject.

Alice’s eyes widen in alarm. “Oh, I don’t—”

“I know,” Rio interjects. “But like you said, she’s just a little old lady. And we’ll probably get more information about the cult. Don’t you want to ask questions?”

Alice hesitates, and Rio has to push away a pang of guilt. She knows Alice hates going out into the field. She’d had a few bad experiences early on in her career – nothing she talks about, but there were whispers of more than one operation gone wrong. Whatever had happened, it was bad enough that Alice had transitioned out of field work and into intelligence analysis. She spends most of her days tucked away behind a computer now, supporting the mission without leaving her desk.

I’m cursed, is how she tends to put it.

Rio juts out her lower lip playfully and flutters her eyelashes. “Please?” she asks. “Think of all the information we might get from her. You love information.”

Alice still looks doubtful, but she sighs. “A little old lady.”

“The littlest.”

“Yeah,” she says finally. “Okay.”

 

 

x

 

 

An hour and a half later, the two of them are sitting in a living room that’s decorated like an iced cupcake. The couch is white and stiff, covered in plastic that squeaks every time Rio shifts her weight. The whole place smells faintly of cloying potpourri. She blows at the steam curling from the teacup in her hands, the china delicate enough that she's afraid to grip it properly.

“Is it alright?” Mrs. Davis asks, leaning forward eagerly.

Rio takes a quick sip and immediately regrets it when it burns the shit out of her tongue.

“It’s perfect,” she says. Next to her, Alice takes her own tentative sip and blows out sharply, then smiles.

“Delicious.”

Mrs. Davis beams. “You know, Mr. Davis always insisted we serve coffee to our guests, but I told him, coffee is too bitter. People like tea.”

“Mm,” Rio says, trying to simultaneously agree and somehow inhale cool air over her tongue. “Well, we really do appreciate you meeting with us, Mrs. Davis.”

“Oh, please, call me Sharon. Only my students called me Mrs. Davis. Or – well, actually, Agatha would have called me Mrs. Hart. That was back before Mr. Davis and I had married, of course.”

“Sharon,” Rio agrees. She puts down her teacup and pulls out a notepad. “And you taught Agatha Harkness at St. Stephen’s?”

“Sixth grade English, yes.”

Alice gives a little grimace. “Awkward age.”

“Oh, you don’t know the half of it,” Sharon says with a laugh. “I used to call them my little giraffes – all knobby knees and long necks, tripping over themselves.” She purses her lips thoughtfully. “Not Agatha, though. She walked in like she owned that school from the very first day.”

“I’ll bet she did,” Rio mutters. She jots down the word confident, though anyone with eyes knew that much already. “Can you tell us more about her?”

Sharon opens her mouth to answer, and then hesitates. “You didn’t say what this was about when we spoke on the phone. Is Agatha in some kind of trouble?”

Rio gives her a bland smile. “Would you be surprised if she was?”

“Well, not… surprised, exactly,” Sharon says. “Agatha was – well, she was a challenging student.”

“Was she violent?” Alice asks. “I didn’t see a record of any disciplinary issues.”

“Oh, no, nothing like that,” Sharon says, waving a hand. “Nothing that would have made it into her record. She was just a handful. Charismatic, and – well, you hate to call a child devious, but that’s what she was.”

“Devious how?” Rio asks.

“Well, she didn’t do her own homework once the entire time I taught her, for one thing. She was careful not to get caught, but I just knew she had someone doing it for her. I tried to get to the bottom of it, but I could never figure out whether she was charming the other children into it, or bullying them. It was always like that with her: she was crafty, but she covered her tracks. You got the feeling she had about ten different little schemes running at any given time."

“You sound kind of impressed,” Rio says, and Sharon laughs.

“Well, she drove me crazy, but she had a brilliant mind. Honestly, if she hadn’t spent so much energy turning my classroom into a battlefield, she could have been the best student I ever had.”

“Battlefield?” Alice asks. “I thought you said she wasn’t violent.”

“No, no, she wasn’t.” Sharon sips her tea, thinking. “It’s hard to explain. There was nothing to point to, nothing that warranted discipline. But every time she would join a little gaggle of friends, within a few weeks, like clockwork, none of them would be friends anymore. They’d all be fighting. And then she would move on to the next group.”

“Okay...” Rio says slowly. “Is that unusual?” She doesn’t know much about kids, but she knows they’re all little assholes. This sounds like normal teenage drama.

“Well, obviously you expect a certain amount of conflict between children that age. But let me tell you, by the end of the school year, the entire class hated each other. I’ve never seen anything like it. And there was Agatha, right in the middle of it. Like she was conducting an orchestra.”

“So you think she… what, she manipulated them into disliking each other?” Alice asks. “Why would she do that?”

“Probably for the same reason some kids set ants on fire with a magnifying glass. I think she found it entertaining,” Sharon says with a shrug. And then her expression hardens. “But if anyone is to blame, it’s that mother of hers. Agatha was just a little girl, but that woman… she was a real witch. Pardon my language.”

“Really? How so?” Rio asks.

“Well, talk about manipulative. She’d managed to get the Board of Governors in her pocket, so every little thing I did had to go through her. If she didn’t like a book I was teaching, I had to teach another. If she thought I wasn’t assigning enough homework, I had to come up with more. If she didn’t like my essay questions, I had to rewrite them. And it was the same with all of Agatha’s teachers. Evanora Harkness basically set the curriculum for the entire school.”

Alice raises an eyebrow. “So she was a helicopter parent before it was cool.”

“How do you think she got the Board on her side?” Rio asks.

“Oh, it was that cult she ran,” Sharon says bluntly. “At least one of them must have been involved.”

Alice leans forward. “Do you know anything about the organization? We haven’t been able to find much.”

“Sorry, dear, I don’t know much. They were pretty secretive unless you were one of them. Although there was this pamphlet that was going around for a while – hang on, I might still have it somewhere. We used to pass it around at staff parties. Well, you have to laugh sometimes or you’ll go crazy, right?”

Sharon bustles over to a large bookshelf across the room, and runs her finger across what Rio realizes is a long row of yearbooks. A long row.

“How long were you a teacher?” she asks.

“Forty-three years. Best job in the world – well, most days. Aha, here we are.” Sharon pulls a yearbook down and flutters through the pages until a leaflet falls out. “I knew I still had it.”

She walks over, offering a typed and yellowing pamphlet to them, and Alice reaches for it eagerly. But Rio stares at the yearbook, curiosity curling in her chest.

“Could I – is there a picture of Agatha in there?”

“Oh, yes, of course you’ll want to see that,” Sharon says, flipping through the pages again. She holds out the book, opened to a page filled with black and white squares. The children are all decked out in their mid-80s finest: perms, braces, feathered bangs. They’re all wearing uniforms, the boys in little ties, the girls in blouses. Rio’s eyes skim over them, looking for the only picture she cares about. There – Agatha Harkness, second row, third picture.

“She doesn’t look devious,” says Alice, peering over Rio’s shoulder.

“Oh, the troublemakers never do,” Sharon says. “She had a very sweet smile.”

Twelve-year-old Agatha does have a sweet smile. Her hair is shoulder-length, her bangs surprisingly understated. She’s got little heart-shaped earrings in her ears. She looks like a kid. Just a kid, like any other. Not someone who would grow up to be a serial killer. Not someone who would someday corner Rio in a warehouse, wrap her hands around her throat—

“Was there ever a moment when you saw her guard come down?" Rio asks. 

“Oh,” Sharon says. She sounds a little surprised at the question. “No, not that I can remember. She always seemed to be completely self-assured, even at twelve. If there was anything beneath that, I certainly never saw it.”

“Did anyone ever get close to her? Did she let anyone in?”

Rio ignores Alice’s eyes on her.

“No. Well – can you blame them?” Sharon asks. “People don’t like to be treated like they’re pawns in someone else’s game. Anyone with any sense learned pretty quickly to head in the opposite direction when they saw her coming.” She shakes her head. “I don’t like to talk badly about any of my students, but the truth is, Agatha Harkness ruined every relationship she touched. She smiled all the time – the sweetest smile you ever saw. But let me tell you... that child was a bomb in the shape of a girl.” 

 

 

x

 

 

“Okay, listen to this,” Alice says from the passenger seat of the car, rattling the pamphlet Sharon Davis had given them and clearing her throat. “‘Energetic Sovereignty is the disciplined practice of mastering your thoughts, emotions, and reactions in order to maintain strategic influence in any environment. It is not about self-control for its own sake. It is about learning to bend the decisions of others through calibrated presence, psychological leverage, and subtle dominance.’”

“Bend the decisions of others through psychological leverage? So… a bunch of con artists, basically.”

“Sounds like,” Alice agrees, skimming the page. “God – this is nuts. Listen to this: ‘Others are a system to be run,’” she reads. “‘People are not mysteries; they are systems of reaction, insecurity, and desire. Sovereigns learn to read these systems and reprogram them in real time. Energetic Sovereignty trains individuals not just to lead, but to own the psychological space around them – to shape loyalties and make obedience feel like alignment.’” She makes a disgusted face. “Gross.”

“Well, I can see why politicians and tech bros would be into this. ‘People are systems’?” Rio drums her fingers on the steering wheel. “Okay, so Agatha’s raised in this, she practices on her schoolmates, and then eventually she kills her mother – why? Because they were vying for power? She wanted to take over?”

“Well, it does seem like the job came with some perks.”

“Yeah. Cult leaders usually target people on the fringes – managing to get a bunch of wealthy powerful people to join up is kind of brilliant, actually. So, okay, let's say she killed her mom and took control of the cult. Why all the other murders?”

Alice shrugs. “Insufficient loyalty, maybe? She killed her mom but they haven’t accepted her leadership, so she’s getting rid of them?”

“Yeah,” Rio says, chewing on her lip. “Maybe.”

“You don’t like it.”

“I don’t know. All their wealth and power isn’t much good to her if they’re dead. And the cult’s whole thing is manipulation, not violence.” Those things are both true, but they’re not getting at what’s bugging Rio. It takes her a moment to put it into words. “It’s not business, you know? It’s pleasure. She’s enjoying herself.”

The way Agatha had disguised herself as Agnes; the taunting letter she’d left behind. Her playfulness at the warehouse: Oh, we are going to have fun together.

Rio grips the steering wheel harder. She can feel Alice gazing at her, but she keeps her eyes firmly on the road.

“Are you okay?” Alice asks eventually.

“Oh my god,” Rio says. “You’ve got to stop asking me that. I’m fine.”

“Yeah, so you keep saying.”

She can’t tell Alice the whole truth. She can’t tell anyone the whole truth. But the question is there, the one she can’t stop asking, and it pushes itself up and out of her mouth before she can find a way to stop it.

“What is it about me?” she asks. “I mean, she must have seen something. Something that made her choose me, decide that I was the one she was going to—”

“No, god, Rio, no – she didn’t see anything in you. There’s nothing wrong with you, okay? You were just the person unlucky enough to cross her path.”

The problem is, unlucky isn’t the word Rio would use. Agatha’s presence doesn’t feel unlucky. It feels… inevitable. It feels like being caught in the pull of an object with its own gravitational field.

“Yeah,” she says finally. “You’re probably right.”

The drive home after she drops Alice off passes in a blur of streetlights and silence. By the time she pulls into her own driveway the sun has started to set, painting her small house in shades of amber and gold that feel too warm and peaceful for the storm she’s carrying in her chest.

She shuts off the car and sits there, listening to the quiet tick of the engine as it cools, staring at the shadows stretching across her front porch. Her gaze travels over her flowerbeds, left wild and untamed to encourage bees and other pollinators. She’d planted purple milkweed and white coneflower, lavender, orange calendula, all of them tiny bursts of color against the dying light. The cardinal flowers and bee balm are so strikingly red in the glow of sunset that their petals seem to be licked by flame, vivid and violent.

She forces herself out of the car and up the front steps. As soon as she steps inside she drops her bag and coat on the floor, closing the door behind her and leaning back against it.

“I need a drink,” she says out loud to no one. She pushes away from the door and kicks her shoes off, padding into the kitchen. Her pour is generous, nearly filling the glass, and she lifts it up and stares into the blood-red wine.

She didn’t see anything in you.

Rio knows that Alice meant the words to be reassuring. “She didn’t see anything in me,” she says, trying the feel of them in her mouth, but hearing it aloud again just makes it worse.

Fuck – what is wrong with her? Who the fuck wants to catch the attention of a serial killer?

But she can’t stop replaying it in her mind: the moment she’d given in to her, the way Agatha bit her lip and groaned. The sound of Rio’s heartbeat thudding in her ears, darkness closing in around her. That feeling of being pulled under. That feeling of wanting it.

Rio takes a shaking breath in, hands suddenly trembling. She tries to put her wine glass down on the kitchen counter, but she moves too fast, and the glass crashes into the granite countertop. She hisses as it shatters, sending glass and wine cascading down her cabinets, trickling toward her bare feet in dark rivulets.

She reaches down without thinking, jerking her hand back as a shard bites deep into her thumb. She tastes iron and salt as she brings it to her lips.

In the dim light filtering through her kitchen window, she lifts her hand and examines the cut. The edges of the wound are sharp, neat, blood oozing out of it like sap from a tree. She stares at it for a long moment, and then she presses her fingers against the edges of the cut, digging her nails in, drawing the pain up sharp and bright.

She presses harder, gritting her teeth, watching a drop of blood trace a winding path down her wrist to soak into the bright white of her sleeve.

She thinks of Agatha's fingers at her throat. The way her heart had pounded for her, eager and shameless.

The blood spreads across the fabric of her shirt like a flower in bloom.

Good, she thinks.

Let it stain.

Chapter 4

The marker squeaks against the whiteboard as Rio adds another arrow connecting Porter's murder to all the others they’ve learned about. She steps back, examining the web of connections she's drawn – victim profiles, timeline, locations – trying to see the pattern that will lead them to Agatha. The fluorescent lights hum overhead, casting everything in harsh white light.

She flexes her left hand, the bandage on her thumb pulling tight. Three days since she'd cleaned up the wine glass. Three days of forcing herself to think like an FBI agent instead of… whatever the fuck she’d been thinking before.

“Alright,” she says, taking a step back. “I think this is a good start.”

Jen eyes the whiteboard. “Well, it definitely looks like the sort of thing a serial killer would make, so you’ve got that going for you.”

Rio caps the marker with more force than necessary and sets it down on the ledge of the whiteboard. “Thanks for the feedback. Okay, so Alice, you’re going to keep looking for a link between the prior victims and the Energetic Sovereigns. Connections to Evanora Harkness, connections to Agatha, connections to each other. Bonus points if we can find any former members willing to talk to us.”

“I’ll keep at it,” Alice says from behind her computer screen.

“Jen—”

“Yeah, yeah, AirB&B, I got it.”

“Let’s see if we can link the rental to any bank accounts, and maybe we can trace those to Agatha. And let’s double check whether Porter’s wife or anyone from his staff recall seeing her before his death.”

Jen raises an eyebrow. "You want me to ask if they remember seeing the woman who pretended to be a detective on the case?”

Rio feels heat crawl up her neck. "Yes, Jen. I want you to ask."

“Okay, you do realize any witness accounts we get are going to be completely compromised, right? She was there for days. She questioned the wife. How are we supposed to separate what they might have seen before from what they definitely saw—”

"Because that's our job," Rio says, her voice sharper than she intends. "Yes, she inserted herself into the investigation. Yes, it complicates things. But we still have to follow every lead, even the long shots."

Jen gives a long-suffering sigh. “Fine.”

"Thank you." Rio turns back to the board, trying to ignore the way Alice is studiously avoiding eye contact. “Look, Agatha might use aliases, but there’s no way she’s left no trace of herself over 25 years. She’s not some hermit living off the grid – she wears nice clothes, she’s got jewelry, she’s getting haircuts.” Her phone buzzes in her pocket, and she pulls it out as she talks. “There are breadcrumbs out there, and we’re going to find them. So let’s find them.”

She unlocks her phone while the others begin gathering their things.

 

Unknown Number: Quick question.

Unknown Number: If I asked you to dinner, would you arrest me when I got there?

 

A wave of ice washes over Rio, followed immediately by a surge of heat. Her grip tightens on the phone as she stares at the words, reading them twice, three times. Her heart hammers against her ribs.

“Hey, we still on for lunch later?” Alice asks from the doorway.

“Huh?” Rio’s head snaps up. “Oh. Yeah.” She plasters a smile on her face and slips her phone back in her pocket. She manages to keep it together until she’s back in her office, and then she closes the door and leans back against it, pulling her phone out again.

She could just ignore it. Delete it. March into Lilia's office right now and tell her everything – about the warehouse, about what happened, about the way Agatha had made her feel like she was drowning in something darker than water.

But even as the thoughts form, she knows she won't. Because buried beneath the panic and the ringing of all of her professional alarm bells is another feeling entirely: relief.

Agatha is reaching out.

Agatha wants to see her again.

God, she tells herself, you are so fucked up.

But she can't pass up the opportunity to make this connection. To talk to her, to find out what she wants. What she's planning. Rio is the lead on this case – it's her responsibility to pursue every avenue, even the dangerous ones. Especially the dangerous ones.

It’s her job.

She tries not to think about the way her pulse quickens at the thought of seeing those blue eyes again as she types out her reply.

 

Rio: only one way to find out

 

She doesn’t have to wait long for a response.

 

Agatha: I never thought I’d say this, but you might actually be TOO into handcuffs, sweetheart.

 

Rio takes a breath. She needs to be careful. She can’t just roll over and fawn at Agatha’s feet, but if she goes too far in the other direction and acts completely disinterested, Agatha might shut down.

Or not. Maybe she likes a woman who can give as good as she gets.

 

Rio: how did you get my number?

Agatha: What can I say? I’m a woman of many talents.

Rio: yeah? and here i thought your only talent was murder

Agatha: Aw – you think I’m talented at murder? :)

 

Rio rolls her eyes. Christ.

 

Rio: are you in DC?

Agatha: I could be. If you said yes to dinner.

Rio: so you’re nearby?

Agatha: So many questions!

Agatha: I’ve got one for you.

Rio: no

Agatha: Come on. It’s important.

Rio: ugh

Rio: fine. what

Agatha: What are you wearing?

 

Rio barks a laugh before she can catch herself. She pushes off the door behind her and crosses over to her desk, dropping down into her chair.

 

Rio: wouldn’t you like to know

Agatha: I really would.

Agatha: You could even send pictures.

 

Rio’s mind flashes to Agnes, the image she’d conjured of her, hunched over a phone in the dark. If Agnes had been real – if they’d stayed in touch—

Okay. No. Hard line in the sand: Rio is not going to start sexting the serial killer she’s supposed to be hunting. Not even to try and draw her out.

 

Rio: i thought that was agnes’s thing

Agatha: You do know I’m her, right? We’re not actually two different people.

Rio: how about you tell me where you are, and then we can talk about pictures

Agatha: Yeah… somehow I don’t feel like that’s a real offer, Agent.

 

Fuck. Rio needs to give her something real, something that will keep her engaged. Not nudes, but—

 

Rio: okay, fine

Rio: dinner. real offer.

Agatha: Right.

Rio: i’m serious

Rio: i have questions for you

Rio: no arrests

Rio: scout’s honor

 

Rio waits. And waits. A minute goes by, and then two, but there’s no response.

 

Rio: hello?

 

Nothing. Rio puts the phone down on her desk and leans back in her chair, staring up at the ceiling. Okay, well. So much for that plan.

She jumps, startled, when her phone buzzes again.

 

Agatha: Alright. See you soon, sweetheart.

 

Rio grabs for the phone, nearly dropping it in her haste to reply.

 

Rio: wait

Rio: when do you want to meet?

Rio: where?

Rio: agatha??

 

Silence.

She flops back in her chair again, letting the phone clatter onto her desk.

“Perfect.”

 

 

x

 

 

Rio props her feet up on her coffee table that night, and takes another sip of wine as she flips through the report Alice had compiled about the Energetic Sovereignty movement. The lamp beside her casts a warm circle of light, just enough to read by.

Several distinct features set cults apart from mainstream religious or social groups. These include authoritarian leadership, isolation, manipulative recruitment, strict control, an us-vs-them mentality, exploitation, and psychological manipulation. Although there is limited public information regarding the Energetic Sovereigns, the evidence indicates that the group exhibited many of these characteristics. In particular, there are strong indications of targeted recruitment, isolation and secrecy, an us-vs-them philosophy, and psychological manipulation directed both within and outside the group. It is also likely that Evanora Harkness was an authoritarian-style leader of the organization.

Rio puts her wine glass down and glances up as she flips to the next page.

Agatha Harkness is standing in the doorway of her living room.

“What the fuck?” Rio yelps, scrambling backward off the couch, backing up until she hits the wall behind her.

Agatha smiles and waggles her fingers in a wave. “Hi, baby.”

“What the fuck are you doing here?” Rio spits. Her eyes dart around, heart pounding: cell phone on the coffee table, Agatha blocking the path to the front door. Kitchen to the left, back door through there. Dead-bolted shut, but she could probably make it.

“You invited me, remember?” Agatha says innocently, stepping further into the room, moving with the same predatory grace Rio recognizes from the warehouse. “Dinner?”

“I didn’t – Jesus, I didn’t invite you to my house. The entire FBI is looking for you.”

“Yeah? Well, I’m betting they won’t look here.” Agatha gives her a mischievous wink, but Rio can see her looking around, taking inventory, assessing the room in the same way Rio just did.

Rio blinks a few times, trying to calm her breathing. She's acutely aware, suddenly, of the fact that she's in yoga pants and a ratty FBI Academy t-shirt while a serial killer stands in her living room in jeans, a casual button down, and a smile like poisoned honey.

She looks good. Fuck.

Rio follows Agatha’s eyes to the coffee table. Wine glass, a plate with cheese and—

They react at the same time, but Rio’s reflexes are faster. She dives across the room and grabs the knife before Agatha can get to it, and then she holds it out, the blade glinting in Agatha’s direction.

“Don’t move.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “Or what, you’re going to stab me with some shitty steak knife you got on sale at Wal-Mart? Come on, sweetheart. That is not how I die.”

Rio fumbles for her phone with her free hand, backing away again until her hip hits a bookshelf, rattling her flower pots. She dials 9-1-1, finger hovering over the call button, but instead of pressing it she glances back up at Agatha.

At Agatha, who notices her hesitation – because of course she does – and looks Rio up and down with knowing eyes. Her bearing seems to shift, her body relaxing, head tilted, mouth suddenly a perfect pout.

“Admit it,” she says softly, and she takes a small step toward Rio. “You’re happy to see me. Isn’t this every FBI agent’s dream? To play cat and mouse with someone like me?”

“I don’t think you can call it ‘cat and mouse’ when the mouse just keeps following the cat around,” Rio says flatly, and Agatha grins.

“Aw, it’s cute you think you’re the cat.” Agatha holds up her hands as Rio tightens her grip on the knife. “Kidding! I’m kidding.”

She takes another slow step toward Rio, hands still raised, biting her lip provocatively.

“Come on. Have dinner with me. Just dinner.”

Rio huffs out a breath. “I don’t think there’s such a thing as just anything with you.”

Agatha lifts an eyebrow, and then her look goes lewd. “Fair enough. I haven’t ruled out dessert.”

“Just – stop,” Rio snaps. “Sit down.” She gestures with the knife toward the couch.

And to her surprise, Agatha does. She gives an easy shrug and settles onto the seat, chin raised. “Alright, fine. I’m sitting. Now what?”

Now what, indeed. The silence stretches between them as Rio tries to think of what to do or say next. She can smell Agatha's perfume again, something dark and earthy and expensive that curls around Rio's senses.

“What do you want?” she asks finally.

“I told you, I want to have dinner with you.” Agatha sits back, fingers trailing along the arm of the couch – Rio's couch, in Rio's house, like she belongs here. “I don’t know why you think I’m lying.”

“Right. You’re one of those honest murderers we hear so much about.”

Agatha gives her a disapproving look. “I would have brought food, but I figured you wouldn’t trust it. We can order, or—”

“I’m not having dinner with you after you broke into my house.”

“Yes,” Agatha says, her tone growing a little annoyed. “You are.”

“Why would I do that?”

“Because you can’t get enough of me,” Agatha says, shrugging with a flourish. “Come on. Sit down. You can hold onto your little knife if you want.”

Now that the adrenaline rush is starting to wear off, Rio’s not all that worried that Agatha’s going to hurt her. Not in a head-on attack, anyway; that’s not her style. But she can’t bring herself to sit down across from her like any of this is normal.

Agatha narrows her eyes a little when Rio doesn’t move. And then, slowly, she bites her lip and smiles.

So that can’t be good.

“Or maybe it’s not me you can’t get enough of,” Agatha says. “You miss Agnes, is that it? You want me to be her?”

Before Rio can respond Agatha flips her hair at the nape of her neck so it looks like it’s in a low ponytail, and at the same time she changes her posture, loosening up a little, relaxing back into the couch and spreading her legs wide. She gives Rio an easy smile. It’s subtle, but the transformation is swift and effective: suddenly Rio is staring at Agnes.

“I missed you too,” Agnes-as-Agatha drawls.

Rio swallows. “Don’t.”

Agatha’s smile slowly shifts from Agnes’s lazy grin into something more like a smirk, and then she shrugs, shaking her head until her hair falls in waves around her shoulders again.

“I still can’t believe ‘asshole cop’ is your thing.”

“Oh – as opposed to asshole serial killer?”

“Well, that’s reductive,” Agatha says. “You don’t even know me.”

Rio stares at her – cheekbones catching shadows thrown by the dim light, full lips, magnetic gaze, the face of a woman who’s entirely at home in the darkness. Finally, slowly, Rio lowers her knife. After a moment she crosses back to the couch and sits down on the opposite side from Agatha.

“I know you,” she says.

“Oh?”

“Agatha Harkness. Born July 23, 1973, in Salem, Massachusetts. Numerous aliases. Graduated high school in 1991. No college degree. Never married, no children.”

“Wow,” Agatha says dryly. “You should write my Wikipedia entry.”

“Father, unknown. Mother, Evanora Harkness,” Rio continues, making note of the way Agatha tenses almost imperceptibly at the mention of her mother. “Evanora was the leader of the Energetic Sovereigns, a cult that promised to teach its members how to manipulate any situation for their own gain. She was murdered via cyanide poisoning in what was originally believed to be a mass suicide event in 1995.”

“And it was so tragic,” Agatha says, placing a dramatic hand over her heart.

“Your mother raised you to be a con artist, and then you killed her in an attempt to take over the cult she founded. You’ve spent the last twenty-five years systematically murdering powerful people – former or current members of the cult, presumably. You exhibit traits of psychopathy and narcissism. You show contempt for authority, you’re self-centered, you’re vain, and you’re exceptionally smart. You use poison because it’s clean and fast and it lets you feel like you’re in control, and your mother never let you feel like you were in control of anything.”

Agatha’s staring at her with a glare so sharp it could cut glass by the time Rio stops talking. Her mouth slowly curls into a snarling smile.

“Well, then,” she says. “I guess you’ve got me all figured out.”

“Am I wrong?”

Agatha just raises her eyebrows disdainfully. Rio shrugs and sits back.

“Explain it to me, then.”

Agatha stares at her for a long moment, and then blinks and clears her throat. “Rio Vidal,” she says. “Born June 26, 1984. Two older siblings. Twins. Parents still alive, still married, still living in Wilmington, Delaware.” Agatha lifts a corner of her mouth as Rio’s heart starts to pound. “Graduated high school in 2002, college in 2006, Quantico 2008. Unmarried, no children.” Agatha glances around. “And no cat? I really expected a cat.”

The muscles around Rio’s mouth have started to tremble. She can see the moment Agatha notices.

“So you know how to Google,” Rio says in a thin voice.

“I just figured I ought to get to know you, too, since you’re obviously obsessed with me.”

“I’m doing my job.”

“Sure,” Agatha says. “And you wanted to meet because you have more questions for me, right? For your job?”

Rio’s jaw flexes as she grits her teeth. She does have questions – questions Agatha’s not likely to answer once she’s arrested. But the mention of Rio’s family has shaken her up more than it should have. Rio’s not surprised that Agatha tried to rattle her, but she’s surprised at how well it worked.

“What is it you want to know?” Agatha continues, as though she’s prompting Rio. “Why I do it?”

Rio runs her still-healing thumb over the point of the blade, remembering the bright, clarifying pain of the glass shard.

“Yes,” she says finally. “For a start.”

“I take the power from the undeserving,” Agatha says simply. “Next question.”

“What does that mean?”

Agatha sighs. “These people are idiots. All that power, and they use it to… what, get rich?” she asks scornfully. “Get laid? I mean, that’s the best they can do?”

“What should they be doing?” Rio asks.

The sound of carnival music mixed with horror movie sound effects drifts from the indoor course, punctuated by the occasional shriek of delighted laughter from other patrons.
