It's ridiculous and over the top and exactly the kind of distraction Rio needs.

“Hi,” comes a voice behind her, and Rio turns around to find Wanda standing there, looking effortlessly put together in dark jeans and a mustard-colored sweater, a cozy scarf wrapped around her neck. “Rio?”

“Yeah,” Rio says. “Wanda? Hi.”

They spend an awkward moment trying to decide whether to shake hands or hug, both of them shifting their weight. Finally Wanda pulls Rio in for a quick hug.

“Okay,” Wanda says, grinning as she pulls away. “So we got the weird introduction part out of the way.”

“Perfect. Now we can skip straight to the part where I embarrass myself at this,” Rio says, glancing over at the golf course.

They stare at each other for a beat too long, smiling, and Rio uses the opportunity to take Wanda in. She has a way of holding herself that’s composed, self-assured, open; Rio wonders if she looks like a brick wall in comparison.

“Well… shall we?” Wanda asks finally, and Rio nods.

“Yeah, for sure. After you.”

 

 

It only takes two holes for them to realize they’re both really, really bad at mini-golf.

"Well, I guess I don't have to worry that I missed my calling," Rio says as her fourteenth shot bounces off the side of a mummy’s foot and rolls even farther from the hole than where it started.

“Depends,” Wanda says, eyebrows raised in amusement as she traces the path of Rio’s ball. “What if your calling is being impressively terrible at mini-golf?”

“Oh, well in that case – I mean, not to brag, but I’ve actually been awful at this since I was a child.”

“Ah, so you’ve put the work in,” Wanda says as she lines up her own shot. “Have you considered going pro?”

“Don’t get me wrong, I’ve thought about it,” Rio says. “But I worry that the fame would go to my head, you know?”

Wanda lines up her shot, sticking her tongue out in concentration. She taps the ball, which immediately gets stuck under a plastic spider.

“Well, every great athlete needs a rival,” she laughs. She tries to dislodge her ball with the putter, and after some prodding she finally manages to pop it free. They both watch as it rolls into a water hazard.

They stare down into the mucky greenish water, and then at one another.

“Drinks?” Rio asks.

“Yes, please.”

 

 

Ten minutes later Rio’s settled on a barstool, a Vampire’s Blood cocktail in hand and Wanda’s knee pressing gently against hers.

“To surviving that disaster,” Wanda says, lifting a glass of something alarmingly green that the menu had called Frankenstein’s Monster.

“Barely,” Rio replies, clinking their glasses together.

They both sip their drinks, Wanda settles back in her stool. “So, you work with Jen. How do you like the whole FBI thing?”

“Uh – yeah, I love it,” Rio nods. “I get to do a little bit of everything, which is nice. White collar cases, organized crime, trafficking, murder…”

“Sounds intense.”

“Sometimes. There’s a lot of paperwork, too.”

“You working on anything cool now? Or is that classified?”

Rio laughs. “Well, I don’t know about cool, but right now we’re looking for a serial killer, actually.”

“What – around here?” Wanda asks, looking alarmed. “Do I need to be worried?”

“No. You’re fine,” Rio assures her, but even as she says the words her stomach gives an uncomfortable twist. Does Wanda need to be worried? Agatha killed Sharon Davis for talking to Rio – but that was because she was talking about her, about Agatha. Her childhood, her family, the cult. That was about control. Wanda shouldn’t even be on her radar.

Unless this is putting her there.

“Hm,” Wanda says. She looks thoughtful as she takes another sip of her drink. Rio tries to shove away her anxiety and bring herself back to the conversation.

“What?”

“I was just thinking, it must be hard seeing the worst of people all the time. Dealing with—” She waves her hand, gesturing around at the sinister decor. “You know. Actual monsters.”

Rio licks her lips, thinking about Agatha’s smirk, her mother. The little heart-shaped earrings she wore in her middle-school yearbook photo. “It would be easier if they were monsters, actually,” she says after a moment. “But they’re just… people.”

“People who kill other people.”

“Well, yeah. Fucked up people. But that’s what makes them interesting.”

Wanda raises an eyebrow. “Interesting?”

“Well, I mean – intellectually.” Rio shakes her head. “Like, what makes a serial killer tick? They don’t commit crimes of passion. They have a plan. They're strategic. There’s an… elegance to it.”

“Yeah,” Wanda says slowly. “I guess.”

“They have to be smart. It’s like…” Rio pauses, searching for the right words. “It’s like a chess match, you know? They’re always three moves ahead, and so you’ve got to figure out how to be a move ahead of that.”

Wanda nods, taking another sip of her drink.

“And there’s this, I don’t know… freedom,” Rio continues, not quite able to stop herself. She remembers the bite of metal on her wrists, the feeling of Agatha’s hands twisted in her hair. You don’t have to pretend with me, baby. “They take what they want when they want it. The only boundaries they have are the ones they choose. It's kind of enviable, when you think about it.”

Silence stretches between them, broken only by the ambient horror movie soundtrack and the distant sounds of other players. Wanda is looking at Rio like she's seeing her for the first time, and not necessarily in a good way.

“That’s…” Wanda clears her throat. “An unusual way to think about murderers.”

Rio blinks, hearing her own words echo in her head, seeing them reflected in Wanda's expression. Elegant. Enviable. Jesus Christ, what is wrong with her?

“I mean,” Rio says quickly, heat flooding her cheeks. “Obviously, it’s terrible. Murder is terrible. I'm not – I don't think it’s good. I just meant... from an academic standpoint…”

But Wanda is still looking at her with those searching green eyes, and Rio can practically see her mind churning: Finds serial killers fascinating. Thinks there’s freedom in not having boundaries. Fuck. Rio might as well have worn an entire outfit made of red flags to this date.

“You know what,” she says. “Let’s forget I said that. I think I’ve been working too much lately. It’s making me weird.”

Wanda lifts a corner of her mouth as she sets her drink down, turning it by the rim. “Jen mentioned you were kind of intense about work.”

Well, intense is better than total fucking weirdo, anyway. Rio can work with intense. “Yeah. Sorry. I hang out with so many agents that it’s easy to forget that Serial killers are my passion probably isn’t a great first date conversation.”

Wanda grins and leans forward slightly, close enough that Rio catches a hint of her perfume. “Alright, well, what else are you passionate about, Agent Vidal? Besides the criminal mind?”

There's a spark of flirtation in Wanda's eyes, a deliberate attempt to salvage the moment, and Rio gives her a grateful smile.

“Other than my budding golf career, you mean?”

“Obviously.”

“Well, right now I’m pretty interested in this cute girl I just met. Tell me about you. How’d you get into interior decorating?”

“Well,” Wanda says, “I went to art school and graduated with a degree in art history, which is famously known for its many lucrative career options.”

“I’ve heard that, yes.”

Wanda smiles. “I don’t know. I guess I’ve always been interested in the way design influences reaction and response. Every room tells you something about the person who lives there, but it also shapes who they become when they're in it. There’s something powerful in that. Or something… beautiful, I guess.” She scrunches up her nose. “Oh, god. That sounded so pretentious, didn’t it?”

“No,” Rio laughs. “It sounded really cool, actually. Shit – should I have gone to art school?”

“I don’t know. How do you feel about having a useless degree and a ridiculous amount of student loan debt?”

“I mean, I was a history major, so…”

“Oh. So – good.”

“Yeah, apparently.”

“Hang on,” Wanda says, laughing. “Let me just—” She reaches over and straightens Rio's collar, biting her lip as she runs her fingertips along the fabric. “This color looks really good on you.”

It's such an easy, normal gesture. Wanda's touch is light, her smile genuine. She's beautiful and funny and clearly trying to flirt despite Rio's earlier weirdness. Everything about this should be sending sparks through Rio. But it isn’t.

There’s just no tension in it, is the problem. Rio doesn’t have to wonder whether Wanda will be gentle or rough, playful or possessive. She’s looking at Rio with affection, but affection is so… straightforward. Rio’s gotten used to being looked at like a puzzle to solve. Like something worth conquering.

Like prey.

Oh, get the fuck over yourself, she chides. This is a smart, gorgeous woman who likes you. Even after you just acted like a psychopath, she’s smiling and flirting. Just… be fucking normal.

“That’s quite the compliment, coming from an art school graduate,” Rio says.

“Oh, it is,” Wanda says, smiling as she leans in.

The kiss is sweet, soft. Wanda’s hands rest on Rio’s hips, and she moves slowly, tilting her head, sliding her tongue gently against Rio’s. It's everything a first kiss should be – inviting, exploratory, full of promise. But Rio finds herself analyzing it even as it's happening, cataloguing the gentleness instead of losing herself in it. It's nothing like kissing Agatha, that feeling of claiming and being claimed, of being devoured. Wanda kisses like she's being careful not to overwhelm Rio, and Rio has to resist the urge to deepen the kiss, to bite, to turn it into something consuming.

It's a nice kiss. It’s the kind of kiss that used to leave her breathless and yearning.

So what the fuck is wrong with you?

Rio should want this. She wants to want this. But sitting here with Wanda’s lips pressed to hers, all she can think about is the difference between want and need, between being desired and being craved.

Wanda is smiling when they pull apart. She brushes her fingers across her lips and clears her throat.

“Well. I don’t think I’ve ever made out with anyone to a horror movie soundtrack before.”

“No?” Rio asks, flashing her a smile. “In my book that’s peak romance.”

“I’ll keep that in mind for next time.” Wanda pauses. “Not – that I’m assuming—”

“No, assume away,” Rio says easily.

It’s fine. She can make this work. After all, the whole point is to find someone who’s not Agatha – someone who offers more than lust and risk and the thrill of doing something she shouldn’t. And Wanda ticks every box: kind, beautiful. Appropriate. She’s smart, has a job, has hobbies that presumably don’t involve killing people. She deserves a chance.

Focused, sane, and normal: that’s what matters. Rio’ll figure out the rest.

“So… can I call you?” she asks.

Wanda’s smile is a sunrise.

“You better.”

 

 

x

 

 

Rio returns home resolute.

There are dishes in the sink that need washing, and so she plunges her hands into the hot water and doesn’t look twice at the glint of the wine glasses in her peripheral vision. Her plants need watering, and so she walks around with her copper watering can, murmuring to each of them, checking their leaves for growth. She keeps her back to the mirror.

She smiles when her phone buzzes in her pocket, already thinking of flirty replies and plans she might suggest.

 

Agatha: Did you have fun?

 

Rio stares down at the screen, heart suddenly thudding against her ribcage.

 

Agatha: She’s cute, I guess, if you’re into the whole generic girl-next-door thing.

Agatha: Personally, I think you could do better.

 

Of course she was there at that stupid mini-golf course. Rio can imagine her lurking around in the shadows, sipping a drink in the corner. Watching her play with Wanda, flirt with her. Watching them kiss.

She inhales a panicked breath and blinks, trying to clear her vision.

Don’t hurt her, she wants to type. If you fucking hurt her, I’ll…

She’ll what?

Rio’s got no leverage. She’s in too deep to turn Agatha in at this point – too many texts, too many lies. There are witnesses, maybe, or… god knows what kind of evidence Agatha’s kept in her back pocket.

If you hurt her, I’ll…

There’s only one thing she has that Agatha wants.

She closes her eyes and takes a long breath. And then she slips her phone back into her pocket and turns back to her plants.

Her phone buzzes again. And again. She stands still, gripping the watering can.

After the third buzz she rips it back out of her pocket and swipes it open.

 

Agatha: Oh, you’re ignoring me?

Agatha: I’d be careful, if I were you, sweetheart.

Agatha: I bet Blondie wouldn’t ignore me.

 

Rio snarls down at the screen.

 

Rio: what do you want??

Agatha: Oh – you’re alive after all. I was starting to worry.

Rio: what the fuck do you want

Agatha: You seem upset, baby. What’s wrong?

 

Rio shakes her head incredulously, typing.

 

Rio: are you serious??????

Rio: you killed sharon davis

Agatha: Who?

 

It takes everything in Rio’s power not to throw her phone across the room.

 

Agatha: Oh – the teacher?

Rio: yes, agatha. the teacher

Agatha: So? Aren’t murders like… job security for you? I thought you’d be happy.

Rio: you did not think i’d be happy

Rio: you were trying to warn us off the case

Agatha: Well, then it sounds like the woman died for a noble cause.

 

Rio slides down onto her couch.

 

Rio: i’m done

Agatha: Done with what?

Rio: this. all of it.

Agatha: Wow.

Agatha: Blondie must be quite the kisser.

Agatha: And it looked so dull from where I was standing. I could practically see you counting down the seconds until it was over.

 

Her stomach clenches.

 

Rio: fuck off

Agatha: Hey. Be nice.

Agatha: I have a present for you.

Rio: i don’t want it

Rio: i don’t want anything from you

Agatha: Come on. It’s a good one.

Rio: okay maybe i’m not making myself clear

Rio: leave me the FUCK ALONE agatha

Rio: i am DONE

Agatha: Well, it’s already on your front porch, so take it or leave it, I guess.

Agatha: But if I were you, I’d take it.

 

 

This time Rio really does throw her phone. She chucks it onto the couch with a frustrated growl, and it bounces off the cushions and onto the carpet where it gives another faint buzz. Rio can just make out the text.

 

Agatha: Don’t be so dramatic.

 

“Oh my god.”

Rio picks up her phone and sets it on the coffee table face down. She closes her eyes and takes a steadying breath, and then she reaches for the remote and switches on the TV.

She keeps her eyes glued to the screen. No more texts come through, but she can feel Agatha’s presence like something physical prowling around outside. A shadow; a wraith; the wolf in the wood.

She tries not to care, but the not-knowing is like an itch. It’s a twist in her stomach, a restless twitch in her legs. I have a present for you.

“Probably a severed head,” she mutters to herself. “Or a dead dog. Fucking psychopath.”

She shifts around so her legs are tucked beneath her. Shifts again so they’re stretched out, feet resting on the coffee table. She tries to watch whatever’s on the TV, some vapid reality show, two women screaming at each other about a man.

A mindless minute goes by. Then another.

“Fuck’s sake,” she huffs finally, shutting off the TV as she pulls herself to her feet.

Everything looks the same as it always does when she opens her front door. No sign of anyone, not a leaf in her garden disturbed. But there, centered on her welcome mat, is a package wrapped in brown paper.

Rio picks it up, flips Agatha off – she figures she’s still out there somewhere, watching – and closes the door behind her.

The package is sleek and rectangular, small enough to hold comfortably in both hands, but heavier than Rio would have expected given its size. She examines it from all angles before slipping a fingernail beneath the tape holding the paper together, pulling it off and letting it flutter to the floor.

Inside is a wooden box, held closed with a silver clasp. Its small hinges creak in protest as Rio opens it.

Every girl needs at least one, a card inside the box reads.

Beneath the card is an ornate knife. Curved steel blade, a rich, deep green handle threaded through with delicate gold accents. Rio stares at it for a moment before slowly lifting it out of the box.

It fits her palm like she was born to it. The weight is balanced and solid, the grip nestling perfectly into her hand. She’s handled knives before, trained on tactical knife work in the field, but those were functional, inelegant things. This is something else. She holds this knife and feels like she’s grown claws.

Her phone buzzes on the coffee table, but Rio doesn’t even glance toward it. Instead she looks up, finding her reflection in the large mirror across the room.

Her hair is loose around her shoulders, eyes dark. She lifts the point of the knife gently to her mouth, pressing the cool steel to her lips. She has the urge to run her tongue along the blade, to bite it. For a moment she is the person Agatha must think she sees when she looks at her: dangerous, beautiful, transformed.

And then she blinks.

Focused, Rio. Sane. Normal.

She drops the knife back in its box like it's an animal that stung her.

And then she snaps the lid closed.

Chapter 6

Rio takes a seat across from Alice’s desk. It’s a wreck as always, strewn with scraps of paper, candy wrappers, chewed pen caps and notes scribbled in her indecipherable shorthand. But it looks even more chaotic than usual today. Like a little stress-bomb has gone off.

In contrast to all the chaos around her, though, Alice looks subdued as she flips through the autopsy photos in Sharon Davis’s file.

“You called it,” she says mechanically, handing Rio the report. “The ME found ferrocyanide salts in her tissue, same as Porter.”

“Of course he did,” Jen says, collapsing down into the chair next to Rio. “We knew it had to be Harkness.”

Rio lifts her eyebrows. “What happened to ‘We have to entertain the idea it was a heart attack’?”

“It’s called keeping an open mind.”

Rio glances down at the autopsy pictures, then immediately looks away from them. Seeing Sharon Davis in the morgue had been bad enough; Rio doesn’t need to see her cut open, sewn up.

A week ago she’d stood in the back of a funeral home, listening to Sharon's sister give a tearful eulogy. She always said there was no such thing as bad kids. Only kids who need more love.

She wonders if Sharon would want to revise that little theory, given the circumstances.

“There’s no forensic evidence at the scene to tie it to Agatha,” Alice says. “But obviously….”

“Obviously.” Jen leans back in her chair, tapping her pen against her notepad. “I mean, it’s an escalation. Definitely not her usual victim profile.”

“She’s fucking with us,” Rio says. “I told you, she’s sending a message. This is a game to her. She thinks she’s untouchable.”

“Or maybe Sharon Davis knew more than she was letting on,” Jen says. “She could have had more information about the cult. Maybe Agatha killed her to shut her up?”

“I don’t think she knew anything else – that wasn’t really the vibe I got. What did you think, Alice?”

“Does it matter?” Alice asks. “Either way, we led Agatha right to her.”

Rio recognizes the ache in her voice. Hollow resignation, a numb sort of apathy – it’s the same tone her own inner monologue uses every time she thinks about Sharon Davis. Suddenly Alice’s stress-bomb of a desk makes a little more sense.

“Hey,” Jen says as Rio’s still trying to figure out a way to respond. “Look at me. You are not cursed.”

“I go on one interview and the woman ends up dead,” Alice says. “What would you call it?”

“Bad luck,” Jen replies.

Or bad company, Rio thinks. Alice has no reason to feel guilty – Rio’s the one who let Agatha go, who took no precautions, who served Sharon Davis up on a silver platter. The only reason Alice was even there was because Rio hadn’t been able to trust herself after the warehouse. She’d dragged Alice to the interview without even considering what it might mean to involve her.

Yet another name on the rapidly growing list of people Rio’s managed to fail.

“This is my fault,” Rio says, and somehow the heavens don’t split open under the weight of the understatement. “You’re not cursed – I should’ve seen it coming, and I didn’t. This is on me, not you.”

“Well, aren’t you two quite the pair,” Jen says. “Look – it happened. Now we know she’s more of a psycho than we thought. But this whole guilt thing is not productive.”

Alice gives a resigned shrug. “It’s a little productive.” She pulls something up on her laptop and turns it around to show them. The screen is filled with photographs – three middle-aged faces, two men and a woman. “I’ve been digging into the other victims from the Energetic Sovereignty murders. The three who died alongside Evanora Harkness.”

Alice clicks a button, and the photos change. Younger faces – professional headshots, LinkedIn profile pictures. “They had seven children between them. Adults now, obviously. And three of them have died of what looked like heart attacks over the past decade.”

Rio stares at the pictures, unblinking. More of Agatha's work, methodical and patient. A slow culling that no one had bothered to connect until now.

“That leaves four,” Alice says. “I don’t know what the other murders have been about – she obviously hasn’t limited herself to these seven. I’m still looking for connections. But the four who’re left seem like obvious targets.”

She clicks through the profiles she’s compiled. “James Sanders, banking exec here in DC. Lucy Dunn and David Kumar, both Silicon Valley. And this guy…” A black-and-white photo appears, grainy and blurred – a news clipping about a winning college basketball team. “Robert Mills. He’s like a hermit or something – basically no digital footprint. This was the only picture I could find. Last seen in upstate New York.”

“Security?” Rio asks.

“Sanders, Dunn, and Kumar, for sure. Private details, personal drivers, gated communities, threat monitoring—”

“Gee, almost like they know someone’s hunting them for sport,” Jen says wryly.

“And Mills has just gone off the grid,” Alice says. “Which is its own kind of security.”

Rio leans forward, a question starting to form, but a knock sounds behind her.

“Agent Vidal?” The young agent in the doorway peers inside. “There’s someone asking for you downstairs at the front desk.” She glances down at a notepad she’s carrying. “A Wanda Maximoff?”

The mood in the room shifts immediately, Alice and Jen’s attention snapping to her like rubber bands.

“Oh really?” Jen asks, grinning. “Visiting you at work?”

“She’s just dropping something off,” Rio says, already pushing herself up from her chair.

“Yeah?” Alice asks, looking perkier than she has all day. “Something you left at her place?”

“Oh my god, it’s my sunglasses. It’s not like I left my bra behind.”

The other two climb out of their chairs, trailing Rio as she leaves the office. She glances behind her.

“I can make it to the front desk without an escort.”

“Hey, I knew her before she ever saw your bra,” Jen says. “It would be rude not to say hello.”

“Uh-huh. And what’s your excuse?” she asks Alice.

“Oh, I just want to see her,” Alice says with a shrug. She blinks innocently in response to the look Rio gives her. “What? I do.”

They head toward the elevators, teasing Rio as they walk, and Rio smiles, laughs, rolls her eyes good-naturedly. The truth is, things with Wanda have been… good. Better than good, really. In the two weeks since the knife appeared on her doorstep – in the two weeks since she’d stopped responding to Agatha’s texts entirely – she and Wanda had settled into an easy pattern. A handful of dinners, a few sleepovers. The conversation is great, the sex is excellent. Rio’s got no complaints.

Except – well, it’s not that it’s boring, exactly. Wanda’s too smart for Rio to be bored, too confident, too sexy. She’s the sort of woman Rio would have fallen all over herself about, before.

It’s just that it’s a little bit… exhausting. There’s a performance quality to all their interactions, like Rio’s playing the role of someone good enough to date a woman like Wanda. To be honest, she’s always felt like this in relationships – like she was putting on a show, trying to present herself as just the right combination of cool but not aloof, interested but not clingy. But before Agatha, she’d never felt like it was work to keep her thoughts focused, her reactions normal. Now she’s had a taste of something else, this way that Agatha has of looking at her that’s terrifying and electric and dangerous and vital. She’s a constant thrum beneath her skin, a tension between her shoulder blades. Rio keeps dreaming about her. About the glint of knives, about Sharon Davis’ blank gaze. About hands around her throat. She keeps waking up in a sweat, half-hoping and half-dreading that she’ll find Agatha standing in the shadows of her bedroom.

She’s changed the locks on her house, scoured every room for cameras. She’s been drawing the shades every evening so Agatha can’t peer inside. She keeps looking over her shoulder to see if she’s being followed.

In the face of all that, it takes effort to play the part of the ordinary, uncomplicated woman that Wanda deserves.

The elevator dings, and they step into the lobby to find Wanda waiting near the security desk. She lights up when she sees Rio.

“Wow,” Wanda says, crossing over to them, her emerald sweater and dazzling smile vivid against the backdrop of people walking around in dull black suits. “I didn’t realize I’d get a whole welcome party.”

“We couldn’t resist,” Jen says. “It’s good to see you, Wanda! How is everything?”

“Everything’s good,” Wanda says, glancing toward Rio with warm eyes. “This one’s been keeping me entertained, so I guess I have you to thank for that.”

“Eh, well, I figured you could do worse than Vidal.”

Rio raises her eyebrows. “High praise from Jenny Kale,” she says. “And this is Alice.”

“I’ve heard so much about you,” Alice says, shaking Wanda’s hand.

“She’s heard a normal amount about you,” Rio corrects.

“Right,” Alice agrees happily. “That’s what I meant. I’ve heard such a normal amount about you.”

Wanda laughs. “Same, I think? It’s nice to finally put a face to the name.” She smiles at Rio, then reaches over and pulls her into a quick hug. “Hi.”

“Hi. How’s your day going?”

“Oh, you know. One client meeting down, one to go. Oh – before I forget…” She rummages around in her bag, fishing out a pair of sunglasses and handing them to Rio.

“Thanks,” she says, flashing an I told you so look in Jen and Alice’s direction. “You really didn’t have to come all the way here just for this.”

“And leave those gorgeous brown eyes defenseless against the sun?” Wanda teases. “It’s fine, it was on my way.”

“Well. I appreciate it.”

“Of course.” She tilts her head, smile playing at the corner of her lips. “But since I did come all this way... any chance I could lure you out for a lunch date?”

“Ah, the ulterior motive reveals itself,” Rio says, and Wanda laughs. “I wish I could but I’m pretty buried right now. I think I’m gonna have to eat at my desk.”

Wanda glances around the building, wrinkling her nose. “Well, I hope your office is nicer than this. Tell me you have a window, at least.”

“Yeah. I’ve got plants and everything.”

“Of course you do,” Wanda laughs. “Okay, I’ll let you go back to saving the world. Call me later?”

“Definitely.”

Wanda hesitates, and then she leans in. “Can I kiss you goodbye, or is that not FBI-appropriate?” she asks in a conspiratorial voice.

The memory of Agatha's mouth crashes over Rio – demanding, consuming, nothing like the sparkling question in Wanda’s eyes.

She pushes the thought away and drops into a stage whisper. “I think we could probably get away with it.”

Wanda's kiss is soft and sweet, entirely appropriate for a federal building. When she pulls away, she’s smiling.

“Bye.”

“Bye.”

“Okay,” Jen announces as they watch Wanda leave. “I obviously made a huge mistake. You two are so cute it's disgusting.”

Alice nods. "Absolutely revolting.”

“Shut up,” Rio laughs. She skates her fingertips over her lips. This is good, she reminds herself. This is normal. This is what she wants.

This can be enough. With a little more work, she can make this enough.

 

 

x

 

 

The next day, everything kicks into overdrive.

Alice greets her at the office door, bouncing on her heels, excitable as a puppy. “We got a hit on one of her aliases.”

“Mm.” Rio hurriedly swallows her coffee. “Shit. Tell me everything.”

The details spill out in a rush as they walk to Rio’s office. Astrid Hark – one of about ten different aliases Alice has been tracking – has registered for tomorrow night’s gala for the Hartwell Foundation.

“What does the Hartwell Foundation do?” Rio asks, dropping her coat and briefcase and settling into her desk chair.

Alice follows her in. “They help fund cancer research. But I don’t think that’s why she’s going.”

“Oh? You don’t think our suspect has a charitable disposition?”

“Apparently it’s the social event of the season.” Alice grins. “And James Sanders is on the guest list. One of the Sovereign Seven, in the flesh.”

“Really.” Rio leans back in her chair, staring up at the ceiling. “Okay, then.”

Agatha's not an idiot. If she's using an alias they've flagged, it's because she wants them to know she'll be there. It’s been two weeks of silence on Rio’s part, two weeks of ignoring her, of shutting her out literally and figuratively. So of course Agatha’s escalating. Of course she’s trying to force Rio's hand.

Rio’s stomach gives a painful twist at the thought of what will happen once they catch her. At everything that will come to light when the FBI starts poring through her communications. If Agatha goes down, she’s almost certainly taking Rio down with her.

But what’s her other option? Stand by while Agatha murders someone else? Stare down into the face of another victim in the morgue, dream about their eyes every night?

She made bad choices. They might come back to haunt her. But she’s decided who she is now, and so that’s who she’s going to be.

“Right,” she says, sitting up. “Okay, I’ll reach out to Sanders’ security team, let them know there’s a threat to his life. We can put someone on him, too. Hopefully he’ll just… stay home, hunker down until we catch her.”

“What if he doesn’t?”

Rio sighs. “Then… the Bureau better let me expense a new dress.”

 

 

“Check check check,” Rio says.

“All good.” Rio hears the words twice – once live from Alice sitting across from her in the small surveillance van, and again through the earpiece nestled into her ear.

“Great,” Rio says. “Cameras up?”

“Entrances, exits, and everything in between. We’ll have eyes on her the whole time.” Alice spins around in her chair to review the many screens laid out in front of her. It’s nice to see her like this, in her element, decisive and self-assured. Her guilt about Sharon Davis seems to have transformed into a grim determination to bring Agatha down. She hadn’t even hesitated when Rio had told her she needed her in the field.

“I want to know the second she shows up.” Rio pulls open the van door and steps out, straightening her suit and shaking out her hair. She’d spent way too long looking for a dress she thought she could run and jump and shoot in before finally settling on something menswear-inspired. Pants had yet to fail her.

“On it, boss,” Alice says, punching some buttons on the complex control panel in front of her.

“Jen, do you copy?” Rio asks as she walks into the gala. The Great Hall of the National Building Museum is gorgeous – massive ceilings, soaring Corinthian columns, walls made up of a long series of arches on either side. All of it is alight in dramatic blues and purples. It’s like walking into some sort of nebula.

With way too many shadows, she thinks, glancing around.

“Copy,” comes Jen’s voice through the earpiece.

“How’s our guy?”

“Oh, you know. Schmoozing.”

Jen sounds as disdainful as Rio feels. They’d reached out to Sanders, informed him that they had reason to believe his life was in danger. In response, he’d told them – well, his lawyer had told them – that he’d never heard of Agatha Harkness. And he wasn’t going to miss the gala because some “nut job” had it out for him.

This charity is very close to Mr. Sanders’ heart, the lawyer had said. And his security team is more than capable of protecting him. But we thank you for your concern.

Rio didn’t like it, but there wasn’t much she could do if Sanders was refusing help. She’d assigned Jen to monitor him and intervene if his security failed; other than that, she just had to hope that they’d get to Agatha before Agatha got to him.

Her stomach flutters at the thought. She usually feels some tense combination of nerves and excitement at the beginning of every operation, but tonight she feels like she’s practically vibrating. By the end of the night, Agatha Harkness is going to be in handcuffs. It’ll be the highlight of Rio’s career, the sort of work that leads to recognition, promotions, awards. Or it would, if it wasn’t almost guaranteed to completely destroy her.

But she can’t think about that right now.

“How much do you think you have to donate to get invited to a party like this?” Alice asks through the comms.

“Tickets were a grand, and tables were between five and fifteen,” Rio says.

“Thousand dollars?” Alice sputters. “Holy shit. Where’s Harkness getting all this money?”

Rio scans the crowd as she answers. “Stolen from her mother? Being a cult leader’s a pretty lucrative gig even when your cult’s not made up of a bunch of rich people. The woman must have been loaded.”

“God,” Jen says. “Can you imagine having all the money in the world, you can do whatever you want, live wherever you want, spend all your time on a beach somewhere, and instead you just go around killing people for fun?”

“Well, everyone’s got hobbies,” Rio says, and Jen snorts.

“That’s not exactly—”

“Guys?” Alice interrupts. “She’s here.”

Rio swivels around, heart leaping into her throat. “Okay,” she says. “I’ve got Agatha; Jen, do not take your eyes off Sanders. Alice, confirm uniforms at every exit.”

“Confirmed. She’s sealed in. She’s not getting out of here.”

“Alright,” Rio says, swallowing hard. “Let’s do this.”

She keeps her eyes glued to the entrance. A long minute passes. And then another.

“Where is she?” she asks. “Alice, I’m not seeing her. I need you to get eyes on her, she’s—”

And then Agatha walks in.

Rio's focus telescopes until there's nothing in the room other than Agatha, who steps forward, looking around. She’s wearing a long black dress with a low-cut V, sleek and form-fitting. Her hair is half up, long strands brushing her shoulders, framing her face. Her lips are a perfect pout, kohled eyes sparkling under the colored lights.

“Never mind,” Rio says. “I’ve got her.”

Rio circles the crowd slowly, taking the long way around, watching Agatha from afar. She doesn’t want to spook her – or worse, give her the chance to start saying god-knows-what with Jen and Alice both listening in. So she keeps her distance, trying to blend in, keeping to the edges of the crowd.

Agatha stands still for a moment, scanning the room like a queen observing her subjects. Rio takes a step back into the protective shadow of one of the wall’s many arches. She licks her lips and the haughty look on Agatha’s face, dangerous and brilliant and completely unrepentant.

“Be ready, Jen,” she murmurs. “I think she’s looking for your guy.”

But when she moves again, it’s away from Sanders, and toward the open bar. Alice makes a frustrated sound.

“Just go arrest her now,” she says.

“There are hundreds of people here and we don’t know what she’ll do if she feels cornered,” Rio says, moving in closer. “We’ve gotta be patient.”

Agatha joins the end of the long line, taking her place behind a woman in a long silver gown. Rio watches her stand in line at the bar, studying the way Agatha holds herself. The tilt of her head, the casual scan of the room – reading everyone around her, making subtle adjustments to how she holds herself depending on whose eye she happens to catch.

And watching her do it is... fascinating. Rio gets it now, why Agatha might enjoy watching someone from afar. At this distance, she can see all of it – the little manipulations, the calculated charm in her smile. It's like watching a master class in human behavior, every gesture intentional and calibrated.

Agatha’s attention settles on the woman in front of her in line. She looks her up and down with predatory focus, and then she leans forward, murmuring something into her ear.

The woman turns around with a smile, and Agatha says something that makes them both laugh. She puts her hand on the woman’s arm.

“Who is that? Do you think they know each other?” Alice asks.

“Doubt it,” Rio says in a dry voice. She hopes it covers the twinge of jealousy she’s feeling at the sight of Agatha’s slender fingers resting against another woman’s skin. “She makes fast friends.”

Drinks in hand, Agatha and the woman start making their way through the crowd, toward a group of people who greet them both warmly.

“What’s Sanders’ 20?” Rio asks.

“Still on the other side of the room,” Alice reports. “She doesn’t even seem to be looking for him.”

“Well, we know she has something planned,” Rio says. “She’s not here for the wine.”

Rio jumps as a loud metallic shriek breaks the air, followed by the amplified sound of someone clearing their throat.

“Good evening, ladies and gentlemen,” a bespectacled man in a tux announces from the stage. The main lights begin to fade, and a spotlight comes up, focused on him. “We’re going to go ahead and get started, if you’ll take your seats.”

The crowd begins to shift, moving toward the tables.

“Fuck,” Rio murmurs. The room’s massive columns cast long, deep shadows over the room in the dimming light, and the glare of the spotlight turns the crowd into silhouettes. Rio starts to push her way through mass of people, trying to keep Agatha in her sights.

“Let’s have a round of applause for the incredible turnout tonight!” the man says, and everyone breaks into appreciative applause.

“Guys,” Rio says, a warning in her tone. “Check in.”

“Sanders is at his table,” Jen says. “He’s got a security guy with him.”

“Alice? Do you have her?”

“I’m tracking the group. They’re all moving together, but I can’t make out individuals in this light.”

“Me either,” Rio says, pushing past a group of women who’d seemingly decided on ‘hideous feathers’ as the theme for their outfits.

“Wait – did you lose her?” Jen asks. “Are you kidding me?”

“I’m on her,” Rio snaps. “It’s dark as fuck in here, Kale.”

“Oh my god.”

“Focus on your own guy,” Rio says as she reaches Agatha’s group and scans them quickly.

No Agatha.

Of course, no fucking Agatha.

Despite everything – Sanders in danger, the entire operation going sideways – Rio finds herself shaking her head slowly, chuckling. Agatha had timed it perfectly, used the chaos. Elegant.

She pushes her way toward the woman who’d been in line with Agatha at the bar. “The woman you were talking to,” she asks. “Where did she go?”

“Oh, uh…” The woman glances around. “I don’t know. She wasn’t with us.”

“But did you see where she went?”

“Her own table?” she says with a vague shrug, then turns back to the speaker.

“She’s not at her table,” Alice reports.

Rio turns and scans the room. The walls are nothing but shadow, but Rio knows that about half of the arches that run the length of the room are framing recessed doors. Twenty-five of them, at least. Agatha could have ducked away anywhere.

Where would I go? she thinks, mind buzzing. What would I do?

“Okay, I’m gonna do a lap and start checking doors. Jen, do not let Sanders move until we’ve located her. Sit on his lap if you have to. Alice, keep scanning the area. And ask them to turn up the fucking lights.”

Rio heads to the east wall and starts trying doors.

“She could’ve gone into the back hallways,” Alice says.

“I know, but this is closer to Sanders,” Rio says, checking a door, finding it locked. “I’ll head there next.”

“She could be doing anything. She could sneak into the kitchen and poison his food.”

“We put a uniform on the kitchen,” Jen reminds her.

Rio throws open a door. Office, dark and empty.

“She could get past an officer, though, right?” Alice asks. Her voice sounds a little more high-pitched than usual. “She could charm him, or—”

“They’re all on high alert for her. It’s gonna be fine,” Rio says.

“We should have put cameras in the back, too.”

“Yeah, well, limited resources,” Rio says, jiggling a door handle a little too hard.

“I know, but—”

“Alice,” Rio interrupts. “We’re doing our best. Did you ask them about turning up the lights?”

There’s a brief pause.

“I’m gonna go check the back halls,” Alice says.

“What?” Rio asks. “No – you’re the only one with eyes on the whole place. Stay in the van and deal with the lights.”

“Let Rio handle it, Alice,” Jen says.

“No,” Alice says, voice grim and determined. “Agatha Harkness is not killing anyone tonight. Not if I can help it.”

“Alice, do not leave your post. That is an order.” Rio pauses, waiting for a response. “Alice?” she asks when one doesn’t come. “Do you copy?”

“I’m, uh… guessing she left her post,” Jen says.

“Goddamn it. Does she even have a weapon?”

“I don’t think so. You want me to—”

“No.” Rio closes her eyes and takes a deep breath. “Stay on Sanders. I’ll go put her back in the van.”

The crowd has disappeared now that most people have taken their seats. Rio makes her way across the massive space, nearly the size of a football field, and heads for the door leading to the back halls. She pushes through, heading toward the kitchens.

“Did Agent Wu-Gulliver come through here?” she asks the officer posted by the swinging doors. Through the porthole windows, she can see the catering team preparing to serve dinner to several hundred wealthy donors.

“No, ma’am.”

“Alright – if she comes by, stop her. I’m looking for her.”

She doubles back and takes her next right, heading toward the exit nearest the van. Maybe Alice hadn’t had time to make it to the kitchens yet.

“We don’t have time for this shit,” she mutters to herself, taking long strides as she rounds a corner. She nearly trips over Alice’s dead body.

Her heart drops through the floor.

“Oh fuck,” she stammers. “Fuck.”

“What’s up?” Jen asks.

Rio’s blood is ice in her veins. “Oh god—” She drops to the ground and rolls Alice over. “Alice?” she asks, shaking her. “Alice.”

“Rio, what’s happening?” Jen asks.

“Alice—”

“Is she down?”

“She – yes,” Rio says. “But I don’t see any sign of trauma, or—”

“Is she breathing?”

An image of Sharon Davis flashes across Rio’s vision, grey-skinned, mouth agape. She closes her eyes and shakes her head, trying to focus her thoughts.

“Rio. Check her pulse.”

She reaches her hand out, hovering over Alice’s neck, but she can’t bring herself to do it. If Alice is dead – if Agatha killed her—

“Talk to me, Rio.”

Please.

Please, please, please.

She presses her fingers to Alice’s carotid. Warm blood thuds beneath her fingertips.

Rio inhales sharply, momentarily lightheaded with relief. She leans down, putting her ear close to Alice’s mouth. “She’s breathing. She’s unconscious, but she’s—”

Jen rounds the corner behind her. Rio blinks up at her.

“He has his own security,” Jen says in a voice that dares Rio to tell her to leave. The words echo in Rio’s earpiece, and she rips it out.

“Stay with her,” she snarls.

She tears down the hallway, turning one corner, then another, slamming doors open as she goes. Where is she? Where the fuck is she? Another corner, then another, checking door after door. And then she spots one that’s slightly ajar.

She pushes on it, heart pounding, but as it starts to swing open something inside her shifts. Her rage and terror is still there, hot as flame, but underneath it is that familiar electricity. She’s here.

The room looks like a storage area, dim and lined with shelves. And there, at its center, stands Agatha.

Rio’s training kicks in, and she nearly shouts for backup, nearly bounds forward to cuff her and haul her out in front of everyone. But she doesn’t. She knows she’s falling into the same trap she keeps falling into, but she can’t find the will to pass up this moment – just the two of them, no Jen listening in, no Alice monitoring cameras. Just this: the chase narrowed down to its essence. Hunter and prey together in a quiet room.

Rio steps inside closes the door behind her.

“What the fuck is wrong with you?” she spits.

“Well, hello to you, too, darling,” Agatha says with a sweet smile.

“What did you do to her?”

“Wow, I saw you from across the room, but this outfit is even better up close,” Agatha says, taking a small step toward her. “You should stop wearing shirts under your suits at work, too.”

“Agatha, I swear to god—”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “She’ll be fine,” she says. “I sprayed her with an aerosolized anesthetic. She might wake up with a headache, but it won’t cause any permanent damage.”

“Aerosolized anesthetic?”

“Yes, chemistry is amazing and I’m brilliant. Is that really what you want to talk about?” Agatha bites her lower lip. “How’ve you been?”

She planned all of this, Rio knows. The alias, the timing, getting Rio here alone. But Rio glances around, swiftly taking in the room. There’s no door but the one Rio entered through. All the exits in the building are covered. Agatha’s not getting away.

“What’s the plan here, exactly? You use an alias that you know we know, you’re practically baiting us to show up here, you attack an agent on the scene – are you trying to get caught?”

“Depends on who’s doing the catching,” Agatha says with a wink, but then she shakes her head. “Not everything is about you, sweet pea. Lots of things are! But not everything.”

“What does that mean?”

“Did you like your knife?” Agatha asks smoothly, as though Rio might not notice she’s changing the subject. “You know, you never texted me back. Not even to say thank you – which was rude, frankly. But I suppose you’ve been busy with Blondie, hm?” She tilts her head. “How’s that going?”

“Why are you trying to kill James Sanders?” Rio demands.

“I don’t know who that is.”

“Bullshit.”

Agatha laughs. “I like you like this. All business. Interrogate me harder, baby,” she says in a teasing voice.

“Would you rather talk back at headquarters?”

“Oh, I don’t think you’d like how that would go,” Agatha says lightly. “There are so many stories I could tell about you.”

“Tell as many stories as you like,” Rio says. “I’m done. This is done.”

Agatha opens her mouth to say something, then closes it again. She studies Rio for a moment with a thoughtful expression.

“You look tired.”

“I look hot,” Rio counters, and Agatha laughs.

“Mmm,” she agrees, looking her up and down appreciatively. “But isn’t it exhausting? All the work you have to do to make yourself palatable for them?”

There it is again, Agatha’s uncanny ability to see things in Rio that no one should be able to see.

“If I look tired,” Rio says, “it’s probably because I’m spending all my time chasing a fucking serial killer. But I’m thinking I’ll sleep pretty well tonight.”

“What, in a cell?” Agatha shakes her head, frustrated. “You’re not like them, Rio. All these small, ordinary people you surround yourself with. I don’t know why you keep pretending you are.”

Rio gives her a condescending smile. “You don’t know me nearly as well as you think you do.”

“I know you down to your bones,” Agatha retorts. “I’m the only one who actually sees you.”

Rio stares at her. At the confidence in her posture, the intensity in her eyes. It’s overwhelming, being this close to her – Rio has to stop herself from letting her eyes linger on the dip and rise of her collarbone, the soft swell of her cleavage, her skin and her perfect mouth and the gentle curl of hair brushing against her shoulders.

I’m the only one who actually sees you.

The words should feel wrong, but they don’t. Everyone who looks at Rio sees the version of herself that she presents: competent, controlled. But somehow Agatha sees down to the restless hunger beneath it.

Rio is careful to sound unfazed when she speaks again. “You realize that sounds crazy, right? Like… weirdo-stalker crazy?”

“Oh, and you’re – what? Sane?” Agatha asks, lifting an eyebrow. “Sane people don’t let serial killers fuck them in their living room, honey.”

Rio’s jaw flexes. “That was a mistake.”

Agatha just looks amused. “Okay. Pretty good mistake.”

“I’m done.”

Agatha makes a production of clearing her throat and putting on a serious face. “Right. Of course,” she says. “I respect your decision.”

“For fuck’s sake—”

“What? Look, if your idea of a good time is having mediocre sex with some perky blonde while you try not to think of me, more power to you.”

Rio glares at her. “She’s a redhead, actually.”

“I cannot express to you how much I do not care,” Agatha says with a tight smile. “The point is: I’m not wrong.”

“Yeah. You are.”

Agatha takes a few steps forward, closing the distance between them. “Am I?” she asks. “When you touch yourself, do you think about her?”

Rio swallows. She starts to step away, but Agatha grabs her hips, pulling her close. “No,” she continues. “You don’t. You think about me. You think about my mouth. My tongue. The way it feels when my fingers slide inside you…” She wraps a hand in Rio’s hair and pulls her close, lips against her ear. “You think about riding me until you scream, don’t you? About getting on your knees for me. About all the ways I absolutely fucking ruin you.”

Rio’s breath shakes as Agatha’s hip presses into hers, fingernails digging into her scalp. There’s a sharp, perfect ache between her legs, so deep it feels like need.

“But,” Agatha says brightly, suddenly releasing Rio from her grasp, “I’m sure Blondie’s fine too.”

She leans back, looking smug.

Rio manages to huff a small laugh. “Please. You think I’m that desperate?”

“I think you’re someone who knows what she wants,” Agatha says. “And you’re waiting for someone to tell you that you can have it.”

She hates that it’s true, but Rio does think about Agatha. Does touch herself thinking about those blue eyes, that dangerous smile. She feels more alive in these moments than she has in years. Maybe ever. If it were just the sex, all of this would be so much easier, but it's not. It’s all of it. The thrill of her, the risk, the chase, the intoxicating push and pull. The feeling of being seen. Chaos and honesty, truth and ruin, all wrapped up in one devastatingly gorgeous woman.

She takes a long breath in. “Agatha Harkness, you’re under arrest for the murder of Sharon Davis.”

“Oh god – this again?” Agatha says, rolling her eyes. “I swear, you’re like the girl who cried handcuffs.”

“You have the right to remain silent.”

“Yeah, not really known for that.” Agatha sighs. “Look, I keep telling you, sweetheart, you don’t have to pretend with me. We both know you’re not ready for this to end. If you arrest me now, we both go to prison. What’s the fun in that? But if you let me go… we get to keep playing.”

“You mean you keep killing people.”

“Well, a chase with no stakes isn’t much of a chase.”

“I’ve chased you here,” Rio says with a bland smile. “End of the line, Agatha.”

“God,” Agatha says, clicking her tongue. “You really are so cute when you think you’ve won. It almost makes me want to let you win.”

“Okay. Turn around and put your hands behind your—”

Agatha’s hand darts up and sprays something directly into her face.

Rio jerks backward, coughing and sputtering, but it’s too late. The darkness is already coming for her, velvet dark and enveloping.

“It’s okay, I get it,” Agatha says as Rio presses the palms of her hands against her stinging eyes. “You’re not ready to admit it yet. You need me to fight harder for you. I can do that.”

“No, I…” Rio trails off. The last words she remembers sound too close and very far away at the same time.

“We’re not done, sweetheart. We belong to one another.”

“How are you feeling?” Lilia asks.

“Fine.”

“Liar,” Alice says from the bed next to her. “Your hands are shaking.”

Rio glances down. Alice is right – they are. Her head feels like someone took steel wool to the inside of her skull. Her mouth tastes like she licked a battery, and the antiseptic smell permeating the hospital room makes her want to vomit. Every thought has to wade through mud to reach the surface.

And none of it matters.

Agatha got away.

“Yeah, okay, I feel like shit,” she says. “When can they discharge me?”

“They’re keeping you both overnight for observation. Ah-ah—” Lilia lifts a hand to stop Rio’s protest. “I don’t want to hear it. You’re where you’re supposed to be.”

Rio flops back onto the pillows, wincing as she pays for her little tantrum with a horrible throb in her head.

“I’m not,” Alice says.

“You’re not what?” Jen asks from the chair beside her.

“Where I’m supposed to be.” She takes a shaking breath, looking over at Rio, tears glittering in her eyes. “This is my fault. I ruined the operation. I should have listened – I should have known—”

“Hey,” Rio says, but Alice is still talking.

“—that everything I touch turns to shit. James Sanders is dead because of me.”

The words hit Rio like a physical blow. All their planning, all their surveillance, and Sanders had died anyway while she was unconscious on a storage room floor.

“James Sanders is dead because of Agatha Harkness,” Lilia says firmly. “You disobeyed a direct order, and we will deal with that. But you are not responsible for the man’s death.”

“But we would have caught her—”

“We weren’t expecting her to spray us with fucking – whatever the fuck this was,” Rio says. “You’re the one who’s going to be able to tell us what we’re dealing with.”

“We’re going to catch her,” Jen says, taking Alice’s hand and threading their fingers together. “But we need you. Okay?”

Alice gives a half-hearted shrug, closing her eyes and lying back against the pillows. Another tear slips down her cheek.

Shit.

“Lilia,” Rio says.

You’ve got to take me off this case.

The words catch in her throat before she can say them out loud. It’s the right thing to do, to insist on it. She’s compromised; things have gone way too far. She was making a move to arrest Agatha, yes, but the truth is, even she isn’t sure she would have gone through with it in the end.

Lilia reads her expression, and seems to understand some version of what Rio can’t find the words to say.

“It’s been a rough night,” she says. “But you can do this, kid.”

I can’t, Rio thinks. I really don’t think I can. But what can she say? ‘Actually, Agatha and I are locked in some sort of psychosexual power struggle, and I’m pretty sure I’m losing’?

Another person is dead on her watch. Alice is a mess. She should walk away. End this, let someone else take the reins.

But how is she supposed to do that? Hand Agatha off to the next agent, let someone else chase her? Would Agatha even let that happen? Would she act out, escalate? Or would she move on and start stalking whoever took Rio’s place?

The thought causes a savage jealousy to flare inside her so strong she nearly bares her teeth. Agatha, pressing someone else into a wall. Giving someone else that cruel smile. Leaving marks on another person’s skin.

No. This is her hunt. We belong to one another.

She glances down again. Her hands are steady.

“Yeah,” she says to Lilia. “Don’t worry about it. I’ve got this.”

Agatha Harkness is mine.

Chapter 7

The tent stake goes into the ground on the second thump of the mallet.

Rio moves to the next corner and lines up another stake, her swing easy. Wanda hums under her breath as she unpacks their cooler on the picnic table. The campsite is dusted with pine needles that cushion Rio’s knees; the air is crisp with the smell of woodsmoke and river water. The early October sun warms her shoulders as she works.

She takes a long breath as she stands up, stretching extravagantly. She's always felt more settled in the woods, just trees and sky and the work of making camp. There’s no tension coiled in her spine, no tightness in her jaw. She’s been carrying anxiety inside her like a second skeleton for so long that it almost feels like she’s floating now that it’s gone.

She heads back to Wanda’s hatchback, which is open and spilling out camping supplies. “How do I inflate this?” she calls, pulling out a folded air mattress. “Is there a bicycle pump or something?”

“Nah. It’s got a thing you plug into the USB port in the car,” Wanda answers as she sorts their snacks.

Rio lifts her eyebrows. “Okay, your tent is the size of a castle, and now your air mattress has wifi? This is officially the fanciest camping trip I’ve ever been on.”

Wanda grins. “Welcome to adulthood, babe. We sleep in style.”

Rio laughs. That feels easy, too.

She spreads the mattress on the ground and plugs in the pump. It whirrs to life, drowning out the chirping of birds around her.

It’s been three weeks. Three weeks since the gala, three weeks since Rio had sat in that sterile hospital bed staring down at her hands. Three weeks of terrible sleep, of chain-smoking on her back porch at 2 AM, sitting with the mess of her own mind and staring at the knife Agatha had left her until the green vines seemed to thread into her vision.

And somewhere, in all that quiet and all that noise, something had settled. Not an answer, really, but something simpler, something that feels almost radical in how uncomplicated it is.

I want this.

Not Agatha, exactly, but… this. This feeling of being alive. The truth of her own hunger. The parts of herself she’s been trying to starve.

She doesn’t know exactly what it means. She doesn’t have a plan; when she thinks of the future, everything is sort of hazy, out of focus. All she knows is that as soon as she let herself think the thought – I want this – her frenzied mind finally went still. There’s been a war inside her for months, ever since the moment Agatha appeared in that warehouse and wrapped herself around Rio with both hands. She struggled, clawed, she fought and she hasn’t stopped fighting. But she understands, finally, that there’s only one way forward. That there only ever was.

So she’s dropping her hands to her sides; she’s letting her lungs burn. Drowning as freedom.

It feels incredible.

“Need help?” Wanda calls from the picnic table as Rio hauls the inflated mattress into the tent.

“I got it,” Rio says. She emerges to find Wanda just outside, holding two bottles of beer.

“To the great outdoors,” she says, offering one to her. Rio takes it with a smile and taps their bottles together.

“Thanks for coming with me,” Wanda says. She nudges Rio’s shoulder with hers. “I’m glad we’re doing this.”

“Me too.” Rio takes a sip of her beer and looks out over the river. The water is swift and rippling, but she can see the glint of small fish in the calmer eddies near the bank. Their campsite is tucked into a clearing, surrounded by old-growth pines. She closes her eyes and inhales deeply.

Her eyes flutter back open as she realizes Wanda’s watching her.

“What?”

“Nothing. You just… you look happy.”

Rio laughs. “As opposed to how miserable I normally look?”

“No. Not miserable.” Wanda threads her arm around Rio’s waist and rests her head on her shoulder. “I don’t know.”

Rio takes another sip of her drink. They both know what Wanda’s not saying. She’d been deeply freaked out about the whole Rio-being-attacked-by-a-serial-killer thing, which – fair. It’s not like Rio could explain that she didn’t think Agatha would actually hurt her.

She was the younger sister; her siblings were twins, and her childhood was basically one long attempt at trying to work her way into their impenetrable fortress of a relationship. Her sister didn’t look at her with a smile very often – her sister didn’t look at her very often, period. It’s a nice memory.)

“That’s Ana?” Agatha asks.

Right, of course Agatha knows her sister’s name. “Yeah.”

“None,” Rio says.

Agatha raises her eyebrows. “Really? What are you, like the only cop in America who hasn’t murdered someone for looking at you the wrong way?”

“Right,” Rio says slowly. It makes sense, except—

“Okay, but – they’re not the only ones you’ve killed, though.”

Rio pushes herself up to sitting, scrunching back against the headboard. She shouldn’t be surprised anymore at the way Agatha can talk so nonchalantly about executing people, but it’s still uncomfortable. “Those are – those people aren’t trying to kill you. Agatha’s laugh is dry as desert air. “None of them are innocent, honey.”

“So…” Rio worries her lower lip with her teeth. “Okay, then what changed? Broke the détente?”

Agatha grins and runs a playful hand up Rio’s leg. “Ooh, speak more French to me, baby.”

“Agatha.”

She lets her hand drop and rolls onto her back. “Bobby Mills,” she says, with genuine loathing in her voice.

“Bobby… you mean Robert Mills? The hermit guy?”

“I wish he was a fucking hermit,” Agatha says. “He was diagnosed with cancer a few years ago. And I guess he’s decided that the only thing he wants before he shuffles off this mortal coil is to see me dead.” She shakes her head, frustrated. “You know, all of this used to be easier. Get a few fake passports, set up some shell companies, open bank accounts overseas. It took actual legwork to track someone down. But now, thanks to your police state, suddenly there are cameras everywhere, facial recognition, digital financial tracking. Fucking AI, now? You can’t escape it.”

“Right. Okay,” Rio says. She doesn’t want to get pulled into some rant about all the ways modern tech has upended the halcyon days of serial killing. “So Mills found you.”

“He always was a weasel. He had this little ferret face – whatever. Yeah. He burned a bunch of my identities, started emptying my accounts. Honestly, I didn’t think he had it in him. Rio stares down at Agatha, trying to fit all the pieces together. Agatha was feeling trapped, running low on resources, looking for another way out. A new plan. She could have been long gone, but she stuck around Porter’s investigation for days, insinuating herself into the case, endearing herself to Rio. Leaving enough clues behind that she’d inevitably get caught. There’s no way that was an accident.

An uneasy thought seeps into Rio’s mind. It suffuses her chest, creeps down her spine, pools cold as ice in her stomach.

“Agatha,” she says slowly. “Did you know who I was before we met?”

“Hm?” Agatha asks. “What do you mean?”

“I mean – was I just the agent who happened to run across you, or did you already know who I was?”

“God, I wish I’d known you earlier,” Agatha says, smirking as she looks Rio up and down. “Think of all the fun we could have been having.”

“Answer me,” Rio says, heart pounding. “If you didn’t know who I was, then say so. ‘No, I didn’t know you.’”

Agatha stares at her with those sparkling blue eyes, deep and impenetrable as the sea.

“The FBI agent who’s got a thing for female serial killers?” she says finally. “Of course I knew who you were.”

Rio sits frozen in place for the span of a breath. And then she pushes herself up and out of bed, powered by something primal, some bone-deep dread that wants her to put as much space between her body and Agatha’s as she can.

“Get out,” she says, standing with her back to the wall.

Agatha sits up, giving her an exasperated look. “Come back to bed, sweetheart. Let’s talk about this.”

“Don’t – do not call me sweetheart,” Rio spits. “Get out.”

“Okay, where is this coming from?” Agatha asks. “You must have known—”

“That you were spying on me? No, I did not fucking know that.”

“I wasn’t spying on you,” Agatha says patiently. “I had a short list of agents who I thought would be good candidates—”

“Oh my god.”

“—and you were on it. I knew killing Porter would draw someone from your unit, so I took a chance. And it worked.”

“And you thought, oh, good, I’ll just seduce this idiot and all my problems will go away?”

“Oh, come on – I wouldn’t have chosen you if I thought you were an idiot,” Agatha says. “And does it look like all my problems have gone away?”

“Yes, Agatha, because I’ve been fucking you instead of arresting you! That seems like a pretty big fucking problem has been solved for you. Oh my god,” Rio groans, pressing the palms of her hands into her eyes so hard that she can see starbursts behind her eyelids. “I am such a fucking idiot. Fuck.”

She startles as Agatha’s hands wrap around her wrists, gently lowering her hands. “No, you’re not. You’re exceptional,” Agatha says softly.

Rio rips her arms out of her grip with a growl.

“You are,” Agatha insists. “Look, I’m as surprised as you are – I mean, who falls for an FBI agent? It’s embarrassing. No offense.”

“Stop,” Rio spits. “Stop lying to me.”

Agatha flinches back, almost imperceptibly. “I’m not.”

“Bullshit. That’s all you do – that’s what you were raised to do,” Rio says venomously. “You really are your mother’s daughter, aren’t you?”

Agatha takes a step back, blinking. Rio wants to slap the wounded look off her face.

“I—” Agatha begins, but she can’t seem find the words that come next. She trails off. Closes her mouth.

And then she turns and walks back over to the bed. She sits down, staring at her hands in her lap. There’s no trace of her usual swagger. Rio’s trembling – with rage, with fear – but she stays where she is, rooted to the spot.

“You know those men who used to institutionalize their wives?” Agatha says. “If a woman was too opinionated, or disagreed with her husband – they’d lock her up. And the more she’d argue she was sane, the more it was used as proof she wasn’t. She’d scream and cry about being called crazy and hysterical, and the doctors would say, well, look at her, she’s crazy and hysterical.”

“What the fuck are you talking about?” Rio snaps.

Agatha looks up at her. “My mother didn’t care about truth. It was just another tool – useful, if it got you what you wanted, but otherwise irrelevant.” She gives Rio a smile that comes nowhere near her eyes. “Now imagine a five-year-old girl, standing in front of a woman like that, asking her if she loves her.” She shakes her head, eyes bright with tears. “It doesn’t matter. The point is, those women never got out once their husbands put them away. The world decided who they were, and that was that.”

Rio stares at her. This is manipulation, too, she knows, all of it. Those sad, tearful eyes, that mention of a tiny Agatha asking her mother if she loved her. Casting Rio as the uncaring doctor, callously ignoring Agatha’s protestations of innocence, of honesty. It’s masterful – and the way that Rio knows it’s masterful is that she sees every bit of it for what it is, and she can feel it working anyway.

Two things can be true at once, she thinks. Agatha probably did grow up with a mother who didn’t love her – and that’s no excuse for everything she’s done. Rio is reflexively mistrustful of everything that comes out of Agatha’s mouth – and… it still might be true. Something doesn’t have to be a lie to be manipulative.

Rio forces her body to relax. She takes a few long breaths, and tries to control the trembling in her limbs. And then she walks over to the bed, and she sits down next to Agatha.

“Are you working with any other agents?” she asks.

“No,” Agatha says. She flashes Rio a wry smile. “The one I’ve got is kind of a handful.”

Rio doesn’t smile back. “So it’s just me you’re using.”

“Well, that’s not how I would put it, but – yeah. It’s just you, Rio.”

The words tug on something in Rio’s chest that she can’t afford to examine right now.

“What if it hadn’t worked?” she presses on. “What if I hadn’t gone for it?”

Who wouldn’t go for it? she expects Agatha to ask. Have you seen me? But instead she just sighs.

“Look. I’m down to my last good identity. I’ve got two or three months of resources left, if I’m lucky, and Mills has made sure hiding isn’t an option for me anymore. So I figured – if I got my name out through the FBI, he’d have to watch his step, at least. I needed more eyes on things to buy some time. It seemed like my best shot.” She looks up at Rio from behind her long lashes. “Sleeping with you… I don't know. You were cute. I was having fun playing detective. And I figured, best case, maybe you'd hesitate before you arrested me, once you knew who I was. Which, in my defense…” She trails off, glancing pointedly around the room at the rumpled sheets, their discarded clothes. “Kind of worked. But I didn’t expect, you know. This.”

Rio licks her lips, staring at Agatha.

“I don’t know if you’re lying to me right now,” she says finally.

“Yeah,” Agatha says. “I know.”

Rio falls back onto the bed, staring up at the ceiling. After a moment, Agatha does the same, and they lie there, side by side.

“Do you… want me to go?” The uncertain hitch in Agatha’s voice might actually be authentic, Rio thinks. But it might just be another lie.

Rio turns to look at her, and Agatha stares back at her, beautiful, vulnerable, intriguing, unfathomable. Rio can see, for a moment, all of her: the five-year-old girl that no one loved, the awkward teen coming into her power, the twenty-something learning to wield it, the adult woman who would rather die than surrender even an ounce of it.

Maybe it doesn’t matter whether she can prove that Agatha is telling the truth. The question has never been whether Agatha is trustworthy; Rio has always known she isn’t. The question is what Rio can live with. Whether she can keep choosing Agatha, knowing exactly who she is. Whether she’s capable of existing in this place with her: all this darkness, and all this light.

And somehow, even now, her answer is yes. Because whatever this is between them, however it started, the truth and the lies – it feels right. It’s like settling onto a throne Rio was always meant to inhabit, like wearing a crown she was always meant to bear. She doesn’t want to give this up. Even if it’s a mistake. Even if it ruins her.

Real. I feel real.

“No,” Rio says. “I don’t want you to go.”

Agatha breaks into a smile, slow and hopeful. Like a blooming thing.

And despite everything – because of everything – Rio smiles back.

Chapter 9

Rio props her head up on one elbow, gazing at Agatha as she buttons her blouse. She watches her dress with the same hungry attention she’d devoted to watching her undress hours before. Silvery streetlight filters through the window, catching the curve of Agatha’s throat, the precise movements of her fingers as she slips each button closed.

Agatha glances up at her. “What?”

Rio stretches, cat-like and lazy, exposing her skin like an offering. “Oh, nothing.”

Agatha smirks and crosses back to the bed, leaning down to brace her hands on either side of Rio, hair falling forward to curtain them both. She’s close enough that Rio can see the soft creases around her eyes. “Don’t tempt me, hot stuff.”

“But you’re so temptable.” Rio reaches up, threading her fingers through Agatha's hair, pulling her down into a kiss that starts gentle and turns desperate within seconds. She can taste herself on Agatha's lips, can feel the satisfied hum in Agatha's throat as Rio's tongue curls against hers. She wants to keep her here, pull her back into bed, make her stay through sheer force of want.

“And everyone thinks I’m the dangerous one,” Agatha murmurs into Rio’s mouth, voice teasing. She disentangles Rio’s hands from her hair and stands up. “You’re the one they should be watching out for.”

Rio snaps her teeth playfully as Agatha laughs.

“Come on. It’s only—” Rio checks the clock on her bedside table. “Two. Still a few hours til daylight.”

Agatha has returned to tucking her shirt into her pants with efficient grace. “Yeah, well, we don’t all have jobs we can just coast through on autopilot, now do we?”

“Whatever. You don’t even have a job,” Rio says as Agatha shrugs on her coat. “What could you possibly have to do that’s more fun than this?”

Agatha pauses in front of Rio’s mirror, running a hand through her wild hair, trying to straighten it. Her reflection meets Rio’s eye and winks. “Yeah, nice try, agent. I’m not falling for that one.”

Before Rio can think of a retort, Agatha turns and crosses back over to her, bending down and capturing her mouth in another kiss. Rio pushes up onto her knees this time, pressing into Agatha, bare skin sliding against the rough fabric of her coat. “See?” she says, pulling away. “Dangerous.”

“Yeah, yeah.” Rio flops back onto the bed. She gives a heavy sigh. “Fine. I’ll just have to take care of myself, then.”

She bites her lip as Agatha’s eyes drop to follow the hand she trails down her body – fingertips ghosting across her clavicle, over the swell of her breast, down the plane of her stomach, between her legs.

“Okay. That’s not fair,” Agatha says as Rio’s hand starts to move. Rio just lifts her eyebrows and pokes her tongue into her cheek, daring Agatha to walk out.

“You,” she says, crawling between Rio’s thighs with a hungry grin, “are a menace. You know that?”

But whatever Rio’s going to say dies in her throat as Agatha's mouth closes over her.

 

x

 

An hour later, Rio lies alone in the wreckage of her bed, tangled in sheets that smell like sex and sweat and Agatha’s earthy perfume. She closes her eyes and follows the sound of Agatha’s footsteps on the stairs, the soft click of the front door closing behind her. Disappearing back into whatever life she lives when she’s not breaking into Rio’s house or stalking her or showing up to fuck her senseless.

Rio pushes herself out of bed and moves to the window, peering through the gap in the curtains. Agatha’s silhouette moves down the sidewalk with an unhurried confidence, hands tucked into the pockets of her slacks. Rio watches her pass under one streetlight, then another. She doesn’t look back.

Why should she? Agatha knows where Rio lives, where she works. She probably knows where she buys her groceries, how she takes her coffee, what time she goes for her morning run. She shows up in Rio’s life like weather, inevitable and unpredictable. But Rio has no idea where she goes where she leaves. Where she sleeps, what her days look like. What she wears, what she eats, how she looks in the light of early morning. Whether she wakes up alone.

Rio acts quickly. She yanks on the jeans she’d kicked off earlier, pulls her shirt over her head. She doesn’t let herself think about it – if she thinks about it, she’ll talk herself out of it. She just moves: pulls on her shoes, shoves herself into her coat, grabs her keys off the table by the door.

The winter air hits her face as she plunges outside, bitter enough to sting her cheeks. Agatha’s farther down the block now, almost at the corner. Rio slides into the driver’s seat of her car and closes the door quietly behind her as Agatha turns left at the corner and disappears.

Rio counts to ten before starting the car. She creeps to the corner, headlights off, craning her neck to peer around.

There. Halfway down the block, brake lights flare red in the darkness. A sedan pulls away from the curb.

Rio lets her get more than a block away before she flicks on her headlights and follows. She keeps as far back as she dares. Tailing someone in a residential neighborhood is tricky in the light of day, much less at 3am, but her training takes over: maintain distance; take parallel routes; kill the headlights when turning after the target.

The sedan turns onto a larger street, and Rio follows. There’s slightly more traffic here – late-shift workers, bar crowds heading home – and it’s a little easier to blend in. She lets a car slip between them, then another. Agatha doesn’t speed, doesn’t make any sudden turns. She’s driving like someone with nowhere to be.

The sedan’s left turn signal flickers. Rio hangs back and watches as Agatha pulls onto a side street. She pulls over and counts to ten again, then follows, flicking her headlights off.

The houses lining this street are elegant and expensive – much more expensive than Rio’s. Massive trees arch overhead, their bare branches casting a web of shadows beneath the streetlights. The sedan is halfway down the next block now, braking.

Rio slows to a crawl, watching as Agatha pulls into a curving driveway. Rio glides to a stop three houses down. She peers through her windshield, taking in Agatha’s house.

It perches on the manicured lawn like something out of Architectural Digest magazine. Clean lines, steel and glass and stone glowing in the moonlight. Floor-to-ceiling windows reveal glimpses of the interior: soaring ceilings, a floating staircase, at least one fireplace.

This isn't some rundown AirB&B with cheap furniture and crappy anonymous decor. This isn’t somewhere Agnes would live. This place is all Agatha.

I’ve got two or three months of resources left, if I’m lucky, Agatha had said, and – yeah, no shit, if this is how she’s spending her money. The monthly rent on this place is probably more than what Rio makes in six.

Agatha sits in her car. The windows glow with a bluish light; she must be looking at her phone. Rio’s half-tempted to text her, just to see what would happen. She kind of gets it now, what it is that Agatha enjoys about this – the thrill of being so close to her, of Agatha having no idea she’s—

The figure creeps up behind Agatha’s car, crouching down behind it. There’s only moonlight for illumination, but from the figure’s stance and bearing, it looks like a man. Masked, broad-shouldered, poised and waiting. One of the Seven, Rio thinks – or, no, they wouldn’t come here themselves. Of course they wouldn’t. This is someone they sent. Someone they hired.

Someone who’s here to murder Agatha.

Adrenaline floods Rio’s bloodstream, imagines flickering through her mind so quickly she barely registers them. Sharon Davis’s body lying on a slab, stiff and grey. The terror of stumbling over Alice’s unmoving body. Agatha staring into her eyes, pupils dilating. Do you want me to go?

She reaches back, groping around in the footwell behind her, hand closing around the cold metal of a tire iron. Training and panic and fury collide as she twirls the tire iron in her hand and raises her arm, swinging as hard as she can. The impact shudders through her, metal finding meat and bone.

The man grunts as he topples forward, a noise of surprise and pain, the sound of a wounded animal. Something falls from his hand. He shifts, tries to push himself up.

“Rio.”

Rio looks over, breathing heavily. Agatha is standing next to the car. She glances down at the figure at Rio’s feet, and then looks up at Rio, awed.

“Okay,” Agatha says softly, lifting her hands, the way you might approach a frightened horse. “Okay.”

“Yes, I—”

“Agatha!”

Minimum necessary force.

The words clang through her head like a bell. All her years of training and experience taught her how to handle situation like this – assess the risk, call for backup, identify yourself as an agent. Neutralize the threat. Use minimum necessary force.
