Rio tries to make her face smile, to give some sort of response like a person would, but the word cheating sticks somewhere in her chest, rendering her unexpectedly silent.

“Five bucks,” the barista says, looking her up and down as Rio fumbles in her pocket for her wallet. “Wow. I like this look. You going undercover or something?”

The barista – Cait, Rio vaguely recalls her name is Cait – is about twenty years younger than Rio, and has spent the past year unabashedly flirting with her every chance she gets. With everyone, probably, but Rio’s always grinned and teased and flirted right back. But that was Agent Vidal. Today all she can manage to do is tap her card to pay and rasp something like Thanks as she takes her coffee and flees to a seat in the corner facing the door.

Nice. Perfect. Super normal.

This is going to go great.

 

 

She spots them through the window before they walk in – sharp suits, painted nails, costumes that still fit – and slinks down in her chair, taking a long sip of her coffee to help hide her face. As soon as they join the line she abandons the half-finished drink and darts outside.

It takes about five minutes for them to emerge, heads together, deep in conversation.

“Hi.” She gives an awkward wave.

Jen takes half a second to register who’s standing in front of her.

“No,” she says, already pushing past her.

“Wait – Jen, wait. Alice. Please.”

Alice doesn’t look as pissed as Jen, but she doesn’t look happy, either. “We’re not allowed to talk to you.”

“We don’t want to talk to you,” Jen snaps.

“Please,” Rio says again. “Look, I get how this looks. I would be thinking the same thing if I were you. But she is setting me up. She’s trying to ruin the investigation, okay? She pretended to be a cop, for god’s sake. She’s fucking unhinged. Just – please. Hear me out.”

Jen is already shaking her head, but Alice’s mouth twists a little, uncertainly. There, Rio thinks.

“Alice,” she says, focusing in. “I need your help. I have to find her. Please.”

Alice opens her mouth, glancing over at Jen. “I don’t… I can’t, um—”

“I don’t want to die in prison,” Rio says, and she lets her voice break a little. It doesn’t take much. “Please.”

“No one is helping you,” Jen says, lifting a hand. “You need to go before I call someone.”

But Rio can’t go. Not yet.

“Alice,” she presses. “How many cases have we worked together? You know how I run an investigation. You know I'm careful. Does any of this feel like me?"

Alice's eyes drop. She looks at her shoes, at her coffee. Anywhere but at Rio.

“There’s…” Alice says. “I mean, we’ve been trying to figure out—“

"Alice,” Jen says sharply. She gives her a warning glance before turning on Rio. “Did she send you?”

“What? Who – Harkness? No, of course not.”

“Oh, she’s ‘Harkness’ now? Really? Because in that voicemail Wanda played me, she was very clearly Agatha.”

Rio can feel the blush creeping up her face. She knows Jen’s clocking it, too, and so she’s careful to keep her voice even. “That wasn’t me, Jen. She’s trying to humiliate me. She’s trying to destroy my career.”

“Yeah? Was that before or after you guys went camping together?”

A tiny, high-pitched noise starts ringing in Rio’s ears.

“That was – listen—”

“No,” Jen says. “You listen. You made your bed, and you fucked a serial killer in it. I am not letting you drag us into this.”

“Alice—” Rio takes Alice by the arm as they try and push past her. “I just need – please. Anything that you can tell me about where she is. I just need to find her.”

Alice stops, but so does Jen. She stares down at Rio's hand on Alice's arm.

"When she killed that hit man," Jen says slowly, her voice flat now, anger carefully tucked away behind something more careful, "she had an accomplice.” Her eyes lift to meet Rio’s, cool and clinical. “Do you know anything about that?”

Rio snatches her hand away from Alice. “Are you serious? Jen, come on. We’ve known each other forever. You know me.”

“Exactly,” Jen says. “I know you.”

Rio’s jaw flexes as she grits her teeth.

“Jen, she’s not—”

“Uh-uh. No. Do not take her side in this,” Jen snaps at Alice. “She’s always had some bizarre thing for serial killers. You know that.”

“We don’t know anything yet,” Alice says. “We said we were going to wait—”

“She’s the one who showed up here.”

“Jen—”

“No.”

Rio looks between them. The argument is happening in the gaps between sentences, in what they're not saying as they stare at one another. She doesn't know what they were planning to wait for. She doesn't know when she stopped being a part of their conversations.

“We’re going,” Jen says finally, turning to face Rio. “Do not come near us again. Ever.”

Rio stands on the sidewalk and watches them walk away from her. Jen has her hand on the small of Alice's back, possessive, protective. The suit-wearing crowd flows around Rio, competent people on their way to do their competent jobs. The sun is still too bright.

She doesn’t move until they disappear from view.

 

x

 

Back home.

Couch.

The crack in the plaster.

Frustrated tears slip out of her eyes and down into her hairline. She’s been lying to herself for so long now that it had started to feel real: the thought that she would be okay. That she could bear the consequences of her choices, that it would all work out in the end. Be worth it.

Her cigarette has burned down to the filter. She drops it onto the plate beside the couch and lights another. Her hands aren't steady. She’d watched Jen and Alice walk away from her this morning. Alice had tilted her head onto Jen's shoulder, the small curve of her body asking for comfort, and Rio had thought—

It doesn’t matter what she thought. She takes a long drag and holds it.

She did this. She gave all of it away – quietly, over months. Each choice she made was a lit match, a tiny burst of flame. She’d told herself the house was still standing. And now she’s lying on the couch in the dark and the house is gone and she’s outside, in the cold, digging through the ash of it with her hands.

For what. For fucking what.

She exhales hard, smoke ribboning up toward the ceiling. Agatha had clocked her from the start. The FBI agent who’s got a thing for female serial killers? Of course I knew who you were. She was the agent who could be wound around Agatha’s finger, who’d look the other way and let her get away with literal murder. Agatha had been using Rio from the start, and Rio had let her. Rio had thanked her for it. She’d moaned things to Agatha in the dark that Wanda and Jen and half the FBI had heard played out loud, and—

I’m going to destroy her.

The thought arrives clean and cool and Rio reaches for it with both hands. Yes. That’s what she wants. She wants to hunt Agatha down and make her hurt. She wants to drag her through the burned out ruin of Rio’s life and force her to acknowledge the damage. She wants her sorry. Begging. She wants her on her knees.

She closes her eyes.

She can picture Agatha’s mouth, the small wry curve of it, the way it tips into laughter when Rio says something she finds amusing. Her hands, her long fingers, the pale skin of her wrists. Her collarbone in shadow. The way she gazes up at Rio when she kneels – her way of looking at her, seeing her, desiring her, holding Rio in her attention like a thing worth holding.

Rio’s eyes snap open.

The sound is so faint that for a second she thinks she’s imagined it. That after spending days conjuring Agatha out of refrigerator hum and silence, her brain has moved on to another way to torture her.

But then she hears it again: three small taps, evenly spaced.

Rio’s heart kicks once, hard, against her sternum.

She sits up and holds herself very still on the couch, cigarette burning between her fingers, straining to hear in the silence. The house seems to hold its breath with her. It’s nothing, she tells herself. A branch or something.

The tapping comes again. Deliberate, and a little faster this time. The rhythm of someone who knows she’s being heard and is tired of waiting.

Rio drops her cigarette onto the plate and stands. The room tilts slightly – she’s moved too fast, smoked too much, eaten nothing, barely slept. She steadies herself against the arm of the couch. And then she crosses the living room on bare feet, stepping across floorboards she sanded herself years ago. She pauses when she reaches the kitchen. Her hand finds the light switch on the wall, but she doesn’t flip it. She stares at the back door with its four-pane window.

Through the glass, in the spill of moonlight, she can see the pale curve of the face she has been dreaming about and hunting and failing to hunt for months. Agatha’s eyes are closed, her hair an unbrushed tangle. Her head rests gently against the doorframe.

Relief hits Rio behind the knees at the same moment a wildfire rage ignites in her chest. She wants to throw open the door. She wants to stare into her eyes and refuse her. She wants to break Agatha and bite her and tear at her skin and kiss her unconscious. The need is violent and deep, her muscles clenching, desire yawning wide beneath her like a chasm.

Agatha’s eyes flutter open. They find Rio’s through the glass, and she gives her a weak smile, lifting a hand in a greeting.

Even in the glint of moonlight, Rio can see the blood.

Her body takes over before her brain catches up, the way it always does with Agatha, and then the door is open. Agatha stands on her stoop, pale and swaying, hand wrapped around her bicep. Her sleeve is dark with blood.

“What are you doing here?” Rio demands. She’s relieved to find her voice still works.

Agatha swallows. “Oh, you know,” she says, trying and failing to sound casual. “Just passing through. Thought I’d say hi.”

“The FBI is probably watching my house.”

“Yeah. I used the back door.”

“Right, because they couldn’t possibly deduce I have a back door.” Rio lets out an angry hiss of air. For all her obsessive rumination, this hadn’t been how she’d imagined seeing Agatha again. I’m going to destroy her. She’d wanted a hunt, a fight. This is some weak, injured rag doll shivering on her doorstep.

Agatha shifts, wincing as she moves. “Well, then you should probably let me in before they see me.”

“Yeah? I’m thinking it solves a lot of my problems if I just tell them you’re here, actually.”

Agatha scoffs and shakes her hair back, managing to turn her pained grimace into something like a smile. “Oh, come on. You don’t want to do that. You’ve missed me.” She dips her head, giving Rio a loaded look. “I’ve missed you.”

A drip of blood trickles out from beneath her hand, trailing down her arm.

“What happened?”

“I was shot.” Agatha leans her head against the doorframe again, closing her eyes. “I’ve been shot. And I’m pretty sure I’m about to pass out, so now might be a good time to make a decision, here, sweet cheeks.”

Her breathing is shallow, face taut with pain. Eyes squeezed shut, lips parted. Collarbone in shadow—

Rio clenches her teeth.

“Just – fuck,” she says finally, glancing around over Agatha’s shoulder before she steps aside. “Why would you come here?”

Agatha gives her a wan smile as she allows Rio to pull her into the dining room.

“I told you. I missed you.”

“Yeah, right.” Rio pulls out a chair and motions for Agatha to sit down. “Just… don’t move.”

Agatha collapses into the seat and lets her head fall back, closing her eyes again. “Where would I go?”

Which sounds to Rio an awful lot like I’ve got you exactly where I want you.

She marches into the kitchen, slamming cabinets as she pulls out a glass. She stares at her reflection in the window as she fills it with water.

It’s never on her fucking terms – it’s always on Agatha’s. Fucking waltzing in here like Rio owes her anything, after everything she’s done, months of fucking with her—

But at least she’s here, says a voice in the back of Rio’s mind.

She sets the water down next to Agatha with more force than is strictly necessary.

“Drink.”

Agatha cracks one eye open, looking the glass up and down. “You don’t have anything… stronger?”

“It’ll help with the blood loss,” she says, already walking away. “Drink the fucking water.”

She returns a minute later with her first aid kit. Agatha’s still leaning back with her eyes closed like she hasn’t moved, but the glass is half-drained. Rio starts unpacking the contents of the kit – gauze, alcohol pads, tape – laying each one out on the table as she fumes.

Agatha clicks her tongue. “Now what did those scissors ever do to you?” she says after Rio slams them down. Rio shoots her a look, but Agatha just gazes at her, eyebrows raised.

“Okay,” she says. “I get it. You’re pissed.”

“Oh, you think?” Rio mutters.

“It’s not like coming here was my first choice,” Agatha says. “In case you’ve forgotten, the last time I was here you stabbed me in the gut.”

Rio has never felt less like laughing, but the words draw a humorless chuckle out of her anyway.

“Oh, is that funny?” Agatha asks. “I almost died.”

“And yet here you are.” Rio picks up the scissors and turns toward her. “Like a fucking cockroach.”

Agatha shifts uncomfortably in her chair. “Hey. Watch where you point those things.”

“What?” Rio widens her eyes and pastes a deranged smile on her face. She snaps the scissors a few times. “These?”

“Stop it.” Agatha purses her lips as Rio huffs another cruel laugh. “I’m glad you find my PTSD to be so entertaining.”

“You want me to bring you a tiny violin?” Rio asks, reaching for Agatha’s wrist. Agatha flinches back, and Rio rolls her eyes. “Oh my god, would you relax? I’m not gonna stab you, I need to cut your sleeve.”

Agatha scoffs. “Absolutely not. This shirt is worth more than your car.”

“It’s covered in blood and there’s a bullet hole in it. You want my help or not?”

Agatha pauses for a moment, considering, and then sighs, closes her eyes, and holds out her arm like an offering. Like she’s doing Rio a favor by heroically submitting to the indignity of being helped.

“Fine,” she announces dramatically.

“Wow. Thanks,” Rio says as she starts cutting up the length of Agatha’s sleeve. Agatha makes a few pained noises that could plausibly be about either the wound or the shirt.

“You gonna tell me what happened?” she asks after a moment, eyes on her work.

“I told you, I was shot.”

“One of Robert Mills’ guys?”

“God, I hope so. I really don’t need someone else coming after me right now.”

“Well, you know Agatha,” Rio says conversationally, “maybe if you weren’t always doing things that made people want to kill you—”

“Oh, we’re victim-blaming now? I thought we’d moved past that. Like, as a society.”

Rio gives her a look. “What happened to the shooter?”

“How should I know?” Agatha says with a shrug. “I was busy running for my life.”

Rio pauses. “Well… did you lose him?”

Agatha lifts her hand and crosses her fingers with sarcastic optimism. “Here’s hoping.”

Rio takes a measured breath. “Agatha, are you telling me that you might have led the guy who’s trying to kill you to my house?”

“Oh, he’s not gonna do anything,” Agatha says dismissively. “You’re an FBI agent.”

“Uh, sure. Except thanks to you I’m not anymore, am I?”

“Well, let’s hope he doesn’t know that."

“I don’t even have a gun in the house! I can’t—” She stops, taking in a sharp breath. “You know what? No. I’m not doing this. You need to get out.”

Agatha’s eyebrows furrow. “Excuse me?”

“I have been trying to find you for weeks. Like, obsessively searching for you. And then the minute I see you again, I remember why things are so much fucking easier when you’re not around.”

A slow smirk plays at the corner of Agatha’s lips. “Obsessively?”

“Get out.”

“No,” Agatha says simply.

“Get the fuck out, Agatha.”

“Hey,” Agatha snaps, all humor suddenly gone. “I’m only here because of you. This is your fault.”

“What? How is it my fault?”

“Uh, you stabbed me? I go my entire life without getting shot by one of these assholes, and then you nearly kill me, and here we are. This is on you. You break it, you buy it. Or… fix it, or whatever.”

Agatha sits back in her chair like it’s settled. Another trickle of blood slips down her arm.

Wait.

Rio, wait.

Don’t—

Rio’s hand twitches with the muscle memory of pushing the knife in, the wet heat of it. She closes her eyes.

“Okay. I will patch you up,” she says evenly. “And then you’re leaving.”

To her surprise, Agatha doesn’t argue. She offers her arm again, and Rio holds it lightly as she cuts away the rest of the sleeve. Agatha’s skin is warm, and the iron smell of her blood mixes with the dark wood scent of her perfume. The shirt – what's left of it – still covers Agatha's abdomen, but Rio knows what’s there. She can feel it, almost. The shape of the place she slid the knife in.

She forces herself to focus on Agatha’s arm. The bullet carved a channel along the outside of her bicep, taking a strip of skin and flesh with it. Ugly, but not as bad as it could have been. No through-and-through, at least, and no embedded fragments. The tissue around it is already turning the deep blackish-purple of what’s going to be a vicious bruise.

“You’re lucky,” she says. “Half an inch over and it would have hit bone.”

Agatha gives a derisive snort. “Right. Lucky.”

Rio grabs a handful of gauze pads and sits down, carefully starting to wipe away the blood.

They go quiet. Rio can hear Agatha breathing, slow and soft, the small hitch every time Rio presses too close to the broken skin. She works methodically, cleaning up the length of her arm first, then closer to the wound itself, the gauze coming away dark each time. Agatha doesn't move, but Rio can feel her staring, eyes fixed on her like she’s waiting for Rio to meet her gaze.

“So,” Agatha says after a while, voice cheery. “Heard from Blondie lately?”

She gives a loud yelp as Rio’s hand swipes over the gash in her skin.

“Ow!” she says indignantly.

“Okay, what the fuck is wrong with you?” Rio asks, throwing bloody gauze onto the table and pushing herself to stand up. “Do you want me to stab you again?”

“Wow. Sorry,” Agatha mutters. “I was just asking.”

“Is this why you really came here? To brag about fucking up my life?”

Agatha raises her eyebrows. “Is your life fucked up?”

Rio just stares at her incredulously.

“She was going to break up with me,” Rio says. “After everything you did at that stupid dinner, she was about to break up with me. She would have been gone. But you sent her back. Why? Just so you could send that fucking voicemail?”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “No,” she says. “I sent her back because what’s the fun in seducing your girlfriend if she’s not your girlfriend anymore? Ugh, I had a whole plan. It would have been glorious. But someone had to stab me.”

Of course. Of course that’s what she’d planned to do. “Well, if you didn’t want to get stabbed, maybe you shouldn’t have fucked me when she was in bed next to me.”

“I don’t remember you complaining at the time.”

“Is my life fucked up,” Rio mutters. “You’ve been the one fucking it up since the day we met! Fucking Agnes—”

“I don’t remember you complaining about her, either,” Agatha says with a cocky grin.

“You keep breaking into my house—”

“To give you gifts! And orgasms! God forbid a girl be thoughtful.”

“Well, congratulations. Yes, my life is fucked up. You’ve destroyed my career and I’m probably going to die in prison. And then, for some fucking reason, you decided to destroy Wanda’s life, too, even though she had nothing to do with any of this.”

Agatha sits back, looking thoughtful. “I destroyed your life all on my own, hm? You had no control over any of it?”

Rio narrows her eyes. “Fuck you.”

“Just sitting there, minding your own business, and all of this just happened to you.” She clicks her tongue sympathetically. “You poor thing.”

“You could have left Wanda out of it.”

“You could have left Wanda out of it,” Agatha retorts. “And I don’t know what you’re complaining about. She’s alive, isn’t she?”

“Oh, what, I’m supposed to give you credit for that? Not killing people is the baseline, Agatha.”

“Not for me, it isn’t,” Agatha sneers obnoxiously. “You brought her into this. You used her as a weapon, fucked her in front of me—”

“She was my girlfriend!”

“No, no, no, no, no.” Agatha’s laugh is cruel. “Don’t act like I was the other woman. She was the other woman.”

Rio stares down at her, breathing heavily. All her arguments rise up in her throat and gather there like smoke.

“Do you have any idea what happens to people who hurt me, Rio?” Agatha asks. “Because I think you do. But your friends, your family, your precious Wanda – all of them are fine. You stabbed me. I sent a voicemail.”

Her lip is curled, her eyes defiant, resentful. And all Rio can do is stand there in silence, bearing the weight of her gaze as the words land. As she starts to understand what it is Agatha is telling her.

All this time. All these months. Every person she'd been afraid for – Wanda, Jen, Alice, Lilia, her friends, her family… none of them had been touched. Agatha had wanted to. Of course she'd wanted to. But she hadn't.

Rio sees it suddenly: the wildfire of Agatha Harkness, Rio’s own hand plunged into the heart of her. And still, Agatha hadn't burned her alive.

She’d held back. She'd controlled herself.

For Rio, she'd controlled herself.

So.

That’s… something.

Rio sits down in the chair next to Agatha. After a moment she picks up a fresh pad of gauze and some tape.

“I’ll just… I’ve gotta finish,” she says. As she leans in, Agatha turns her head so that they’re nearly eye-to-eye. Rio’s heart thuds in her chest.

“Look… you can stay here tonight if you want,” Rio continues. “On the couch. Just… so you don’t get murdered out there.”

Agatha nods slowly. “Mm. Because if I’m going to get murdered, it should be in here,” she says, giving Rio a wry smile. “By you.”

“Well, yeah. You know. Ideally,” Rio says, returning her smile with a small one of her own. She places the last piece of tape and glances up at Agatha: her eyes blue and very close, her breath warm against Rio’s skin. Rio clears her throat.

“All set,” she says, leaning back, and Agatha gives a tentative roll of her shoulder. She winces.

“Well, at least I won’t get gangrene, I guess.”

She stands up and sways, eyelashes fluttering. “Whoa,” she says, grabbing onto the table for support.

Rio’s hand darts out to steady her. “You good?”

“Yeah.” Agatha nods. “But you should probably walk me upstairs so I don’t fall and crack my skull open. Trust me, brain matter is super annoying to get out of rugs.”

Rio shoots her a look. “Okay, first of all, I don’t want to know why you know that. Second of all, I said you could stay on the couch.”

“What?” Agatha asks, pretending to be incredulous. “I thought you were joking. I’m in my fifties, sweetheart – if I sleep on a couch I may never walk again.”

Rio lets her head fall back and gives a dramatic sigh. “Right, of course, what was I thinking. The serial killer who ruined my life and then showed up begging for favors should get the bed.” She lifts her head. “See, now that time I was joking.”

“And I’ll be laughing all the way up the stairs,” Agatha says, starting to cross the room. Rio lets out one more pointed sigh, and then she follows.

 

x

 

Rio's bedroom is dusty and dim and very obviously the bedroom of someone who has not been sleeping in it. The blinds are half-drawn, the sheets tangled at the foot of the bed where she'd kicked them off a week ago. A glass of water sits on the nightstand, a film on the surface. Agatha lowers herself onto the edge of the bed with a small grateful exhale, her good hand bracing against the mattress as her eyes do a slow circuit around the room.

They stop when they get to the painting propped up on Rio’s dresser. Her gaze flickers over to Rio as she gives her the barest hint of a knowing smile.

Rio still hadn’t been able to touch it. The painting had become a talisman of sorts, a reminder of what she’d done. What she could do: hunt and kill, conquer and destroy. Whether that felt like inspiration or an indictment depended on the day.

“Bathroom is there,” Rio says, cutting off whatever gloating Agatha’s obviously about to start in on. “Towels are in the closet. I’d tell you not to go through my shit, but I’m guessing you already catalogued my underwear drawer or whatever when you broke in.”

Agatha’s teasing smile widens. “Which time?”

“Yeah,” Rio says. “Okay, then.”

She turns to leave.

“Wait,” Agatha says. “You’re not actually sleeping on the couch.”

“Annnnd, here we go,” Rio says wearily.

“Here we go, what? I’ve been shot.”

Rio crosses her arms. “You were grazed.”

“Yeah, and I lost a lot of blood. I could die in the night!”

Rio snorts. “Like I’d ever get that lucky.”

“Hey,” Agatha says, outraged, as Rio turns to leave again. “You know, if this is how you treat all the women you bring home, I’m starting to understand why you can’t keep a girlfriend.”

She shouldn’t rise to the bait, but she finds herself spinning on her heel anyway. “If this is how obnoxious you are to people who do you favors, I’m starting to understand why you’re completely alone in the world.”

She expects Agatha to come back with an even angrier reply, but instead she pulls her feet up, lying back against Rio’s pillow and crossing her feet at the ankle, eyes sparkling. “See, you’re gonna miss this if I bleed out tonight.”

“Oh, I think I’d manage somehow.”

The smile slips off Agatha’s face as she stares at Rio, worrying her lower lip, going serious.

“Would you stay? Just for a bit. Just until I fall asleep. Today was...”

She trails off. It takes Rio a moment to realize she’s blinking back tears.

“I don’t think I’ll be able to sleep if I’m…”

She doesn’t finish the sentence, but it’s still the first thing she’s said all night that sounds genuine – the worry in her voice, the small tremor. She looks so small suddenly, sitting on Rio’s bed, her skin still too pale.

It’s manipulation, Rio reminds herself. It’s a show Agatha’s putting on to get her way.

But… she was shot. It’s not crazy to think she’d be experiencing some trauma from that. Rio's seen strong, experienced agents descend into total panic in the days and weeks after being attacked. The dread of your own mortality doesn't care how tough you are.

Manipulation wrapped in truth. Classic Agatha.

Rio glances over at the painting of herself, at her own gaze staring steadily back at her, and she takes a long breath.

And then she releases it and crosses the room, perching on the other side of the bed. After a moment she swings her legs up and lies back next to Agatha, staring up at the ceiling.

“I’m not having sex with you,” she says into the silence.

Agatha scoffs. “Get your mind out of the gutter, Vidal. I’m mortally wounded.”

“Uh-huh.”

“Although…” Agatha says, turning over to look at Rio, “if I did die tonight, I bet you’d really regret not having sex with me one last time. Just something to think about.”

Rio doesn't answer. Agatha is still on her side, watching her, that small wry curve at the corner of her mouth – the same expression she'd had on the stoop, bleeding, telling Rio she'd missed her. The same one she'd had at the dinner with Wanda. The same one she has in every photo in Rio's file. Like nothing she says ever costs her anything.

“Can I ask you something?” Rio asks finally.

“Yeah,” Agatha replies easily.

“You said… before. A while ago. You said you feel… real with me.”

“Uh.” Rio can see Agatha blinking in her peripheral vision. “Did I?”

“Yeah. We were having sex, and you said—”

“Oh, right,” Agatha says dismissively. “That. I mean, you were inside me and you weren’t going to let me come until I said something. So.”

Rio turns her head to look at her. “So it’s not true?”

Agatha lets out a theatrical groan and flops back against the pillow. "Oh, god. Are we doing feelings now? I've lost a lot of blood, Rio, I really don't think—"

“Because everything you do feels like a performance,” she says pointedly.

Agatha raises her eyebrows. “Look who’s talking, sister.”

Rio sits up, back curled against the headboard. “I still don’t know anything about you.”

“What? You know plenty about me. You’ve read my FBI file. You met my sixth grade teacher, for god’s sake.”

“Oh, yeah, and you were thrilled about that.”

Agatha looks momentarily puzzled. “Oh – because I killed her? That was just to get your attention.”

“No it wasn’t. You already had my attention.”

She gives a coy tilt of her head. “Couldn’t stop thinking about me?”

But Rio doesn’t respond. Her mind is too busy turning that day over again – Agatha had murdered Sharon Davis, then she’d showed up in Rio’s living room for the first time. Rio had peppered her with questions, and she’d answered some of them, sort of. It had been mostly deflections. The whole night had been one big deflection, probably. A distraction. Something designed to keep Rio from following the path she was on, digging into Agatha’s past.

“Why did you kill your mother?” Rio asks now, looking Agatha in the eye.

Agatha’s smile drops. “Wow, okay. You really don’t want to have sex,” she says, turning back over to face the ceiling. “Message received.”

“I just want to understand.”

“You know,” Agatha says, “you demand a lot of honesty for someone who can’t admit a fucking thing about herself.”

Rio startles a little at the venom in Agatha’s voice. “Excuse me?”

“How about this. I’ll tell you about my mother if you tell me what I’m doing here.”

Rio raises her eyebrows. “Uh, you just showed up here. It’s not like I invited you.”

“Why did you let me in?”

“Christian charity, obviously,” Rio says flatly.

“And what about the time before that?” Agatha presses, ignoring Rio’s answer. “And the time before that? I’m in your bed, Rio. God – how many knives do I need to hand you?”

There it is – the thing Agatha keeps circling back to, the question underneath all her questions. Agatha keeps offering her the handle of a blade, and Rio keeps pretending she doesn’t know what it’s for. She can taste the words she's being asked to say, but her mouth refuses to form them.

“I don’t want knives,” she says instead.

Agatha laughs. “Says the woman who stabbed me.” Rio catches the hand that Agatha is about to run up her arm, but Agatha is undeterred. “You’re right there, sweetheart,” she breathes. “You’re so close.”

For a second neither of them moves – Agatha's wrist in Rio’s grip, pulse ticking steadily against Rio's thumb.

Rio feels herself leaning in. Toward the words, toward Agatha, toward whatever's waiting on the other side of saying it. Her body always knows before she does.

But she stops. She makes herself stop.

“You’re supposed to be bleeding out," she says.

“You saved me.” Agatha tilts her head playfully. “My hero.”

Rio almost laughs. She'd asked about Agatha's mother and ended up with Agatha's pulse under her thumb and her own confession halfway up her throat. God, there's never any getting to the middle of her – you reach for the center and there's just more Agatha, all the way down. A labyrinth in the shape of a woman. A black hole that can climb into your bed.

“Okay,” she says, pushing herself up. She has to move, now, get away from Agatha’s skin, the warmth of her, the words falling from that dangerous mouth. “Since you’re obviously fine, I’m gonna go sleep on the couch.”

“What – oh, come on,” Agatha says. “We were just getting to the good part!”

Rio spins around. “This is not the good part, Agatha. There’s no good part. My life is over. I’m sorry if I’m not in the mood for whatever the fuck you’re doing right now, but I’m really not.”

Agatha makes an incredulous sound. “Well I don’t know what you think talking about my mother is going to do—”

“Because it would be something!” Rio shouts. “Look – you took everything. And I gave it to you, I did, I know. I did. I just thought that by the end, I would… know you, at least.”

Agatha sucks in her cheeks, frowning as she studies her.

“Well, there’s your problem, sweetheart,” she says finally. “You think this is the end.”

“The FBI is building a case against me. How do you think this ends?”

“I don’t know! That’s what makes it fun.”

“Great,” Rio says, heading for the door. “I’m glad you’re having a good time.”

She makes it to the hallway, halfway to the stairs, before Agatha speaks.

“Rio.”

She keeps walking.

“Rio,” Agatha says more sharply. “Come back here.”

She starts down the staircase, feet thudding so that Agatha can hear her descend.

“Okay, fine,” Agatha calls after her. “If you want me to go through your underwear drawer, great. Happy to keep myself entertained.”

She makes it to the bottom of the staircase and crosses the room, dropping down onto the couch, and she waits.

There’s a long stretch of silence.

“Oh, for god’s… well, I’m not yelling the whole story down the stairs,” Agatha calls finally, irritated.

“Why not?” Rio asks. “I can hear you fine.”

Her mouth twitches a little at the sound of Agatha’s growl. “Just get back up here.”

Rio counts to five. The she takes the stairs slowly and returns to the bedroom, pausing in the doorway with her arms crossed.

“Sit down,” Agatha says.

“I’ll stand.”

“It’s a long story.”

“I’m in pretty good shape,” Rio says. “I think I can manage.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. “Fine.”

She shifts around, wincing as she props up a pillow behind her, taking time to arrange it. Then she clears her throat. She clasps her hands in front of her, then unclasps them. Her mouth starts to form a word, but she seems to think better of it.

Rio almost speaks – “Stop stalling and say it already” – but she’s stopped by the fact that Agatha really does seem nervous. So she stands there, letting it take the time it takes.

“I had a—” Agatha finally says, but then her mouth closes again, and she swallows. She shakes her head, irritated. “Ugh. This is so—”

“No,” Rio says, unfolding her arms. “Say it.”

Agatha looks annoyed, but she closes her eyes and takes a breath.

“I had—” she begins again, and it’s like she’s pulling it up from a well, like the story has to be unearthed from somewhere deep within her and pulled into the light.

“I had a child,” she says finally. “I had a son.”

The words hit Rio like a bullet to the chest.

A son.

Somewhere in all the time Rio has spent building a picture of this woman – the cult, the bodies, the careful catalogue of everything she is – there had been a child, and Rio hadn't known. Hadn't even thought to wonder.

She doesn’t realize she’s moving until she is; she keeps her eyes fixed on Agatha as she crosses the room and sits on the bed, curling her legs beneath her.

“Okay,” she manages.

“She took him from me,” Agatha says.

“Your mother? Why would… where?” Rio’s questions tangle, her mind not able to grasp on as the world tilts.

“She didn’t want me to have him.” Her voice is low, bitter. “That’s how she was. She didn’t want me to have anything that wasn’t hers.”

“So – she just—”

“She had doctors and lawyers and judges. They said I was an unfit mother. That’s what they called me. So they pulled him out of my arms and gave him to someone better.”

Agatha is staring somewhere over Rio’s shoulder. Her fingers curl in her lap, unconsciously grasping.

Someone better.

Rio had known Evanora was controlling and abusive – she’d understood on some level that Agatha had grown up unloved and manipulated, that every good thing about her had been twisted into a weapon or a punishment. But to do this – to try and break her with this—

She leans into Agatha’s line of sight. “I would have killed her, too.”

Agatha doesn’t seem to hear the words. She slips down the bed, curling up in a little ball, and Rio lies down across from her. They stare at one another, silent.

“What was his name?” Rio asks finally.

Agatha blinks away her tears, and this smile, finally, is real.

“Nicholas,” she says. “Nicky. I called him Nicky.”

“Nicky,” Rio says softly.

Agatha closes her eyes, like she’s imagining him in front of her.

“He was perfect.”

Rio’s gaze traces the path of tears down Agatha’s cheek and tries to imagine him, this little piece of her, walking around in the world.

“I know he was,” she says.

Agatha’s eyes open again, and they lie there, staring at one another, their breathing the only sound between them. Agatha looks wrung out, wrecked – dark circles under her red-rimmed eyes, lips pale, hair a wild nest. She looks beautiful. She looks real.

Another tear slides down her cheek, and Rio reaches out. Her thumb brushes it away, and Agatha blinks, slow and unsurprised. Rio traces along her cheekbone, over the whorl of her ear, along her jaw. Agatha’s mouth parts very slightly as Rio runs her thumb along her lower lip.

Perfect, she thinks.

She leans in.

The kiss is soft, quiet. Slow. Agatha’s hand slides into Rio’s hair as they press together, as Rio’s tongue curls and Agatha’s tears wet her own cheeks.

And then Agatha groans, the smallest sound in the back of her throat, and her grip tightens. She rolls on top of Rio, enveloping her entirely, and Rio lets her. She lets Agatha pull her down, dragging her under, leaving her breathless.

Like falling.

Like drowning.

Perfect.

Chapter 14

Rio wakes tangled in Agatha’s arms. Agatha’s hair spills over them both like a blanket, and the soft brush of it against Rio’s skin is the first thing she’s conscious of as she opens her eyes. That, and the heat of Agatha’s body. The substance of her, her breath, chest rising and falling as she sleeps.

She’s here. Agatha Harkness is here, in her bed.

After so long, that persistent snag in Rio’s heart, the constant drum of I can’t, I shouldn’t – all of it has quieted. Rio’s heart beats strong and sure as she gazes at Agatha in the dark. Her eyelashes flutter, eyes moving as she dreams, and Rio wonders what she’s dreaming about. She wants to know every thought in her head. Wants Agatha to flood her senses, the way she did last night: hungry mouth enveloping her own, the smell of her skin in Rio’s nostrils, breathing Agatha’s breath, Agatha’s tears on both their cheeks. Rio knows somewhere in the back of her mind that it’s fucked up to get turned on at the sight of Agatha crying, that the ache between her legs shouldn’t sharpen at the sight, but she’s done with shouldn’t. It’s as potent as a drug: Agatha, vulnerable, murmuring secrets to Rio. Only to Rio, the only one she trusts. The two of them curled up in this world they’ve carved out together, the universe shrinking to the size of Rio’s bedroom, her bed.

And so when Agatha had kissed her, climbed on top of her, when her tears wet Rio’s cheeks, all Rio could think was more. Agatha pressed into her with the desperation of a confessor, like Rio’s body could absolve her of her sins, but it was Rio who was ready to beg, plead, ready to give Agatha anything she wanted, hand over whatever power she demanded from her if she would just—

“Can I?” Agatha had asked softly, staring up at Rio from between her thighs, and the absurdity of the question – the fact that she was asking it now, after everything – wrenched a hysterical sort of laugh out of Rio.

“Yes,” she practically shouted, “Jesus – fuck—” and then Agatha was grinning, and her tongue was slipping over Rio, lapping at her, flicking, her arms wrapping around Rio’s thighs to hold her open, pin her down. Rio had gasped and moaned and laughed and arched against her as the two of them floated, up, and up, and up.

Now Agatha raises an eyebrow in her sleep. Rio marvels at how expressive her face is even at rest, like she’s always about to act, to say the next outrageous thing, to laugh or mock, to snarl or scream. Rio could almost—

There’s a creak in the floorboards somewhere downstairs, barely audible, and Rio realizes all at once that this is why she’s awake. This is the sound that woke her.

“Agatha,” she whispers, but Agatha doesn’t stir. “Agatha.”

“Mm,” Agatha murmurs, pulling Rio closer.

Rio untangles herself from Agatha’s arms and climbs to her feet, walking slowly to the bedroom door.

“What?” Agatha protests sleepily, eyes still closed.

“Get up,” Rio whispers.

She gives a whiny grumble. “Why?”

“Because there’s someone in the house.”

Agatha sits up, suddenly alert, eyes blinking wide and owlish in the darkness.

“How many?”

Only one shooter had gone after Agatha earlier, but if this man was breaking into the house of an FBI agent – if he’d assumed Rio would be armed, trained, prepared – would he have brought backup? Hitmen tend to work alone. But if he isn’t… Rio isn’t armed. Agatha’s injured. They may be dead already.

Agatha rolls out of bed and starts throwing on her clothes, wincing with every flex of her arm. Rio collects her own clothes from the floor, tugging her jeans up, shirt over her head, her movements precise and silent. She keeps her eyes on the bedroom door. It’s ajar, just barely, but she knows it’ll creak loudly the moment she tries to open it. The front door is at the bottom of the stairs, dead-bolted. She’ll have to waste precious seconds finding her keys, getting the right one into the lock, turning it. The back door’s not bolted, but there’s no way they’d make it – there’s too much wide open space between here and there. She glances at the bedroom window. Two stories up. No way. Not with Agatha injured.

Okay.

She strides quietly over to her bedside table and pulls out the knife with its green and twisting vines. Agatha shrinks back a little as she approaches, but Rio ignores her and presses the handle into her palm.

“Defend yourself,” she whispers. “Throw it if you have to, but do not fucking miss.”

Agatha stares down at her hand. “Uh. I’m not really a knife girl.”

Rio rifles underneath her bed and pulls out an expired can of pepper spray. She’d been meaning to replace it, but it was low on her list of priorities. Because she’d always had her fucking gun.

She hands that to Agatha, too. “Nozzle out,” she says, fitting it into her hand so that it points away from her face. Agatha tries to hand back the knife, but Rio shakes her head. “I’m going to unlock the front door. You’re going to cover me.”

“What?” Agatha hisses. “No, I’ll unlock the door. You deal with the weapons.”

“You don’t know where my keys are, and you don’t know which key to use. I’ll be faster.”

Agatha rolls her eyes. She tucks the pepper spray under her arm and reaches into the pocket of her pants. “You mean this key?”

Rio stares at the piece of metal in her hand.

“Okay, if we don’t die tonight, we’re gonna have a conversation about boundaries,” she says after a moment.

Agatha scoffs softly as she pushes the knife and pepper spray into Rio’s hands. “Boundaries are for people who don’t know what they want. Now go stab someone who deserves it and get me out of here.”

Rio moves toward the door, starts slowly easing it open – but in the silence, she hears it. A low creak on the staircase.

He's coming up the stairs.

She pulls the door shut, turns back to Agatha. In the dark she can just make out the pale shape of her face, the whites of her eyes. Rio jerks her chin toward the window.

Agatha's gaze follows, and then she looks at Rio like she’s gone insane. She shakes her head once, hard.

Rio crosses to her in three steps. "No choice," she breathes, barely a sound at all.

"My arm—"

"I know." She's already moving to the window, unlatching it, sliding it up as quietly as she can manage. The night air blows in, tree branches violining together softly. In the dark, the ground is just – gone. She can feel the distance more than see it.

Fuck. This might be a really bad idea.

“I’ll go first,” she says. “You lower yourself as far as you can and then drop. I'll be there to catch you.”

“I’m not jumping out a fucking window,” Agatha whispers sharply. “Just stab him.”

Rio starts to say something about bringing a knife to a gunfight, but the floor creaks again, too close. She turns to catch Agatha’s eye. “I will be there.”

Agatha stares at her for a moment, something complicated moving across her face, and then she nods.

Rio straddles the windowsill and clambers out, slowly lowering herself down. It’s not her first controlled fall; she’d trained for things like this at Quantico, but right now that feels like a million years ago. Still, she does her best, pushing the wall away as she lets go, trying to relax her body as she drops. The impact sends a jolt of pain up her legs, but she keeps her feet together, keeps her knees bent, lets herself roll with the impact.

She winces as she pulls herself up, flexing her wrists and ankles tentatively. Nothing broken, nothing sprained. Good. Okay.

Now for the hard part.

“I am not doing this,” Agatha hisses down at her.

“Fine,” Rio whispers back. “Let the guy with the gun get you.”

Agatha opens her mouth to make some snarky reply, but then she whips her head around. When she turns back to Rio, her eyes are wide, terrified.

“Now!”

Agatha practically throws herself out the window, ungainly and graceless, feet scrambling for purchase on the wall. She inhales sharply as her arm extends, and Rio moves quickly, positioning herself beneath her.

“Ready?” Rio asks. “On three—”

But Agatha is already falling, desperate to get away or unable to hold on any longer. Rio tries to spread the energy of the impact, leaning back as Agatha lands, letting them both collapse with a painful oomph. It knocks the wind out of Rio.

“Come on,” Agatha groans as she rolls away, and Rio coughs, gulping for air as her lungs start to open back up. “Move.”

Rio climbs to her feet as a man’s face appears in the window overhead. Shit. She grabs Agatha’s arm and flattens them both against the side of the house, minimizing his target. Thunderous footsteps shake the walls.

“Where’s your car?” she asks Agatha, pulling her toward the tree line in the backyard even before she gets an answer. They have to move, they have to get out of here, now, but she doesn’t have her car keys, doesn’t have time to—

“This way,” Agatha pants, nodding in the direction they’re already heading. They move as swiftly and silently as they can through the trees, Rio gritting her teeth every time a branch snaps beneath their feet. She keeps looking over her shoulder, but there’s no sign of the man. Yet.

“How much farther?”

“It’s—”

Rio hears a branch crack somewhere behind her, loud as a gunshot.

“Go!”

They break into a full sprint into someone’s yard, Rio a few steps behind Agatha as they pound across the street and down the sidewalk. “Drive,” Agatha shouts as she wrenches open the passenger side door of a nondescript silver sedan.

Rio throws herself into the driver’s seat and fumbles around for the car’s start button, glancing in the rearview as the engine roars to life. A figure emerges from the trees – she can make out jeans, a hat, but the face is obscured by distance and darkness.

“Go!” Agatha growls.

Rio shifts the car into gear and presses down on the gas.

 

x

 

Rio keeps to the speed limit. It feels insane – every cell in her body is screaming at her to floor it – but the last thing she needs is to get pulled over at three in the morning with pine needles in her hair and a serial killer in her passenger seat.

“Get on the Beltway,” Agatha says eventually. It’s the first thing either of them has said in several minutes; her voice is steadier than Rio expected. “Then 66 West."

Rio checks the mirror. Checks it again thirty seconds later. There's a pair of headlights two cars back that have been there since the on-ramp, and she watches them with the same attention she’s paying to her own driving, cataloguing distance, speed, the number of lane changes.

“Well?” Agatha demands after Rio adjusts the rearview for the third time.

“I don’t know,” Rio says. “Could be nothing. I’ve never been followed by a hitman before.”

“Mm. Brag about it,” Agatha grumbles. Rio glances over and finds her staring out the window, jaw tight, cradling her injured arm.

“How is it?”

“Being followed by a hitman?” Agatha asks in a syrupy voice. “So fun.”

“Your arm.”

Agatha gives her an irritated glance. “You made me jump out of a window. What do you think?”

“I think I saved your life by letting you use me as a human trampoline. But whatever.” The headlights behind them peel off at the next exit. Rio watches them go and feels something in her chest unclench, just slightly. “Seriously, are you hurt?”

“I’m fine.” Agatha shoots her another look. “Or I would be, if you weren’t driving like my grandmother. Can we pick it up a little?”

“I’m driving the speed limit.”

“Well, stop it. We’re being chased by a guy who’s already shot me once, in case you’ve forgotten.”

“I don’t want to get pulled over, and I need to watch the mirror.” Rio keeps her eyes on the road. “Any other complaints you’d like to lodge?”

“Yeah, plenty.”

“Great. I’ll be here.”

Agatha exhales through her nose, sharp, and turns back to the window. Her shoulders are hunched, rigid, and she's still got her arm pulled in close against her ribs, like she's protecting it. Rio recognizes the shape of it – not the irritation, but the thing underneath it. The way Agatha is curling around herself, growling like an injured animal. It’s not her arm, Rio understands. That’s not the wound that’s aching.

Rio doesn’t say anything about it; she’s learned that much, at least. Instead she reaches over after a few minutes, not looking away from the road, and she rests her hand on Agatha’s knee.

Agatha goes very still.

But she doesn’t shake Rio’s hand off. She doesn’t say anything, either, and doesn’t turn her head away from the window. But after a moment, her free hand comes down to rest on top of Rio’s. Not quite holding it, not even entirely on top of it. Like it could have just fallen there accidentally. But Rio knows better.

She’s here, Rio thinks again. She’s here.

 

 

“Take this exit,” Agatha says an hour later.

They come off the highway onto a state route, then off the state route onto something that isn't really a road so much as the suggestion of one – gravel giving way to packed dirt, trees pressing in until the headlights feel like the only light in the world. Rio's hands tighten on the wheel as the car bounces over a rut.

“Please tell me you know where you’re going,” she says.

“Oh, come on, sweetheart. Have I ever steered you wrong?”

Rio catches Agatha’s small smile in the dashboard light and grins. “Do you really want me to answer that?”

The turnoff, when it comes, is barely visible – a gap in the trees that Rio would have driven past without a second glance. She eases the car off the dirt road and into it, branches scraping along both sides, and kills the engine.

The silence afterward is enormous, just the tick of the cooling engine and the sound of both of them unbuckling their seatbelts.

"We can't leave it here," Rio says, glancing around once they’re both outside. The car is sitting in plain view of the dirt road.

Rio reaches for the key, then thinks better of it. Too loud. It takes both of them, Rio pushing from the driver's side door while Agatha steers one-handed, to walk the car back into the brush far enough that the road is no longer visible through the windshield. They cover what they can with broken branches, working fast and wordless. Rio eyes it when they’re done. It won't survive close inspection, but it might survive a drive-by.

"Good enough?” Agatha asks, straightening up, breathing hard. “Great. Let's go."

She slings a bag over her good shoulder – she must have grabbed it from somewhere in the backseat – and then she sets off into the trees without waiting to see if Rio's behind her.

She is. Rio falls into step a pace back and slightly to the side, the way she's been trained to walk when providing close protection. There's something almost unreal about Agatha here – slivers of moonlight filtering down through the canopy in pieces, parts of her coming into light and shadow at once. Agatha picks her way over roots and fallen branches like she's done it a hundred times, sure-footed even with one arm useless at her side, even exhausted and bleeding under a layer of gauze that needs changing. There's something a little feral in the way she moves through the woods unbothered, like she belongs here more than she belongs anywhere with walls. Rio's seen her wear a dozen faces – Agnes the detective, the woman in the gala dress, the girl in hiking boots and a loose braid — and she wonders, not for the first time, if this is the face underneath all of them, or just one more mask.

She follows Agatha, matching her step for step, eyes moving methodically through the trees even though there's nothing tactical left in her to draw on. No backup, no weapon. She’d dropped the knife on her bed before jumping out the window, which had seemed like a good idea at the time; the last thing she’d needed was to land the wrong way on the knife and stab herself. But she misses the feeling of it in her hand, the reassuring weight of it. The certainty that she could use it, with the right motivation.

Then, through the trees, a cabin appears.

It squats in the middle of a clearing, low and square, logs gone grey with age, a rusting tin roof sitting on top. The windows are dark. A porch runs along the front, sagging slightly at one end, two wooden chairs facing out toward the trees, taking in a view that's long since grown over. But the door, Rio can see as they climb the porch steps, has a deadbolt that looks newer than everything else around it.

The place is old. Abandoned, by the look of it. But not unguarded.

"Welcome to my humble safe house,” Agatha says, leaning over the lock. “Try not to judge the décor."

“Wow,” Rio says as the deadbolt gives with a heavy click. “So this is where you’ve been hiding out?”

“Not necessarily,” Agatha says. She shrugs when Rio shoots her a look. “What? I’m keeping the mystery alive. Wouldn’t want you to get bored.”

Rio snorts. “Oh, I don’t think there’s much danger of that.”

Agatha starts to walk into the house, but Rio steps into her path, blocking it.

“Hang on. Let me clear it first.”

Agatha blinks. “It’s my house.”

“It’s dark and I haven’t seen the inside of it. Two minutes.”

“There’s only like, three rooms in there.”

“Then it’ll go fast.”

Agatha studies her for a second, pursing her lips, like she's deciding whether this is worth the fight. Fuck’s sake – this woman can’t relinquish control over anything. Rio just crosses her arms and raises her eyebrows, not backing down.

“Oh, fine,” Agatha says finally, stepping back with exaggerated grace, hand pressed to her chest. “Far be it from me to come between an FBI agent and her protocol.”

“Great. Eyes on the tree line. Shout if anything moves."

“Sir, yes sir.” But there's no real bite in it, and Agatha turns around, scanning the dark yard with more attention than her tone implied.

Rio steps inside. The air is close and stale, thick with the mustiness of a place that's been shut up for a long time. Her eyes adjust slowly to the dark. The main room is small. A wood stove squats in one corner, black with old soot, a cast iron skillet still sitting on top of it like someone walked away mid-meal years ago. A threadbare couch faces it, the cushions sunken, a knitted blanket folded over the back. Everything is covered in a film of dust – the windowsills, the small kitchen table pushed against the far wall, two rickety chairs tucked beneath it. A row of mason jars sits on a shelf, lids rusted shut.

Rio moves through the house fast, the way she was trained to – checking around corners, inside closets, under furniture. A narrow hallway leads to two more rooms: a bedroom with an iron bed frame and a bare, stained mattress, and a bathroom barely large enough to turn around in, claw-foot tub streaked with rust stains. She makes a quick count of doors and windows as she goes, checking that everything is locked, eyeing each window’s sightline, making a mental list of forced-entry points.

“Anything else? Attic? Basement?” she calls out the door as she returns to the main room.

“What you see is what you get, sweets.”

“Power?”

“Nope. Lanterns and candles.”

Rio sweeps the place once more with her eyes. “Okay, then,” she says, temporarily satisfied. “You can come in.”

“Oh – can I?” Agatha asks, wide-eyed and sarcastic.

“Yeah, yeah. Get in here and lock the door behind you.” Rio walks around, tugging the curtains closed. “Okay, so this room isn’t going to provide much cover if he shows up. If we have to fall back, head to the bedroom, not the bathroom. The bathroom window is over the tub so it won’t make a good exit, but the bedroom has two windows, and it’s got a bed frame that could be used to barricade the door. If we have to go out the back… what?”

Agatha is staring at her, biting her lip over a smile. “No, no, keep going.”

“What?” Rio demands again.

“Nothing,” Agatha says, eyes traveling the length of Rio, up and down. “I just forgot how hot you are when you take charge.”

Heat creeps up Rio’s cheeks. “Thirty seconds ago you were annoyed that I was taking charge.”

“That’s because you made me wait outside while you were being hot.”

“Ah.”

Agatha twirls and collapses onto the couch, scrunching her nose at the plume of dust that rises around her. Rio can feel her eyes following her as she starts taking inventory of the small kitchen’s contents: two wooden spoons, a tin fork that looks like it’ll bend if she glares in its general direction. Wonderful.

“No knives,” she announces. “Though hitting someone with this skillet could do some damage.”

“Great. We can watch little cartoon stars float around his head,” Agatha says dryly.

“Okay,” Rio says, the plan starting to come together in her mind. “If he finds this place, here's what happens. He's not getting paid to kill me – he’s after you. So the second we hear anything, you head for the bedroom, you head out the window, and you run. Don't wait for me, don't look back, just go."

Agatha lifts her eyebrows. “And what are you doing while I’m running?”

“I’ll be right behind you. But if I'm not – if something slows me down – you keep going. You don't stop for me."

“And so what, he kills you and then he hunts me down in the woods? I don’t think so, Vidal. I’m not dying out here in the middle of nowhere. I’m dying between silk sheets after the best orgasm of my life at the age of two hundred or something.”

“I’m not sending you out there to die. I’m talking about a head start. That’s all I need to buy you.” Rio glances around the room – the stove, the pan, the mason jars on their shelf, nothing in here built for a fight. "If he comes through that door, I’ll try and put something between you and him for as long as possible. Furniture, noise – anything that gets his eyes off you.”

“Right. You’ll Wile E. Coyote him with a frying pan.”

“If I have to, yeah.”

Agatha stares at her for a moment, then sighs and pulls her bag toward her. “Look, I know this is your area of expertise, and I don’t want you to think I don’t appreciate that,” she says, rummaging through it. “But instead of the plan where I probably end up murdered in the woods, I was thinking – how about we just kill him with this?”

She pulls out a gun.

Rio’s mouth drops. “Where the fuck did that come from?”

“My car. What – you think I’m walking around unarmed? Come on, there’s a hitman after me for god’s sake,” Agatha says with an amused lift of her eyebrow.

“Whose is it?” There’s no way Agatha has a gun license. No way this was purchased under her own name.

“Oh… let’s not ask questions we don’t want to know the answer to,” Agatha says, waving a dismissive hand. She stands up and offers the gun to Rio. “The important thing is, I’m not going to die in the middle of some backwoods no-name holler.”

Rio snatches the gun from her hand. She drops the magazine, checking whether it’s loaded – it is – and racks the slide back just enough to confirm there’s a round in the chamber. She lets it close. “You didn’t want to mention this earlier? Like when I was clearing the house completely unarmed?”

“There was no one in the house.”

“But there could have been! We didn’t know—” Rio cuts herself off, drawing a breath. “You know what? Never mind.”

Agatha pulls a sympathetic pout. “Aw, don’t be mad, baby.” She reaches a finger into Rio’s collar and tugs her closer, brief and easy, and kisses her. The soft press of her mouth tastes like an apology she'd never actually say out loud. “Next time I'll lead with the gun.”

“Mm-hm,” Rio says, but it’s hard to stay annoyed with Agatha when she’s nipping at Rio’s lower lip.

“Mmm. You do look good with a weapon,” Agatha says as Rio leans away and tucks the gun into the back of her waistband. Rio’s shaking her head before she finishes the sentence.

“Uh-uh. No. Stop looking at me like that and go sit down over there.”

Agatha gives her a smile like she knows exactly what Rio’s thinking. “So disciplined, Agent."

“Yeah, well, one of us has to be.”

"Fine. But for the record, I prefer you... undisciplined,” Agatha says with a smirk, but she turns and walks over to the couch, sitting back down obediently. "Just in case you're taking notes."

“Sure. I'll write that down for after we escape the professional assassin who's hunting us like dogs,” Rio tells her, turning back to the curtains, checking the line of trees. Still nothing. She glances back at Agatha, who has drawn her knees up, looking entirely too pleased with herself for someone hiding from a hitman. She waggles her eyebrows lewdly at Rio.

Rio can’t help it – she laughs. She knows she should be afraid. She’s got no badge, no gun, and there’s a hired killer on their trail. There's no real plan or protocol for this. But as she looks into Agatha's eyes, she can’t make herself feel what she knows she’s supposed to feel. If anything, it’s the opposite – something loosening in her chest instead of tightening. A feeling of finally doing the thing she was built for.

Admittedly, though, some of her exhilaration starts to wear off after half an hour or so. The cabin grows colder with each passing minute, night air seeping in through the uninsulated walls. Eventually Agatha sighs, head falling back.

“I"m bored,” she announces. “This is boring. And cold. Can we start a fire or something?”

“No. We’re hiding. We’re not here.”

“But we are here, and I’m freezing.”

“Well, next time pick a safe house with central heat.”

Agatha unfolds herself from the couch and sidles up behind Rio, wrapping her arms around her waist and resting her chin on Rio’s shoulder. “Can we at least take off all our clothes and huddle together for warmth?” she purrs into Rio’s ear.

Rio closes her eyes, biting her lip at the image unfolding behind her eyelids.

“Look, once we’re—”

A branch snaps outside.

Agatha tenses against Rio as adrenaline crashes through Rio’s veins, her vision sharpening, focusing. Finally.

The man’s voice carries through the trees. “Agathaaaa,” he sing-songs, almost playful.

Rio’s already moving, pulling Agatha down behind the couch, laying a hand flat against her low back. Stay. She crouches as she moves toward the wall beside the window, pressing back against it, gun held down along her thigh. She angles her head just enough to catch a sliver of yard through the gap in the curtain.

Nothing. Just trees, edges silver with moonlight.

“I know you’re in there,” the voice comes again. “Found your car half a mile back. Nice try with that cute little hiding spot.” He’s closer now, approaching from the left, maybe. It’s hard to tell with the sound bouncing off the trees. She’s surprised he’s announcing himself, after his silent approach at her house. We ran away from him before, Rio realizes. He’s not afraid now because he thinks we’re unarmed.

Okay. Good. That’s good.

She turns back to the couch to find Agatha peering over the top. Get ready to run, she mouths to her.

Agatha’s response is a tiny, faux-confused shrug – What? – as though they hadn’t gone over the entire fucking plan in detail thirty minutes ago.

Rio doesn’t have time for this shit. She crosses the room in three steps, grabs Agatha by her good arm, and hauls her up and over to the bedroom doorway.

“If he gets in, you jump out that window, and you run,” she whispers. “Do not look back.”

“I thought that’s what the gun was for,” Agatha hisses. “So I wouldn’t have to run.”

“The gun is so I don’t have to run. He’s here for you, Agatha. So you’re getting the fuck out of here.”

She doesn’t wait for an argument. She pulls the door shut between them and turns back to the main room just as something heavy slams into the front door – once, twice – wood groaning and splintering around the hinges.

Rio drops behind the couch just as the door gives way, swinging wide and cracking down the middle.

“Agatha.” His tone is almost gentle, like he’s trying to calm a skittish animal. “Come on. This doesn’t have to be a fight.”

He steps inside, feet creaking against the floorboards.

“I’ll tell you what. You stop playing hide-and-seek, I’ll make it fast and painless.” The gentleness falls away. “But if I have to hunt you down, I am going to make it hurt. Your choice.”

He pauses there, framed by the doorway, like he’s waiting for an answer. He hasn’t seen Rio yet. Another three steps inside, maybe four, and he’ll spot her, but by then he’ll be close enough that there’s almost no chance she’ll miss.

Her heart hammers against her sternum, bruising and so loud she’s sure he must be able to hear it. He takes another step.

“Okay, then.” The man gives a theatrical chuckle. “Guess I should have known you’d pick pain.”

Please have run, Rio thinks desperately in Agatha’s direction. Please be so, so far away from here—

She jumps as the man kicks the bedroom door open and it slams into the wall, cracking as loud as cannon fire. She rises to her feet, dread pooling in her stomach as she sees Agatha’s face over his shoulder, stricken and pale, holding up a hand.

Everything slows down, distilled to breath and singing blood.

The man is six feet from her.

She has a clean line of sight.

She sees before, and she sees after. Who she was, and who she has become. She sees so clearly now that all of it has led to this: there is only one world that Rio wants to live in, and it has Agatha Harkness standing at the center of it. Everything else – the badge, the house, the woman she used to see when she looked in the mirror – exists in the other world, the one without Agatha, and she’s not going back there. Not today. Not for this man, and not for anyone else who thinks they can take Agatha away from her.

Her world stops at Agatha’s edge.

She is exactly where she wants to be.

Rio doesn’t blink as the man lifts his gun. She doesn’t hesitate.

She pulls the trigger, and she shoots him through the heart.
